Allah's Existence
intermediate
10 min
Direction is Not a Necessity of Existence
Nasafi proves direction is not essential to existence using self-example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why existence does not require direction, and how this rational principle is used to affirm God's transcendence beyond spatial categories.

Core Idea
Existence does not entail direction; even your own self and its accidents exist without being in a direction.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi builds on earlier proofs to establish that direction is not an essential property of existence. He uses an intuitive example from our own experience: our self (nafs) and its accidents exist but are not in a direction from us. This argument becomes a powerful tool to negate from God any attributes that would imply temporality, such as place and direction. Let's see how the author unfolds this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its flow, then read the literal English translation. This will help you grasp the overall argument before diving into analysis.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the main claim
Find the sentence that states the core thesis: 'ليس من ضرورة الوجود إثبات الجهة' — direction is not a necessity of existence. Underline it.
3
Follow the self example
The author gives an example from your own self (nafsī) and the accidents (aʿrāḍ) that inhere in it. Notice how he argues that these exist without being in a direction from you.
This is the key intuitive proof.
4
Extend to all six directions
Observe how the author systematically checks each of the six directions (above, below, front, back, right, left) and shows that existence does not require any of them.
The argument generalizes from individual directions to all directions.
5
Connect to divine transcendence
Finally, note how the conclusion is applied to negate that God is an accident, substance, or body. The argument shows that an existent can be free of these categories.
This reinforces the doctrine of tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في هذا كله أن ثبوت الصانع جل وعلا وقدمه علم بما لا مدفع له من الدلائل ولا مجال للريب فيه، فقلنا بثبوته وقدمه، وعرفنا استحالة ثبوت أمارات الحدوث في القديم، فنفينا ذلك عنه لما في إثباتها من إثبات حدوث القديم أو بطلان دلائل الحدوث وذلك باطل كله على ما قررنا وفي إثبات المكان والجهة إثبات دلالة الحدوث على ما مر، وليس من ضرورة الوجود إثبات الجهة، لأن نفسي وما قام بها من الأعراض ليست مني بجهة وهي موجودة، وما كان مني بجهة ليس بقائم بي وهو موجود وكذا ليس من ضرورة الوجود أن يكون فوقي، لوجود ما ليس فوقي ولا أن يكون تحتي، لوجود ما ليس تحتي، وكذا قدامي وخلفي وعن يميني وعن يساري، وإذا ثبت هذا في كل جهة على اليقين ثبت في الجهات كلها، إذ هي متركبة من الأفراد. فإذا ليس من ضرورة الوجود أن يكون مني بجهة لوجود ما ليس مني بجهة، ولا أن يكون بي، لوجود ما ليس بقائم بي. وظهر أن قيام الشيء بي وكونه بجهة مني ليس من لواحق الوجود وضروراته على ما قررنا هذا الكلام في نفي كونه تعالى عرضا أو جوهرا أو جسما، وخروج الموجود عن هذه المعاني كلها معقول لما بينا من الدلائل، أن ليس من ضرورة الموجود ثبوت معنى من هذه المعاني، لما مر من ثبوت موجود ليس فيه كل معنى من هذه المعاني على اليقين. غير أنه ليس بموهوم لما لم يحس موجود يعرى عن هذه المعاني كلها. إذ ما يشاهد من المحسوسات كلها محدثة، وارتفاع دلالة الحدوث عن المحدث محال، وفي الغائب قائما
And the principle in all of this is that the establishment of the Maker, exalted and glorified be He, and His eternity is known by proofs that cannot be repelled and in which there is no room for doubt. So we affirm His existence and eternity, and we know the impossibility of affirming signs of temporality in the Eternal. So we negate that from Him because in affirming them there is affirmation of the temporality of the Eternal or invalidation of the proofs of temporality, and all of that is false as we established. And in affirming place and direction there is affirmation of an indication of temporality, as has passed. And it is not from the necessity of existence to affirm direction, because my self (nafsī) and what subsists in it of accidents are not in a direction from me, yet they exist; and that which is in a direction from me is not subsisting in me, yet it exists. Likewise, it is not from the necessity of existence that it be above me, because there exists what is not above me; nor that it be below me, because there exists what is not below me; likewise before me, behind me, to my right, and to my left. And when this is established with certainty for every direction, it is established for all directions, since they are composed of individuals. So it is not from the necessity of existence that something be in a direction from me, because there exists what is not in a direction from me; nor that it be in me, because there exists what is not subsisting in me. And it became clear that the subsistence of a thing in me and its being in a direction from me are not among the attachments and necessities of existence, as we established. This discourse is in negation of His being, exalted, an accident, or a substance, or a body. And the departure of the existent from all these meanings is intelligible, because of the proofs we have shown, that it is not from the necessity of the existent to affirm any of these meanings, because of what has passed of the establishment of an existent that does not contain any of these meanings with certainty. However, it is not imaginable because no existent is perceived that is devoid of all these meanings. For all that is witnessed of sensible things is temporal, and the removal of the indication of temporality from the temporal is impossible. And in the unseen, it is subsisting.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a culminating argument that direction is not a necessary concomitant of existence. The author begins by reaffirming that the existence and eternity of God are established by undeniable proofs. Since we know that signs of temporal origin (ḥudūth) cannot apply to the Eternal, we negate from God anything that would imply temporality, such as place and direction. The author then argues that existence as such does not require being in a direction. He uses an intuitive example: one's own self (nafsī) and the accidents that inhere in it are not in a direction from oneself, yet they exist. Conversely, objects that are in a direction (e.g., above or below) are not inherent in the self, yet they also exist. Therefore, existence is not linked to directionality. This is examined for all six directions (above, below, front, back, right, left), and since it holds for each, it holds for all. The author concludes that being in a direction or inhering in something are not necessary properties of existence. This argument serves to negate that God is an accident (ʿaraḍ), substance (jawhar), or body (jism). While it is conceivable that an existent can be free of all these categories, we do not perceive such an existent in the sensible world, because all sensible things are temporal. Thus, the argument is not based on direct observation but on rational deduction.

Key Terms
جهة
نفسي
عرض
ضرورة الوجود
حدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since all observable existents are located in a direction, existence necessarily implies being in a direction.
Correction: Nasafi refutes this by pointing to the self and its accidents, which exist without being in a direction from oneself. Therefore, direction is not an essential property of existence.

Checkpoint
What example does the author use to show that existence does not require being in a direction?
A) The existence of bodies in space.
B) The existence of one's self and its accidents.
C) The existence of the heavens.
D) The existence of abstract concepts.

Key Takeaway
Direction is not a necessary concomitant of existence; rational arguments show that an existent can be without direction, which is essential for affirming God's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself imagining God as being 'somewhere'—perhaps above the sky or in a particular direction? How does the argument that even your own self exists without being in a direction challenge that mental picture? What would it mean for your worship to truly believe that God is not confined to any place?
?
The passage uses your own self as evidence that existence does not require direction. When you reflect on your own existence, do you experience yourself as occupying a direction? How might this help you understand God's transcendence in a way that goes beyond mere intellectual acceptance?
?
If you cannot imagine an existent without direction because all sensible things have direction, does that mean such an existent is impossible? The author says it is rational even if not imaginable. Are you willing to let your reason override your imagination in understanding God? What concrete step can you take to train your mind to think of God beyond space and direction?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
6 min
Absence from Imagination Does Not Imply Non-Existence
Al-Nasafi establishes that rational proofs and signs demonstrate the Creator's existence beyond imagination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that rational proofs and effects establish the existence of things beyond imagination, including the Creator.

Core Idea
What is beyond imagination still exists; effects prove the unseen.

Many deny the Creator because they cannot imagine Him. Al-Nasafi argues that this is a flawed approach. He shows that rational proofs of origination (ḥudūth) and the distinction between the rational and the imaginary provide a solid foundation. Furthermore, numerous real entities—like intellect and spirit—are known only through their effects, not through imagination.

Guided Path
1
Read the main principle
Read the opening sentences where Al-Nasafi states that absence from imagination does not equal non-existence. Note the reference to rational proofs of origination.
The term 'ḥudūth' (origination) is central to kalam arguments for God's existence.
2
Identify the examples
Find the list of meanings (maʿānī) that are beyond sensory perception but known through effects: intellect, spirit, sight, hearing, smell, taste.
These are everyday examples that illustrate the point clearly.
3
Understand the analogy
Al-Nasafi uses the analogy of denying whiteness in a seen body because it cannot be heard. Reflect on how absurd that is, and apply the same logic to denying the Creator.
4
Connect to the main argument
Conclude that relying on imagination nullifies rational proof. The passage shows that the Creator's existence is established by signs (āyāt), not by imagination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأمر بخلافه، وليس من ضرورة الارتفاع عن الوهم العدم، لما ثبت من الدلائل العقلية على الحدوث وظهر التفرقة بين المعقول والموهوم على ما تقدم ذكره على وجه لا يبقى للمنصف فيه ريبة ثم إن الله تعالى أثبت في نفس كل عاقل معاني خارجة عن الوهم لخروجها عن درك الحواس، ويعلم وجودها على وجه لم يكن للشك فيه مدخل لثبوت آثارها كالعقل والروح، والبصر والسمع والشم والذوق، فإن ثبوت هذه المعاني متحقق، والأفهام عن الإحاطة بما بينها قاصرة لخروجها عن الحواس المؤدية المدركة صور محسوساتها إلى الفكرة، ليصير ذلك حجة على كل من أنكر الصانع مع ظهور الآيات الدلالة عليه لخروجه عن التصور في الوهم، ويعلم أن لا مدخل للوهم في معرفة ثبوت الأشياء الغائبة عن الحواس، ومن أراد الوصول إلى ذلك بالوهم ونفي ما لم يتصور فيه مع ظهور آيات ثبوته، فقد عطل الدليل القائم، لانعدام ما ليس يصلح دليلا، فيصير كمن أنكر وجود البياض في جسم معاينته ذلك، لانعدام استدراك ذلك بالسمع، وجهالة من هذا فعله لا يخفي على الناس فكذا هذا. ثم لا فرق بين من أنكر الشيء لخروجه عن الوهم، وبين من جعل خروج الشيء عن الوهم دليلا للعدم لما فيهما جميعا قصر ثبوت الشيء ووجوده على الوهم، وخروج الموجود عن جميع أمارات الحدوث غير موهوم لما لم يعاين موجودا ليس بمحدث، وإثبات أمارات الحدوث فى القديم محال، وبنفيها عن القديم إخراجه عن الوهم وبخروجه عن الوهم يلتحق بالعدم فإذا لا وجود للقديم. فصارت المجسمة والقائلون بالجهة الجاعلون ما لا يجوز عليه الجهة في حيز العدم قائلين بعدم القديم. فضاهوا الدهرية في نفي الصانع، الذي ليس فيه شيء من أمارات الحدوث وساعدوهم بإثبات قدم من هو متمكن في المكان أو متحيز إلى جهة في إثبات قدم من تحققت أمارات حدوثه، وبإثبات القدم للعالم نفي الصانع، فإذا عند الوقوف على هذه الحقائق علم أنهم هم النافون للصانع في الحقيقة دون من أثبته ونفي عنه الجهة والتمكن اللذين هما من أمارات الحدوث. والله الموفق.
The matter is otherwise, and it is not necessary that absence from imagination is non-existence, because of what has been established by rational proofs of origination (al-ḥudūth) and the distinction between the rationally conceivable (al-maʿqūl) and the imaginary (al-mawhūm) has appeared as previously mentioned in a manner that leaves no doubt for the fair-minded. Then God Almighty established in the soul of every rational being meanings (maʿānī) external to imagination due to their being beyond the reach of the senses, and their existence is known in a way that has no entry for doubt due to the establishment of their effects, such as intellect (al-ʿaql) and spirit (al-rūḥ), and sight, hearing, smell, and taste. For the existence of these meanings is certain, and the minds are incapable of encompassing what is between them because they are beyond the senses that convey and perceive the forms of their sensed objects to thought, so that this becomes a proof against everyone who denies the Creator despite the appearance of signs indicating Him, because He is beyond conception in imagination. And it is known that imagination has no entry in knowing the existence of things absent from the senses. And whoever seeks to attain that through imagination and denies what is not conceived in it despite the appearance of signs of its existence has nullified the standing proof, due to the absence of what is not fit to be a proof. So he becomes like one who denies the existence of whiteness in a body that he sees, due to the absence of perceiving that through hearing—and the ignorance of one who does this is not hidden from people. So likewise this. Then there is no difference between one who denies a thing because it is outside imagination and one who makes a thing's being outside imagination a proof of non-existence, because in both cases they restrict the existence of a thing to imagination. And the existence of the existent is free from all signs of origination (amārāt al-ḥudūth), which is not imaginary because no existent that is not originated has been witnessed. And to establish signs of origination in the Eternal (al-qadīm) is impossible, and to negate them from the Eternal removes Him from imagination, and by His removal from imagination He joins non-existence, so then there is no existence for the Eternal. So the anthropomorphists (al-mujassima) and those who affirm direction (al-jiha), who place what does not allow of direction in a locus, become deniers of the Eternal, saying non-existence of the Eternal. So they resemble the materialists (al-dahriyya) in denying the Creator, who has no sign of origination, and they assist them by affirming the eternity of one who is located in place or situated in a direction, in affirming the eternity of one whose signs of origination are realized, and by affirming the eternity of the world they deny the Creator. So when one stops at these truths, it is known that they are the deniers of the Creator in reality, not the one who affirms Him and negates from Him direction and location which are both among the signs of origination. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who deny the existence of the Creator because He cannot be imagined. The author first establishes that not being subject to imagination does not entail non-existence, since rational proofs have established the distinction between the intelligible and the imaginary. Then he provides examples of things known through their effects but not perceived by the senses, such as intellect and spirit. He argues that if someone were to deny whiteness in a seen body because it cannot be heard, that would be absurd; similarly, denying the Creator because He is not imagined is absurd. Next, he criticizes the anthropomorphists (mujassima) and those who affirm direction for God, saying that by imposing spatial attributes on the Eternal, they in effect deny His eternity. They have restricted existence to what is imagined, and since the Eternal is free from signs of origination, He cannot be imagined; thus they end up denying Him. The author concludes that such people are the true deniers of the Creator, unlike those who affirm God and negate direction and location from Him.

Key Terms
الوهم (al-wahm)
المعقول (al-maʿqūl)
الموهوم (al-mawhūm)
الحدوث (al-ḥudūth)
العقل (al-ʿaql)
الروح (al-rūḥ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If something cannot be imagined, it does not exist.
Correction: Many real entities (e.g., intellect, spirit) are known through effects, not imagination. Absence from imagination does not imply non-existence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the logical consequence of restricting existence to what is imagined?
A) It leads to denying the Eternal because He is free from signs of origination and thus unimagined.
B) It leads to affirming the Creator because He is perfectly imagined.
C) It makes no difference to theological arguments.
D) It only affects the materialists.

Key Takeaway
Imagination is not a reliable criterion for existence; rational proof and effects establish the reality of the unseen, including the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your mind cannot picture Allah, but this lesson proves that many real things—like your own intellect—are beyond imagination. When you feel doubt about Allah's existence because you can't see or imagine Him, are you trusting your limited imagination more than the clear rational signs? Will you now make a conscious effort to affirm Allah through reason and creation, even when your imagination falls silent?
?
You know your own spirit exists, even though you can't imagine it. Why then do you hesitate to believe in the Creator whose signs are everywhere? Is it because you've secretly required Allah to fit inside your imagination—a box you've built for Him? Will you repent from this hidden arrogance and accept that the Creator of imagination cannot be contained by it?
?
This passage compares denying the Creator to denying whiteness in a seen object because it can't be heard. When you struggle with faith, do you similarly reject a clear proof because it doesn't come through your preferred sense? Will you today choose to submit to the rational certainty of Allah's existence, even if your heart feels distant, and ask Him to increase your conviction?

Allah's Existence
intermediate

The Outcome of Limiting Existence to Imagination: Refuting Anthropomorphism
Al-Nasafi demonstrates the consequences of restricting existence to imagination and critiques those who affirm direction or location for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how restricting existence to imagination leads to denying the Eternal, and why anthropomorphists are actually deniers of the Creator.

Core Idea
To deny direction and location is to truly affirm God, not to deny Him.

Al-Nasafi continues his critique by examining the logical consequences of limiting existence to imagination. He argues that this leads to denying the Eternal. He then turns to the anthropomorphists (mujassima) and those who affirm direction for God, showing that by imposing spatial attributes, they inadvertently deny His true eternity and align with materialists.

Guided Path
1
Read the logical argument
Read the part where Al-Nasafi shows that denying a thing due to unimaginability and using unimaginability as proof of non-existence are equivalent. Both restrict existence to imagination.
This is a key point linking the two positions.
2
Understand the implication for the Eternal
The Eternal (al-qadīm) has no signs of origination. Since we have never witnessed a non-originated being, the Eternal is unimaginable. If existence is limited to imagination, then the Eternal must be non-existent.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Analyze the critique of anthropomorphists
Al-Nasafi states that anthropomorphists and those who affirm direction (jiha) place God in a locus or direction, which are signs of origination. Thus they affirm something that has signs of origination as eternal, which is contradictory.
They inadvertently affirm the eternity of the world (a materialist position).
4
Draw the conclusion
The passage ends by stating that the true deniers of the Creator are those who impose spatial attributes, not those who negate them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأمر بخلافه، وليس من ضرورة الارتفاع عن الوهم العدم، لما ثبت من الدلائل العقلية على الحدوث وظهر التفرقة بين المعقول والموهوم على ما تقدم ذكره على وجه لا يبقى للمنصف فيه ريبة ثم إن الله تعالى أثبت في نفس كل عاقل معاني خارجة عن الوهم لخروجها عن درك الحواس، ويعلم وجودها على وجه لم يكن للشك فيه مدخل لثبوت آثارها كالعقل والروح، والبصر والسمع والشم والذوق، فإن ثبوت هذه المعاني متحقق، والأفهام عن الإحاطة بما بينها قاصرة لخروجها عن الحواس المؤدية المدركة صور محسوساتها إلى الفكرة، ليصير ذلك حجة على كل من أنكر الصانع مع ظهور الآيات الدلالة عليه لخروجه عن التصور في الوهم، ويعلم أن لا مدخل للوهم في معرفة ثبوت الأشياء الغائبة عن الحواس، ومن أراد الوصول إلى ذلك بالوهم ونفي ما لم يتصور فيه مع ظهور آيات ثبوته، فقد عطل الدليل القائم، لانعدام ما ليس يصلح دليلا، فيصير كمن أنكر وجود البياض في جسم معاينته ذلك، لانعدام استدراك ذلك بالسمع، وجهالة من هذا فعله لا يخفي على الناس فكذا هذا. ثم لا فرق بين من أنكر الشيء لخروجه عن الوهم، وبين من جعل خروج الشيء عن الوهم دليلا للعدم لما فيهما جميعا قصر ثبوت الشيء ووجوده على الوهم، وخروج الموجود عن جميع أمارات الحدوث غير موهوم لما لم يعاين موجودا ليس بمحدث، وإثبات أمارات الحدوث فى القديم محال، وبنفيها عن القديم إخراجه عن الوهم وبخروجه عن الوهم يلتحق بالعدم فإذا لا وجود للقديم. فصارت المجسمة والقائلون بالجهة الجاعلون ما لا يجوز عليه الجهة في حيز العدم قائلين بعدم القديم. فضاهوا الدهرية في نفي الصانع، الذي ليس فيه شيء من أمارات الحدوث وساعدوهم بإثبات قدم من هو متمكن في المكان أو متحيز إلى جهة في إثبات قدم من تحققت أمارات حدوثه، وبإثبات القدم للعالم نفي الصانع، فإذا عند الوقوف على هذه الحقائق علم أنهم هم النافون للصانع في الحقيقة دون من أثبته ونفي عنه الجهة والتمكن اللذين هما من أمارات الحدوث. والله الموفق.
The matter is otherwise, and it is not necessary that absence from imagination is non-existence, because of what has been established by rational proofs of origination (al-ḥudūth) and the distinction between the rationally conceivable (al-maʿqūl) and the imaginary (al-mawhūm) has appeared as previously mentioned in a manner that leaves no doubt for the fair-minded. Then God Almighty established in the soul of every rational being meanings (maʿānī) external to imagination due to their being beyond the reach of the senses, and their existence is known in a way that has no entry for doubt due to the establishment of their effects, such as intellect (al-ʿaql) and spirit (al-rūḥ), and sight, hearing, smell, and taste. For the existence of these meanings is certain, and the minds are incapable of encompassing what is between them because they are beyond the senses that convey and perceive the forms of their sensed objects to thought, so that this becomes a proof against everyone who denies the Creator despite the appearance of signs indicating Him, because He is beyond conception in imagination. And it is known that imagination has no entry in knowing the existence of things absent from the senses. And whoever seeks to attain that through imagination and denies what is not conceived in it despite the appearance of signs of its existence has nullified the standing proof, due to the absence of what is not fit to be a proof. So he becomes like one who denies the existence of whiteness in a body that he sees, due to the absence of perceiving that through hearing—and the ignorance of one who does this is not hidden from people. So likewise this. Then there is no difference between one who denies a thing because it is outside imagination and one who makes a thing's being outside imagination a proof of non-existence, because in both cases they restrict the existence of a thing to imagination. And the existence of the existent is free from all signs of origination (amārāt al-ḥudūth), which is not imaginary because no existent that is not originated has been witnessed. And to establish signs of origination in the Eternal (al-qadīm) is impossible, and to negate them from the Eternal removes Him from imagination, and by His removal from imagination He joins non-existence, so then there is no existence for the Eternal. So the anthropomorphists (al-mujassima) and those who affirm direction (al-jiha), who place what does not allow of direction in a locus, become deniers of the Eternal, saying non-existence of the Eternal. So they resemble the materialists (al-dahriyya) in denying the Creator, who has no sign of origination, and they assist them by affirming the eternity of one who is located in place or situated in a direction, in affirming the eternity of one whose signs of origination are realized, and by affirming the eternity of the world they deny the Creator. So when one stops at these truths, it is known that they are the deniers of the Creator in reality, not the one who affirms Him and negates from Him direction and location which are both among the signs of origination. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who deny the existence of the Creator because He cannot be imagined. The author first establishes that not being subject to imagination does not entail non-existence, since rational proofs have established the distinction between the intelligible and the imaginary. Then he provides examples of things known through their effects but not perceived by the senses, such as intellect and spirit. He argues that if someone were to deny whiteness in a seen body because it cannot be heard, that would be absurd; similarly, denying the Creator because He is not imagined is absurd. Next, he criticizes the anthropomorphists (mujassima) and those who affirm direction for God, saying that by imposing spatial attributes on the Eternal, they in effect deny His eternity. They have restricted existence to what is imagined, and since the Eternal is free from signs of origination, He cannot be imagined; thus they end up denying Him. The author concludes that such people are the true deniers of the Creator, unlike those who affirm God and negate direction and location from Him.

Key Terms
الوهم (al-wahm)
القديم (al-qadīm)
الحدوث (al-ḥudūth)
المجسمة (al-mujassima)
الجهة (al-jiha)
الدهرية (al-dahriyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming direction or location for God is necessary to affirm His existence.
Correction: Affirming such attributes actually imposes signs of origination on God, which leads to denying His true eternity. True affirmation negates these attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the anthropomorphists and those who affirm direction become deniers of the Creator?
A) Because they deny rational proofs altogether.
B) Because they impose signs of origination on the Eternal, thus affirming eternity for something that has originated attributes.
C) Because they do not believe in God.
D) Because they rely on imagination instead of senses.

Key Takeaway
Imposing spatial attributes on God leads to denying His true eternity; affirming God's transcendence is essential for true belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray or think about God, do you catch yourself forming a mental image, even vaguely, of where He is or what He 'looks' like? What can you do today to consciously purify your worship of all spatial and human-like limitations?
?
The passage equates those who affirm direction for God with those who deny His existence. Could your insistence on a particular description of God—even one you think is reverent—actually be hiding an unwillingness to accept His absolute transcendence? What one change will you make in how you speak about Him?
?
If God is truly beyond every human category and imagination, then what does that demand from you when you face trials or doubts? Are you willing to trust a God you cannot fully comprehend, or do you still secretly wish for a God that fits your understanding? Commit to one specific act of trust that acknowledges His incomprehensible greatness.

God Must Be Eternally Knowing and Powerful
Proof that God must be eternally knowing and powerful.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must be eternally knowing and powerful, and why the opposite would lead to impossibility and doubt.

Core Idea
God cannot lack knowledge or power at any time—it would imply createdness.

This passage presents three compelling arguments that God must possess knowledge and power eternally. If He were not, He would be ignorant and powerless—attributes of created beings—leading to impossibility. Let's examine these proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the three distinct arguments.
2
First argument: absence implies opposite
Understand that if God lacked knowledge and power in pre-eternity, He would have the opposites (ignorance and powerlessness), which are signs of being created. This would make the Eternal created—contradictory.
This is a direct reductio ad absurdum.
3
Second argument: self-defeating scenario
Reflect on the question: If God were not knowing by essence or attribute, how would He know to create knowledge and power for Himself? This is incoherent.
4
Third argument: slippery slope to uncertainty
Consider the implication: if it were possible for God to lack knowledge and power and acquire them as created, then they could be annihilated, leaving God again without them. This would make resurrection and judgment merely possible, not certain, leading to doubt.
The author warns this leads to disbelief.
5
Review the conclusion
The author concludes that such a view is clearly kufr. Reflect on why this matters for Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأنه تعالى لو كان لم يكن في الأزل عالما قادرا، لكان جاهلا وعاجزا، لأن ارتفاع العلم والقدرة عمن يحتمل الاتصاف بهما، لن يكون إلا عن ثبوت ضدهما، وثبوت الجهل والعجز من أمارات المحدث. فإذا كان القديم في الأزل حادثا وهو محال . ولأنه تعالى ولو لم يكن في الأزل عالما بنفسه، ولا بالعلم والقدرة. فكيف علم أنه ينبغي له أن يخلق لنفسه علما وقدرة. ولأنه لو كان جاز خلوه عن العلم والقدرة وهما مخلوقان، جاز إفناؤهما فيبقى على ما كان غير عالم ولا قادر، وإذا دخل هذا في حد الجواز دخل البعث بعد الموت، والثواب والعقاب في حد الجواز. ولم يبق شيء من ذلك متيقن الوجود، بل صار ذلك كله مشكوكا فيه، ولا يخفي كفر من هذا قوله والله الموفق.
And because if the Exalted were not in pre-eternity knowing and powerful, He would be ignorant and powerless, because the removal of knowledge and power from one who is capable of being described by them can only be due to the establishment of their opposites, and the establishment of ignorance and powerlessness are signs of the created. So if the Eternal was in pre-eternity created, that is impossible. And because if the Exalted was not in pre-eternity knowing by His essence, nor by knowledge and power, how would He know that it is fitting for Him to create for Himself knowledge and power? And because if it were permissible for Him to be devoid of knowledge and power, both being created, it would be permissible for them to be annihilated, so He would remain as He was, not knowing nor powerful. And if this enters the realm of possibility, then resurrection after death, reward and punishment would enter the realm of possibility. And nothing of that would remain certain of existence; rather all of that would become doubtful. And the disbelief of one who says this is not hidden. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage gives three arguments for why God must be eternally knowing and powerful. First, if He were not, He would have the opposites (ignorance and powerlessness), which are signs of createdness. Thus the Eternal would be created—a contradiction. Second, if God were not knowing by His essence or by attributes, how would He know to create knowledge and power for Himself? This is a self-defeating scenario. Third, if it were possible for God to lack knowledge and power and then acquire them as created things, it would also be possible for them to be annihilated, leaving God once again without them. This would make all beliefs in resurrection and judgment merely possible, not certain, leading to doubt and disbelief. The author concludes that such a view is clearly kufr.

Key Terms
الأزل
الجهل
العجز
أمارات المحدث
البعث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God could be ignorant temporarily and then acquire knowledge through a created attribute.
Correction: This is impossible because ignorance is a sign of createdness, and the Eternal cannot be created. Also, if He could lack knowledge, He would not know to create it, and if He acquired it as created, it could be annihilated, leading to uncertainty in all religious truths.

Checkpoint
What is the third argument against God lacking knowledge and power?
A) It would imply God is ignorant.
B) It would make resurrection and judgment uncertain.
C) It would contradict His eternality.
D) It would mean He cannot create.

Key Takeaway
God must be eternally knowing and powerful; otherwise, absurdities arise that undermine all religious certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that God could have been ignorant or powerless at any point, how would that affect your trust in His promises about the afterlife? Are you currently living with complete certainty in resurrection, reward, and punishment, or do you act as if they are merely possible?
?
The passage argues that if God could acquire knowledge through a created attribute, He would have needed prior knowledge to know to create that attribute. Do you ever act as if you can acquire spiritual knowledge or closeness to God without first relying on His guidance? Where are you trying to 'create' something for yourself that only God can give?
?
Consider the claim that ignorance and powerlessness are signs of createdness. In what areas of your life do you still cling to ignorance or weakness, acting as if they are acceptable for a servant of the All-Knowing, All-Powerful? What would it mean for you to truly reflect His attributes in your character?

Three Proofs of God's Eternal Knowledge and Power
Nasafi presents three arguments that God must be knowing and powerful from eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational proofs that God must have been knowing and powerful from pre-eternity.

Core Idea
God's attributes of knowledge and power are eternal, not acquired.

Nasafi presents three arguments to establish that God's knowledge and power are intrinsic to His essence from pre-eternity. These proofs counter the idea that God could have acquired these attributes later, which would imply imperfection. The passage grounds the necessity of divine eternal attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the overall flow.
Notice that the passage contains three distinct arguments.
2
Identify the three arguments
Find the beginning of each argument. The first starts with 'ولأنه', the second with 'ولأنه' again, and the third with 'ولأنه'? Actually the passage has three 'ولأنه' clauses. Identify the logical structure of each.
They are marked by the repetition of the conjunction.
3
Analyze the first argument
Understand the conditional logic: if not eternally knowing/powerful → ignorant/powerless → signs of createdness → the Eternal would be created, which is impossible.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Analyze the second argument
Consider the epistemological point: without pre-eternal knowledge, God would not know to create knowledge and power for Himself.
This highlights the necessity of self-sufficiency.
5
Reflect on the third argument's consequences
If God could be devoid of knowledge/power, then resurrection and judgment become merely possible, undermining certainty of faith.
The author warns that this leads to disbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الله تعالى –- ولأنه تعالى لو كان لم يكن في الأزل عالما قادرا، لكان جاهلا وعاجزا، لأن ارتفاع العلم والقدرة عمن يحتمل الاتصاف بهما، لن يكون إلا عن ثبوت ضدهما، وثبوت الجهل والعجز من أمارات المحدث. فإذا كان القديم في الأزل حادثا وهو محال . ولأنه تعالى ولو لم يكن في الأزل عالما بنفسه، ولا بالعلم والقدرة. فكيف علم أنه ينبغي له أن يخلق لنفسه علما وقدرة. ولأنه لو كان جاز خلوه عن العلم والقدرة وهما مخلوقان، جاز إفناؤهما فيبقى على ما كان غير عالم ولا قادر، وإذا دخل هذا في حد الجواز دخل البعث بعد الموت، والثواب والعقاب في حد الجواز. ولم يبق شيء من ذلك متيقن الوجود، بل صار ذلك كله مشكوكا فيه، ولا يخفي كفر من هذا قوله والله الموفق.
God Almighty – and because if He had not been in pre-eternity knowing and powerful, He would be ignorant and powerless, because the removal of knowledge and power from one who is capable of being described by them can only be due to the establishment of their opposites, and the establishment of ignorance and powerlessness are signs of originatedness. So if the Eternal in pre-eternity were originated, that is impossible. And because even if He were not in pre-eternity knowing by His essence, nor by knowledge and power, how would He know that it is befitting for Him to create for Himself knowledge and power? And because if it were permissible for Him to be empty of knowledge and power while they are created, then their annihilation would be permissible, and He would remain as He was: not knowing and not powerful. And if this enters into the realm of possibility, then resurrection after death and reward and punishment enter into the realm of possibility. Nothing of that would remain certain of existence; rather, all of that would become doubtful. And the disbelief of one who says this is not hidden. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents three independent arguments proving that God must have been knowing and powerful from pre-eternity (al-azal) and cannot have acquired these attributes later. The first argument follows a conditional: if God were not knowing and powerful in pre-eternity, He would have been ignorant and powerless. But ignorance and powerlessness are characteristics of originated beings (al-muhdath), so the Eternal would be originated—an impossibility. The second argument asks: if God had no knowledge or power in pre-eternity, how would He even know that He should create them for Himself? The third argument draws out a dangerous consequence: if it were possible for God to be devoid of knowledge and power before they were created, then it would be possible for them to be annihilated later; this opens the door to doubting resurrection and judgment, since they too would be merely possible. The author concludes that such a view amounts to disbelief.

Key Terms
الأزل (al-azal)
العلم (al-ʿilm)
القدرة (al-qudra)
الجهل (al-jahl)
العجز (al-ʿajz)
المحدث (al-muhdath)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's knowledge and power were acquired after creation.
Correction: The arguments show that God must have been knowing and powerful from pre-eternity, otherwise He would be imperfect and doubt would be cast on religious truths.

Checkpoint
What does the first argument conclude if God were not eternally knowing and powerful?
A) He would be like a human
B) He would be ignorant and powerless, which are signs of originatedness
C) He would still be knowing by essence
D) He would create knowledge later

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge and power are eternal attributes, and denying their eternality leads to rational absurdities and undermines religious certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God knows every thought you have ever had and will ever have? How does that truth change the way you live today—what secret thought are you harboring that you need to repent of now?
?
If God's power is eternal and unlimited, why do you still act as if your problems are too big for Him? What one area of your life are you failing to trust His power over, and what will you do today to surrender it?
?
The passage warns that denying God's eternal attributes leads to doubt about resurrection and judgment. Do you live with certainty about the afterlife, or do your worries and choices reveal hidden doubts? What step can you take to strengthen that certainty today?

Proof from Creation: Design and Knowledge
Al-Maturidi's argument from creation for God's knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Maturidi's argument that the purposeful creation of substances and their needs proves God's comprehensive knowledge.

Core Idea
Creation's design reveals the Creator's knowledge of every thing's need.

Imam al-Maturidi presents a powerful argument from the order and purpose inherent in creation. He points to how every substance is created with its specific need and means of continuity, which can only be explained if the Creator knows the modality of each thing. This passage sets the stage for understanding how the natural world points to divine omniscience.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the specific items mentioned: substances that are not tested, things intended for continuity, and their means of continuity.
The argument is dense; focus on the logical flow from creation to knowledge.
2
Identify the premises
Break down the argument into its premises: (1) God created all substances with specific purposes, (2) He created everything that is meant to last along with what sustains it. What does this imply about His knowledge?
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that God knows the modality of everything, its need, and what sustains it. This is a direct proof of divine omniscience.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this argument is important: it uses the observable order of creation to infer a necessary attribute of God, countered to those who claim God does not know particulars.
This is a common argument in kalam, known as the argument from design.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله تعالى فقال: إنه تعالى إذ خلق كل الجواهر التي لا تمتحن في مصالح الممتحنين، وخلق كل شيء أريد به البقاء مع خلق ما به بقاؤه علم أنه كان ممن يعلم كيفية كل شيء وحاجته، وما به القوام والمعاش ولا قوة إلا بالله. ويقال لهؤلاء: إن الله تعالى هل أخبر عما يكون في المستقبل؟ فإن قالوا: لا. فقد أنكروا ما أخبر الله تعالى الأنبياء المتقدمين عليهم السلام من أنباء نبينا محمد عليه السلام، وبشارة عيسى عليه السلام به على ما نطق به الكتاب بقوله
And Shaykh Abu Mansur – may God have mercy on him – argued and said: When He created all the substances that are not tested in the interests of the tested, and created everything by which continuity is intended along with creating what maintains its continuity, it is known that He was one who knows the modality of everything and its need, and what constitutes subsistence and livelihood, and there is no power except through God. And it is said to them: Did God inform about what will happen in the future? If they say: No, then they have denied what God informed the previous prophets, peace be upon them, about the news of our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, and the glad tidings of Jesus, peace be upon him, of him, as the Book states with His saying
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage contains two additional proofs. First, Imam al-Maturidi argues that the creation of all substances and things, each with its specific need and means of continuity, indicates that the Creator knows the modality and requirements of every thing before its creation. This is a direct argument from the order and purposefulness of creation. Second, the author poses a question to the objectors: Did God inform the previous prophets about future events such as the coming of Muhammad? If they deny that God knew these future events, they deny the prophecies in the scriptures. Since the Qur'an and previous books contain such news, it proves that God knows future events (which are currently non-existent). The objection is left incomplete, but the argument is clear.

Key Terms
الجواهر
الممتحنين
كيفية كل شيء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Maturidi's argument is a generic 'design argument' without specifics.
Correction: His argument is specific: it points to the creation of substances and their coordinated needs, not just any order.

Checkpoint
What does al-Maturidi use as evidence for God's knowledge of all things before their existence?
A) The prophecies of previous prophets.
B) The creation of all substances with their specific needs.
C) The use of the word 'perhaps' in the Quran.
D) The consensus of theologians.

Key Takeaway
The order and purposefulness of creation necessitate that the Creator knows the modality and needs of every created thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof says God knows the 'kayfiyya' (modality) of everything. Think of a current struggle in your life where you are obsessing over the 'how'—how it will work out, how you will manage. Does your anxiety reveal a lack of trust in God's detailed knowledge? What would it look like to surrender the 'how' to Him today, even for just one hour?
?
God created everything meant to persist along with what sustains it. He knows your exact needs for survival and flourishing—physical, emotional, spiritual. Are you living as if that is true? Where are you trying to sustain yourself apart from His provision? Will you repent of self-reliance and ask Him for one specific need you have been ignoring?
?
If God's knowledge extends to the 'haja' (need) of every created thing, then He knows your deepest, unspoken needs. When was the last time you poured out your heart to Him with absolute honesty, believing He already knows and cares? What is stopping you from doing that right now?

Challenge from Prophecy: Future Knowledge
Al-Maturidi's challenge using future prophecies to prove divine knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Maturidi's challenge to opponents: if they deny God's knowledge of future events, they must reject biblical prophecies about Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
Prophecy proves God knows the future, including the non-existent.

Following his argument from creation, al-Maturidi poses a direct question to those who deny that God knows future events before they occur. He points to the prophecies of previous prophets, especially the glad tidings of Jesus about Muhammad, which are recorded in the scriptures. This challenge uses the authority of revelation to argue for divine omniscience.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that it begins with a question: 'Did God inform about what will happen in the future?'
The passage is incomplete; it cuts off at 'saying' but the argument is clear.
2
Understand the challenge
Al-Maturidi poses a dilemma: if opponents say God does not inform about the future, then they deny the prophecies about Muhammad in the Torah and Gospel. If they affirm those prophecies, then God must know future events.
3
Examine the evidence
The specific evidence is the glad tidings of Jesus about Muhammad, as stated in the Qur'an. This shows that God informed previous prophets about a future event.
The argument relies on the authenticity of these prophecies.
4
Reflect on the theological point
The argument establishes that God's knowledge includes future contingent events, which are non-existent at the time of the prophecy. This counters those who limit God's knowledge to existents only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And Shaykh Abu Mansur – may God have mercy on him – argued and said: When He created all the substances that are not tested in the interests of the tested, and created everything by which continuity is intended along with creating what maintains its continuity, it is known that He was one who knows the modality of everything and its need, and what constitutes subsistence and livelihood, and there is no power except through God. And it is said to them: Did God inform about what will happen in the future? If they say: No, then they have denied what God informed the previous prophets, peace be upon them, about the news of our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, and the glad tidings of Jesus, peace be upon him, of him, as the Book states with His saying

This passage contains two additional proofs. This is a direct argument from the order and purposefulness of creation. ?

?
If God knows your entire future, including your sins and your repentance, does that make you more cautious or more careless about your actions? How can you use the knowledge that God sees your future to strengthen your reliance on Him and your sincerity in worship?

Refuting the Mu'tazili Argument: Existence and Origination
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazili argument by distinguishing origination from existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazili argument that every existent in the physical world is temporally originated, by distinguishing between the first state of existence and the state of persistence.

Core Idea
Origination applies only at the moment of beginning, not during persistence.

The Mu'tazila argued that every existent in the physical world is temporally originated (muhdath), and since the unseen (gha'ib) is also existent, it too must be originated. Nasafi exposes this as a sophistry by showing that the term 'originated' applies only to the first moment of existence, not to the state of persistence. Let's examine his precise reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazili argument
Read the first part of the passage where Nasafi presents the objection: every existent in the physical world is originated, and every originated is existent, yet the unseen is existent but not originated. Note the logical tension.
Nasafi also points out that Corporealists could use the same argument against the Mu'tazila.
2
Identify Nasafi's first refutation
Nasafi says being originated does not co-rotate with being existent. The label 'originated' truly attaches only at the first state of existence (the moment of coming into being), not in the state of persistence (baqa'). In persistence, the thing is existent but not originated.
Originating an already existing thing is impossible.
3
Identify Nasafi's second refutation
Nasafi adds that a thing is not called originated because it is existent, but because it has a beginning of existence. So attribution of 'originated' can be to something other than existence—specifically, to the beginning itself.
In the case of God, both respects are opposite: He has no beginning and no origination.
4
Reflect on the overall refutation
Consider how Nasafi's two points dismantle the Mu'tazili analogy between physical and unseen. The Mu'tazila assumed that existence entails origination, but Nasafi shows the concepts are distinct.
This lesson strengthens the Maturidi position that God's existence is eternal and unoriginated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن أسئلتهم أنهم يقولون كل موجود في الشاهد محدث، وكل محدث موجود، ومع ذلك الغائب موجود وليس بمحدث وعين هذا الكلام يتوجه عليهم للمجسمة فما انفصلوا به في تلك المسألة فهو انفصالنا في هذه المسألة. ثم نقول لهم: هذه مغالطة فإن كونه محدثاً لا يدور مع كونه موجودا، فإن المحدث حقيقة ما يتعلق به الإحداث وهو يتعلق به في أول حالة الوجود لا في حالة البقاء، لاستحالة إحداث الموجود، فإذا هو في حالة البقاء موجود وليس بمحدث إلا موجود باعتبار إبقاء اسم ما كان لا على الحقيقة والثاني أنه ما كان محدثا لأنه موجود بل لوجود الابتداء لوجوده فلم يستحل إضافة كونه محدثا إلى غير الوجود، وفيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه في الوجهين جميعا.
Among their questions is that they say: Every existent in the physical world is originated, and every originated is existent, yet the unseen is existent and not originated. The same statement applies against them from the Corporealists. So what they answer with in that issue is our answer in this issue. Then we say to them: This is a sophistry, for being originated does not co-rotate with being existent. For the originated is truly that to which origination attaches, and it attaches to it in the first state of existence, not in the state of persistence, because originating an existent is impossible. So in the state of persistence it is existent and not originated, except existent by virtue of preserving the name of what was, not in reality. And the second is that it was not originated because it is existent, but rather because of the existence of beginning of its existence. So it is not impossible to attribute being originated to something other than existence. In our case, the matter is contrary in both respects.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes a Mu'tazili objection. The Mu'tazili argument is: Every existent in the physical world (al-shahid) is originated (muhdath), and every originated is existent. The unseen (al-gha'ib) is existent but not originated. Therefore, there is a problem. But the same argument can be used by the Corporealists against the Mu'tazila. Nasafi then refutes: The statement is a sophistry (mugalata) because being originated does not necessarily co-rotate with being existent. 'Originated' truly means that which origination (ihdath) attaches to. Origination attaches only in the first state of existence (the moment of coming into being), not in the state of persistence (baqa'), because it is impossible to originate something that already exists. So in the state of persistence, a thing is existent but not originated, except in name (preserving the term 'created' as a label). The second point: a thing is not called originated because it is existent, but because it has a beginning of existence. Therefore, attributing originated to something is not conditioned on existence in the sense that it must be always originated while existent. In the case of God, the matter is opposite: He is not originated at all. So the Mu'tazili objection fails.

Key Terms
محدث (muhdath)
إحداث (ihdath)
وجود (wujud)
بقاء (baqa')
مغالطة (mugalata)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'originated' and 'existent' are inseparable and co-extensive.
Correction: Nasafi shows they are distinct: origination applies only at the moment of beginning, not during persistence.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the main flaw in the Mu'tazili argument that every existent in the physical world is originated?
A) The unseen is also originated
B) Origination only applies in the first state of existence, not in the state of persistence
C) The Mu'tazila have no argument against the Corporealists
D) Existence and origination are the same thing

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazili equation of existence and temporality by showing that origination is tied to the beginning of existence, not to existence itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that being originated attaches only at the first moment of existence. Reflect on your own existence: You were originated in your mother's womb, but now you persist. Do you live as if your created nature ended at birth, or do you still feel the weight of being a creature dependent on your Creator every moment? What would change if you truly internalised that your persistence does not erase your need for Him?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed that existence itself implies origination, and they used this to argue against the eternity of Allah. But Nasafi showed that origination is not tied to existence but to a beginning. Now consider your own assumptions: Do you ever equate 'being real' with 'being created'? In your heart, do you subconsciously think of Allah's existence as similar to that of His creation? How can you purify your understanding of His uncreatedness?
?
Nasafi says that in the state of persistence, a created thing is existent but not originated, except by preserving the name. This means that after your first moment, you are no longer being 'originated' but sustained. Do you live as if you are self-sustaining, or do you acknowledge that every breath is a new gift? What practical act can you do today to remind yourself that your existence is not self-sustained but constantly upheld by Allah?

Reductio Against Mu'tazilite View on Quran's Location
Imam Nasafi presents a reductio ad absurdum against Mu'tazilites on the Quran's location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi theologians used reductio ad absurdum to refute the Mu'tazilite claim that the Quran is created and exists in multiple locations as distinct instances.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilite view of a created, multiple Quran collapses into absurdity and sophistry.

This passage presents a powerful logical argument against the Mu'tazilite position on the Quran's createdness. The author, a Maturidi theologian, uses a reductio ad absurdum to show that their view leads to contradictions and ultimately aligns with sophistry. By following the steps of this argument, you will see how theological reasoning relies on consistent metaphysical principles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the full argument sink in before analyzing.
The passage is dense but self-contained.
2
Identify the target claim
The author addresses Iskaafi and Jubba'i, who hold that the Quran is created and exists in multiple places as multiple individual instances. Note how this contrasts with the Maturidi view.
3
Follow the reductio
The author lists consequences: if the Quran is created in each recitation and writing, then the same speech exists in countless tongues and mushafs, yet it would simultaneously increase and decrease. This is impossible.
Focus on the phrase 'one thing' (شيء واحد) and its implications.
4
Understand the analogy
The author compares the Mu'tazilite position to claiming all black things share a single blackness, or a single body exists in east and west. Such claims are dismissed as foolish. This strengthens the absurdity.
The analogy shows the logical inconsistency of the Mu'tazilite position.
5
Conclude with the dilemma
The author presents a dilemma: if the Mu'tazilite accepts the analogy as valid, he contradicts reason; if he rejects it, he condemns his own position. The argument ends by associating the view with sophistry.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول للإسكافي والجبائي : إن كان القارئ إذا قرأ القرآن، فهذا كلام الله تعالى قام بهذا اللسان، ولو كتب في المصحف قام بذلك المصحف وهو متلو ومكتوب، وهو بعينه في أكثر من ألف ألف مصحف، وقائم بأكثر من ألف ألف لسان وهو شيء واحد، ويقرأ الإنسان بعدما لم يكن يقرأ فيوجب في لسانه، ويكتب في مصحف بعد أن لم يكن فيصير قائما به وهو بعينه في ألفي مصحف ببخارى وفى مثل ذلك بقيروان المغرب، وكذا في جميع ديار أمصار الإسلام وقراها، وهو بنفسه شيء متحد الذات ليس بمتعدد، ثم يوجد في مصحف يكتب الآن ولم يزدد ويعدم عن مصحف انعدم ولم ينتقص وينعدم عن واحد مع وجوده في مصاحف أخرى، فلم يلزم الاستحالة واتصافه بالوجود والعدم فلا أصح إذا من مذهب السوفسطائية ولسنا نظن أن مجنونا يرضى بنسبه مثل هذا القول إليه. أرأيت لو أن قائلا قال: إن جميع ما اتصف من الأجسام بالسواد اتصف بسواد واحد حل في المحال كلها، وكذا البياض وسائر الألوان، وكذا الحركات والسكنات، وكذا القدرة والإرادات، وكذا الجسم الواحد يوجد في حالة واحدة بالمشرق والمغرب، وفي ألف كورة ومكان. أفيلتفت إلى قوله ويضيع الوقت بالإصغاء إلى ما يخيله السوداء إليه أنه دليله؟ أم يعرض عن معارضته، ويقضي عليه بأول الوهلة بالحماقة والوقاحة؟ فإن قال بالأول خالف العقلاء أجمع. وإن قال بالثاني قضى على نفسه بما قضى به على هذا القائل.
Then we say to Al-Iskaafi and Al-Jubba'i: If the reader when he recites the Quran, then this is the speech of God (Allah ta'ala) that has arisen in this tongue, and if he writes it in the mushaf it has arisen in that mushaf, and it is recited and written, and it is the very same in more than a thousand thousand mushafs, and it exists in more than a thousand thousand tongues while being one thing, and a person reads it after he was not reading it, so it comes into existence in his tongue, and he writes it in a mushaf after it was not, so it comes to exist in it, and it is the very same in two thousand mushafs in Bukhara and likewise in Qayrawan in the Maghreb, and likewise in all the cities and villages of the lands of Islam, and it is in itself a single self-identical thing, not multiple, then it exists in a mushaf that is written now and it has not increased, and it ceases to exist from a mushaf that has perished and it has not decreased, and it ceases to exist from one while existing in other mushafs. So impossibility is not necessary and its being qualified by existence and non-existence is not valid. So then it is nothing but the doctrine of the sophists. And we do not think that a madman would be pleased to have such a statement attributed to him. Have you considered if someone said: All bodies that are qualified by blackness are qualified by a single blackness that inheres in all places, and likewise whiteness and all other colors, and likewise movements and quiescences, and likewise power and wills, and likewise a single body exists in a single state in the east and the west, and in a thousand regions and places. Would he turn to his statement and waste time listening to what his blackness imagines to be his proof? Or would he turn away from opposing him and judge him at first glance to be foolish and shameless? If he says the first, he contradicts all rational people. And if he says the second, he has judged against himself with what he judged against this speaker.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a proof by reductio ad absurdum against the Mu'tazilite view that the Quran is created and exists in multiple places as multiple instances. The author first outlines the logical consequences of their position: the Quran would be the very same speech existing in countless tongues and mushafs, yet it would also be created anew in each recitation and writing, leading to the absurdity of a single self-identical thing simultaneously increasing and decreasing, existing and ceasing. He likens this to the sophist (sufistai'iyya) doctrine. He then strengthens the argument with an analogy: if someone claimed that all black things share a single blackness or a single body could be in the east and west simultaneously, that would be dismissed as foolish. The dilemma concludes: if the Mu'tazilite accepts the comparison as valid, he contradicts reason; if he rejects it, he condemns his own position.

Key Terms
الإسكافي
الجبائي
السوفسطائية
عين
متحد الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the author is arguing that the Quran is multiple or created. In fact, he is exposing the absurdity of that very claim.
Correction: The author uses reductio to show that the Mu'tazilite view implies impossible contradictions and is therefore false.

Checkpoint
What does the author use to illustrate the absurdity of the Mu'tazilite view?
A) The idea of a single blackness inhering in all black things
B) The claim that the Quran is uncreated
C) The fact that recitation is an accident
D) The consensus of rational people

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite view that the Quran is created and multiple leads to logical contradictions, reducing it to sophistry and self-refutation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe it is the very speech of Allah, or do you subconsciously treat it as a created product like any other book? How would your recitation change if you were absolutely certain you were uttering the eternal, uncreated speech of your Lord?
?
The Mu'tazilite position leads to absurdity, but do you ever treat Allah's attributes as multiple or compartmentalized in your mind? Where in your understanding of Allah do you risk falling into a similar contradiction—such as believing His mercy and justice are in tension?
?
Imam Nasafi says even a madman would not accept such a view. What does it say about your own heart if you find yourself accepting comfortable or popular positions about Allah without subjecting them to the rigorous logic that the scholars demand? Will you commit to testing your beliefs against the proofs of the Quran and Sunnah, even when they challenge your assumptions?

Purpose in Originated vs. Eternal Existence
Distinguishes originated and eternal existence regarding purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why only originated existence, not eternal existence, requires a purpose or cause.

Core Idea
Originated things need a reason; the Eternal needs none.

This passage presents a foundational distinction in Islamic theology: the difference between created beings and the Eternal Creator when it comes to purpose. The author argues that asking for the 'why' behind an eternal attribute is like asking why God exists before creation—a question that reveals misunderstanding of the nature of the Necessary Existent. Let's follow the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic original once, then the English translation. Notice the contrast between 'al-muhdath' (originated) and 'al-qadim' (eternal).
2
Identify the two claims
Find where the author states that originated existence is attached to causes and purposes, and that eternal existence is not. Note the reasoning for each.
The author uses the phrase 'إذ المحدث لم يكن ثم كان' to explain why originated beings need a purpose.
3
Examine the analogy
The author compares questioning the purpose of God's eternal existence to foolishness. Reflect on why this analogy strengthens the argument.
The analogy shows that demanding a purpose for an eternal attribute is logically incoherent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نكشف عن المعنى فنقول: إن الأصل أن وجود المحدث هو الذي يتعلق بالعلل والحكم، لا وجود القديم، إذ المحدث لم يكن ثم كان بتكوين غيره إياه فيتقصى عن الحكمة التي لأجلها أحدثه الصانع وأوجده. فأما ما كان لا ابتداء لوجوده وهو واجب الوجود لذاته، لم يكن وجوده متعلقا بمعنى وراء ذاته الذي هو واجب الوجود أليس أن من قال: لا حكمة في وجود صانع العالم سابقا على العالم سبقا لا نهاية له يستحق وينسب إلى الغباوة والجهل لما مر من العلة، فكذا هذا.
Then we uncover the meaning and say: The principle is that the existence of the originated thing is what is attached to causes and purposes, not the existence of the eternal. For the originated was not then came to be by the bringing into being of another, so it seeks the wisdom for which the Maker brought it into existence and created it. As for that which has no beginning to its existence and is necessary of existence in itself, its existence is not attached to a meaning beyond its essence which is necessarily existent. Is it not that whoever says: 'There is no wisdom in the existence of the Maker of the world prior to the world with a priority that has no end' deserves and is attributed to stupidity and ignorance due to the cause that has passed? So likewise this.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is a foundational kalam argument about the distinction between created and eternal beings regarding purpose (hikma). The author states that originated existence (muhdath) is inherently tied to causes and purposes because it comes into being through another's action. Therefore it requires a reason for its creation. In contrast, the Eternal (al-Qadim) has no beginning and exists necessarily in itself; its existence is not dependent on any external purpose. The author then uses an analogy: it would be foolish to ask about the wisdom of God's existence before creation, since that existence is eternal and has no cause. Similarly, God's speech, being eternal, does not require a purpose for its existence in pre-eternity.

Key Terms
المحدث
القديم
العلل
الحكم
الحكمة
واجب الوجود لذاته
الغباوة والجهل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Every action of God, including His eternal attributes, must have a purpose.
Correction: This passage clarifies that only originated acts require a purpose; eternal existence does not, because it is necessary in itself and has no cause.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key difference between originated existence and eternal existence?
A) Originated existence is attached to causes and purposes; eternal existence is not.
B) Both require wisdom for their existence.
C) Eternal existence is created by God.
D) Originated existence is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Originated existence requires a purpose; eternal existence does not, because it is necessary in itself and beyond causation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

When you face a trial, do you always demand to know the purpose behind it, as if God's actions must have a reason you can grasp? Write one specific area where you will stop insisting on an explanation and trust His eternal wisdom.
?
The passage says it is foolish to ask about the wisdom of God's existence before creation. Have you ever questioned why God created you with your particular circumstances, treating your existence as if it needed a purpose beyond His eternal decree? What would it look like to accept your existence as an expression of His necessary being, rather than a problem to be solved?

The Debate on Whether Allah Was Creator in Pre-Eternity
Nasafi recounts conflicting positions on whether Allah was Khaliq in pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different positions among Islamic theologians on whether Allah was described as 'Creator' in pre-eternity, and how the Maturidi position resolves the debate.

Core Idea
Was Allah called 'Creator' before creation? The answer reveals deep truths about divine attributes.

This passage from Nasafi presents a key theological debate: is the attribute of 'Creator' eternal or originated? Different schools took different views, and the Maturidi position resolves the tension by grounding creatorship in the eternal attribute of takwin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overview of the debate. Notice the different groups mentioned.
2
Identify the four positions
Identify each of the four positions: the majority (Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, Ahl al-Hadith), Abu al-Hudhayl, the Karramiyya, and the Maturidis (ashabuna). Note how each defines Allah being 'Khaliq' in pre-eternity.
3
Compare the Karrami and Maturidi affirmations
Both the Karramiyya and Maturidis affirm that Allah was Creator in pre-eternity, but they differ: the Karramiyya interpret it as power to create, while the Maturidis ground it in the eternal attribute of takwin subsisting with His essence.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider the final statement: everything that is an attribute of Allah is eternal. This is the Maturidi resolution—He was described by all attributes in pre-eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلف القائلون بحدوث التكوين أن الله تعالى هل كان في الأزل خالقا رازقا مصورا محيبا ومميتا أم لا؟ فذهب جمهور المعتزلة والنجارية وجميع متكلمي أهل الحديث أنه ما كان خالقا حتى حدث المخلوق، وكذا في سائر الصفات. وقال أبو الهذيل العلاف: إنه كان في الأزل خالقا بمعنى أنه سيخلق. وقالت الكرامية : إنه كان في الأزل خالقا بالخالقية رازقا بالرازقية، وكذا في سائر الصفات ويفسرون الخالقية بالقدرة على التخليق. وقال أصحابنا : إنه كان خالقا لقيام صفة الخلق وهو التكوين بذاته في الأزل، كما كان عالما قادرا سميعا بصيرا وصار الحاصل أن جميع ما هو صفة الله تعالى كان أزليا ، وهو تعالى كان موصوفا به في الأزل ، تعالى ربنا من أن يحدث له صفات المدح.
Then those who held the origination of takwin differed: was Allah Most High in pre-eternity a Creator, Provider, Shaper, Giver of life and Giver of death or not? The majority of the Mu'tazila, the Najjariyya, and all the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith held that He was not a Creator until the created thing occurred, and likewise for the other attributes. Abu al-Hudhayl al-Allaf said: He was in pre-eternity a Creator in the sense that He will create. The Karramiyya said: He was in pre-eternity a Creator with creatorship (khaliqiyya), a Provider with providership (raziqiyya), and likewise for the other attributes, and they interpret khaliqiyya as the power to bring into existence. Our companions said: He was a Creator because the attribute of creation (khalq) — which is takwin — subsisted with His essence in pre-eternity, just as He was Knowing, Powerful, Hearing, Seeing. And the result is that everything that is an attribute of Allah Most High was eternal, and He Most High was described by it in pre-eternity. Exalted is our Lord above having attributes of praise come into existence for Him.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage presents the differing views on whether Allah was Creator in pre-eternity. It begins by framing the question: For those who say takwin is originated, was Allah in pre-eternity a Creator, Provider, etc.? The majority of Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, and Ahl al-Hadith say He was not a Creator until the created thing came about. Then Abu al-Hudhayl proposes that He was Creator in pre-eternity in the sense that He will create (future sense). The Karramiyya affirm that He was a Creator with creatorship, which they interpret as the power to create. Finally, the Maturidis (ashabuna) state that He was a Creator because the attribute of creation (takwin) is eternal, so His description as Creator is eternal. He is eternally described by all His attributes. The passage concludes that all of Allah's attributes are eternal and He was described by them in pre-eternity.

Key Terms
الخالق
الخالقية
التخليق
التكوين
صفات الذات
صفات الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think all schools agreed that Allah was not Creator in pre-eternity.
Correction: Actually, the Karramiyya and Maturidis affirm that Allah was Creator in pre-eternity, though with different interpretations (power vs. eternal attribute).

Checkpoint
How do the Karramiyya interpret the meaning of Allah being 'Khaliq' in pre-eternity?
A) As the power to create
B) As actually creating eternally
C) As not being Creator
D) As will to create

Key Takeaway
All of Allah's attributes, including that of being Creator, are eternal; He was described by them in pre-eternity, as affirmed by the Maturidis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah was always the Creator even before any creation existed, what does that mean for your reliance on His ability to create solutions in your life before you even ask? Do you truly trust that His attribute of creation is eternally ready to act on your behalf?
?
The passage concludes that all of Allah's attributes are eternal and He was described by them in pre-eternity. Is there any attribute of Allah that you sometimes think of as 'temporary' or only relevant when you need it? How would your worship change if you consistently remembered that He is eternally everything He is?
?
You have just read a detailed theological debate about Allah's attributes. But this is not mere information—it is about who your Lord is. Does your heart tremble with awe that the Creator's very attribute of creation is eternal and perfect? Or do you treat this as an abstract discussion, safe and detached from your daily life?
