Five Categories of Quranic Theological Proofs
Imam al-Nasafi lists five categories of Quranic evidences for theological doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five categories of Quranic proofs that Imam al-Nasafi identifies for establishing theological doctrines such as the existence of God, His oneness, and resurrection.

Core Idea
The Quran contains rational proofs for five foundational theological doctrines.

Imam al-Nasafi presents a systematic overview of how the Quran itself provides reasoned arguments for core Islamic beliefs. In this passage, he enumerates five distinct types of proofs, each supported by specific Quranic verses. This lesson unpacks each category and shows how the Quran engages the intellect.

Guided Path
1
Proof of the world's origination
Read the first category about proofs for the temporal origination of the world. Notice how the Quran argues that anything subject to change cannot be divine, citing verses like 'I do not love those that set.'
This refutes the possibility of multiple eternal gods.
2
Proof of the Creator's existence
Read the second category about proofs for the existence of the Maker. The Quran presents verses challenging self-creation or creation from nothing, urging reflection on signs in the universe.
3
Proof of the Creator's oneness
Read the third category about proofs for the oneness of the Maker. Imam al-Nasafi references earlier arguments against Jews, Christians, and polytheists from Surat al-Ma'ida and Surat al-An'am.
4
Refutation of naturalism
Read the fourth category about refuting natural properties (tabā'i'). The Quran uses the verse about diverse tracts of land to argue against inherent natures.
5
Proof of resurrection
Read the fifth category about proofs for resurrection. The Quran argues from the first creation to the return, emphasizing that what is more difficult in our estimation is also possible for Allah.
The passage highlights the subtlety of the Quranic argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه آخر من دلالات الكتاب ما تضمن من دلائل حدوث العالم استحالة القول بالألوهية من تعتري عليه الحوادث ويتعاقب عليه الأضداد المتباينة من نحو قوله: ﴿ لَا أُحِبُّ الْآفِلِينَ ﴾ وقوله: ﴿ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ آيَاتٌ لِلْمُوقِنِينَ وَفِي أَنفُسِكُمْ أَفَلَا تُبْصِرُونَ ﴾ ودلالة ثبوت الصانع من نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ أَمْ خُلِقُوا مِنْ غَيْرِ شَيْءٍ أَمْ هُمُ الْخَالِقُونَ أَمْ خَلَقُوا السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ ﴾ وقوله: ﴿ وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَنْ خَلَقَكُم مِّن تُرَابٍ ثُمَّ إِذَا أَنتُم بَشَرٌ تَنتَشِرُونَ ﴾ وقوله: ﴿ وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَن يُرْسِلَ الرِّيَاحَ مُبَشِّرَاتٍ ﴾ وقوله: ﴿ إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَالْفُلْكِ الَّتِي تَجْرِي فِي الْبَحْرِ بِمَا يَنفَعُ النَّاسَ وَمَا أَنزَلَ اللَّهُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مِن مَّاءٍ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا وَبَثَّ فِيهَا مِن كُلِّ دَابَّةٍ وَتَصْرِيفِ الرِّيَاحِ وَالسَّحَابِ الْمُسَخَّرِ بَيْنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ لَآيَاتٍ لِّقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ ﴾ في آيات كثيرة يطول حصرها وإحصاؤها حرض فيها على التأمل والتفكر، ونبه عن المعنى الموجب أن يكون لهذه المحدثات صانع دلالة توحيد الصانع على ما سبق ذكر بعضها في إثبات وحدانية الصانع ومحاجة اليهود والنصارى والمشركين على ما تتضمن سورتا المائدة والأنعام، وذلك على وجه يتعجب المبرز في صنعة الكلام الماهر في وجوه الخصام من ذلك. ودلالة بطلان القول بالطبائع من نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ قِطَعٌ مُّتَجَاوِرَاتٌ ﴾ الآية. ودلالة إثبات البعث وإثبات الاستدلال بالبدء على الإعادة، وبيان إثبات القدرة على ما هو الأصعب في تقدير عقولنا على ما هو الأهون فيه، ولو لم يكن في ذلك إلا قوله: ﴿ وَضَرَبَ لَنَا مَثَلًا وَنَسِيَ خَلْقَهُ ﴾ إلى آخره.. لكان حقيقاً أن يتعجب العاقل منه بل يتحير ويبهت من لطف تلك المحاجة واستمالها على إبطال جميع ما يتخالج فيه عن الشبه ووجوهها، وهذا لأن إنكار حدوث ما يدعي أحد حدوثه وإدعاء استحالته يعتمد وجوهاً خمسة لا يعدوها.
And another aspect of the evidences of the Book: what it contains of proofs for the temporal origination of the world — the impossibility of divinity being attributed to what is subject to events and is succeeded by opposing opposites — such as His saying: 'I do not love those that set' and His saying: 'And on the earth are signs for those who are certain, and in yourselves; do you not see?' And proof of the existence of the Maker from His saying, may He be exalted: 'Or were they created from nothing, or are they the creators? Or did they create the heavens and the earth?' and His saying: 'And among His signs is that He created you from dust, then behold, you are humans spreading out' and His saying: 'And among His signs is that He sends the winds as bearers of glad tidings' and His saying: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the alternation of the night and the day, and the ships that sail in the sea with what benefits mankind, and what Allah sends down from the sky of water, giving life thereby to the earth after its death, and dispersing in it every creature, and the directing of the winds and the clouds subdued between the sky and the earth, are signs for a people who use reason' — in many verses whose enumeration and counting would be lengthy, which urge reflection and contemplation, and alert to the meaning that necessarily entails that these originated things have a Maker. And proof of the oneness of the Maker as previously mentioned in establishing the oneness of the Maker and debating the Jews, Christians, and polytheists as contained in Surat al-Ma'ida and Surat al-An'am, in a manner that would amaze one proficient in the craft of kalam, skilled in the ways of disputation. And proof of the falsehood of the claim of natural properties from His saying, may He be exalted: 'And in the earth are neighbouring tracts' — the verse. And proof of establishing resurrection and establishing inference from the first creation to the return, and demonstrating the establishment of power over what is more difficult in our minds' estimation to what is easier in it. And if there were nothing in that except His saying: 'And he strikes for Us an example and forgets his own creation' to its end, it would be worthy that the intelligent person should marvel at it, indeed be bewildered and astounded at the subtlety of that argument and its winning over to refute all that afflicts one from doubts and their aspects. And this is because denial of the temporal origination of what someone claims to be originated and the claim of its impossibility relies on five ways that do not exceed them.
Source pages p. 757

Commentary
This passage lists five categories of Quranic proofs for theological doctrines. First, proofs for the temporal origination of the world (ḥudūth al-ʿālam) by arguing that anything subject to change cannot be divine, citing verses like 'I do not love those that set' and those about signs in the earth and selves. Second, proofs for the existence of the Creator (thubūt al-Ṣāniʿ) through verses that question creation from nothing or self-creation. Third, proofs for the oneness of the Maker (tawḥīd al-Ṣāniʿ) referencing earlier arguments against Jews, Christians, and polytheists. Fourth, refutation of naturalism (ibṭāl al-qawl bi-l-ṭabāʾiʿ) using the verse about diverse tracts of land. Fifth, proofs for resurrection (ithbāt al-baʿth) by arguing from the first creation to the return, and demonstrating divine power over what is considered more difficult. The passage concludes that denial of temporal origination depends on five ways, which the Quranic arguments refute.

Key Terms
دلائل حدوث العالم
ثبوت الصانع
توحيد الصانع
بطلان الطبائع
إثبات البعث
وجوه خمسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quran only contains moral guidance and not reasoned theological arguments.
Correction: This passage shows that the Quran explicitly provides rational proofs for foundational beliefs like God's existence, unity, and resurrection.

Checkpoint
How many categories of Quranic proofs does the author list in this passage?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Six

Key Takeaway
The Quran presents rational arguments for five key theological claims: the world's creation, the existence and oneness of God, the falsehood of naturalism, and the reality of resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you had to defend the existence of God using only the proof from creation (e.g., 'Or were they created from nothing or are they the creators?'), would you be able to do so without hesitation? What does your hesitation say about the strength of your conviction?
?
The Quran says the signs are for 'a people who use reason'. Are you one of those? Which one of these five proofs have you actually internalized to the point that it changes your actions?
?
If you deny naturalism based on the verse about diverse tracts, does your daily life reflect trust in Allah's direct control over every event, or do you still act as if natural causes are independent?

Quranic Call to Reflection and the Five Bases of Denial
Nasafi cites Quranic verses urging reflection and identifies five bases for denying occurrence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses Quranic verses to urge reflection and introduces the five bases for denying occurrence.

Core Idea
Quranic reflection leads to recognizing the five rational bases of denial.

Nasafi opens by marshaling Quranic evidence that calls humanity to contemplate the created world. He then reveals that denial of occurrence rests on only five possible grounds, setting up a systematic refutation. This lesson establishes the scriptural foundation for the kalam arguments that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the Quranic verses
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Pay attention to the verses cited: from Surat ar-Rum, Surat an-Naml, and Surat al-Baqarah.
These verses are classic proofs for God's existence through reflection.
2
Identify the three categories of evidence
Nasafi mentions evidence for the Maker, against natural dispositions (taba'i'), and for resurrection. Find each in the text.
This shows the breadth of Quranic argumentation.
3
Understand the purpose: denial has finite bases
The passage ends by stating that denial of occurrence relies on five ways. This is the key structural point for the upcoming discussion.
These five ways will be enumerated in subsequent lessons.
4
Reflect on the Quranic grounding
Notice that Nasafi emphasizes the Quranic origin of these arguments, countering the idea that kalam is purely philosophical.
This guards against the misconception that the five ways are abstract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تُرَابٍ ثُمَّ إِذَا أَنتُم بَشَرٌ تَنتَشِرُونَ. وقوله: ﴿ وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَن يُرْسِلَ الرِّيحَ مُبَشِّرَاتٍ ﴾ وقوله: ﴿ إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَالْفُلْكِ الَّتِي تَجْرِي فِي الْبَحْرِ بِمَا يَنفَعُ النَّاسَ وَمَا أَنزَلَ اللَّهُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مِن مَّاءٍ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا وَبَثَّ فِيهَا مِن كُلِّ دَابَّةٍ وَتَصْرِيفِ الرِّيحِ وَالسَّحَابِ الْمُسَخَّرِ بَيْنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ لَآيَاتٍ لِّقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ ﴾ في آيات كثيرة يطول حصرها وإحصاؤها حرض فيها على التأمل والتفكر، ونبه عن المعنى الموجب أن يكون لهذه المحدثات صانع دلالة توحيد الصانع على ما سبق ذكر بعضها في إثبات وحدانية الصانع ومحاجة اليهود والنصارى والمشركين على ما تتضمن سورتا المائدة والأنعام، وذلك على وجه يتعجب المبرز في صنعة الكلام الماهر في وجوه الخصام من ذلك. ودلالة بطلان القول بالطبائع من نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ قِطَعٌ مُّتَجَاوِرَاتٌ ﴾ الآية. ودلالة إثبات البعث وإثبات الاستدلال بالبدء على الإعادة، وبيان إثبات القدرة على ما هو الأصعب في تقدير عقولنا على ما هو الأهون فيه، ولو لم يكن في ذلك إلا قوله: ﴿ وَضَرَبَ لَنَا مَثَلًا وَنَسِيَ خَلْقَهُ ﴾ إلى آخره لكان حقيقاً أن يتعجب العاقل منه بل يتحير ويبهت من لطف تلك المحاجة واستمالها على إبطال جميع ما يتخالج فيه عن الشبه ووجوهها، وهذا لأن إنكار حدوث ما يدعي أحد حدوثه وادعاء استحالته يعتمد وجوهاً خمسة لا يعدوها.
From dust, then behold you are human beings spreading out. And His saying: 'And among His signs is that He sends the winds as bearers of glad tidings.' And His saying: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the alternation of the night and the day, and the ships which sail through the sea with that which benefits people, and what Allah has sent down from the heavens of rain, giving life thereby to the earth after its lifelessness and dispersing therein every [kind of] moving creature, and [His] directing of the winds and the clouds controlled between the heaven and the earth are signs for a people who use reason.' In many verses whose enumeration and counting would be lengthy, He urged reflection and thought, and alerted about the meaning that necessitates that these originated things have a Maker, evidence of the oneness of the Maker as we have previously mentioned some of it in establishing the unicity of the Maker and debating the Jews, Christians, and polytheists as contained in the two Surahs al-Ma'idah and al-An'am, in a manner that the expert in the art of kalam and the skilled in the modes of argumentation would marvel at. And evidence of the invalidity of the claim of natural dispositions (al-taba'i') from His saying: 'And within the land are neighboring plots' etc. And evidence of establishing resurrection and establishing inference from the beginning upon the return, and a clarification of establishing power over what is more difficult in the estimation of our intellects over what is easier in it. And if there were nothing in that except His saying: 'And he strikes for Us an example and forgets his creation' etc., it would be worthy that the intelligent person marvels at it, rather he would be bewildered and stunned at the subtlety of that argumentation and its drawing towards refuting all that he entertains of doubts and their aspects. And this is because the denial of the occurrence of something that someone claims to have occurred and the claim of its impossibility relies on five ways that do not exceed them.
Source pages p. 758

Commentary
This passage is an introduction by Nasafi to the Quranic encouragement of reflection and the identification of five bases for denying the occurrence of something. He begins by citing several Quranic verses that call for contemplation of creation: the verse from Surah ar-Rum about human creation from dust, the verse about winds as glad tidings, and the longer verse from Surah al-Baqarah listing signs in the heavens and earth. He says there are many such verses urging reflection and thought. These verses alert one to the meaning that necessitates that these originated things (al-muhdathat) have a Maker. He then mentions that the evidence for God's oneness has been discussed earlier in the context of debating Jews, Christians, and polytheists, as found in Surah al-Ma'idah and al-An'am. Next, he mentions evidence against the theory of natural dispositions (al-taba'i'), citing the verse 'And within the land are neighboring plots.' Then he mentions evidence for resurrection and inference from the beginning to the return, and a clarification of power over what is more difficult. He highlights the verse 'He strikes for Us an example and forgets his creation' as a profound argument that astounds the intelligent. Finally, he states the key point: the denial of the occurrence of something and the claim of its impossibility depends on five ways that do not exceed them. This sets up the enumeration that follows.

Misconception: The five ways are merely a philosophical construct without Quranic basis.
Correction: Nasafi grounds them in Quranic argumentation, as he has just cited numerous verses and connects them to the five ways.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the sky, the rain, and the wind, do you truly reflect as the Quran commands, or do you pass them by as mere natural events? What one change will you make today to train your mind to see the signs of your Creator in everyday phenomena?
?
The lesson states that denial of occurrence can only take five forms. Which of these forms might be lurking in your own heart when you doubt God's power over something—perhaps in your struggles or future? Will you ask Allah tonight to purify your heart from any such denial?
?
The Quran's arguments are so subtle that even skilled debaters marvel. Do you humbly submit to the Quran's reasoning, or do you pridefully hold onto doubts? Commit this week to memorize one of the cited verses and ponder its meaning until it moves you to action.

The Proof of Resurrection from Divine Power
Sanusi argues for resurrection's possibility from divine power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic verses establish the rational possibility of resurrection through divine power.

Core Idea
Nothing is impossible for Allah, not even resurrection after death.

Sanusi begins by addressing the skeptics who deny resurrection. He draws from two Quranic verses to argue that if Allah can create the heavens and earth, reviving the dead is even more plausible. This lesson unpacks the logical reasoning behind that claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author begins with a Quranic verse and builds his argument.
2
Understand the argument from greater to lesser
The author argues that creation of heavens and earth is greater in our estimation, so if Allah has power over that, then revival (which is smaller) is even more certainly within His power.
This is a logical argument from greater to lesser.
3
Reflect on the instantaneous command
The second verse shows that Allah's command is immediate, so nothing is difficult for Him. This removes any excuse for denying resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِقَدِرٍ عَلَى أَن يَخلُقَ مِثْلَهُمْ بَلَى (۱) إن أمرًا ما لا يفوت قدرته لعظمه فإن خلق السماوات والأرض في تقدير عقولنا أعظم من إحياء الموتى، فلما كانت قدرته ثابتة على ذلك كانت على الإحياء ثابتة بل أدل في تقدير عقولكم، ثم نبه بقوله: ﴿ إِنَّمَا أَمْرُهُ إِذَا أَرَادَ شَيْئًا أَن يَقُولَ لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ ﴾ (٢) أنه ليس ممن يتعذر عليه شيء (۳) أو يصعب عليه أمر بل سرعة وجود ما يوجده كسرعة قول واحد منكم "كن"، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك لم يبق وجه يمتنع وجود الإعادة والإحياء بعد الموت، فلا معنى للإنكار هذا والله أعلم - مضمون الآية، غير أن الله تعالى لا يخرج كلامه مخرج كلام الواحد منا (٤) إذا ناظر خصمه بل يخرج مخرج مخاطبة السادة العبيد، والأرباب المماليك، فأخرج هذه المعاني على هذا النظم العجيب والوصف البليغ الذي تكاد العقول الوافرة، والألباب الكاملة تتحير (٥) في رونقه وفخامته وبلاغته وفصاحته، بل تذهل من هيبته وجلالته، ثم إن المتكلمين من سلف الأمة منذ تكلموا في هذه الخصوم وأثبتوا دلائلها فى التصاريف لم يزيدوا على ما في الكتاب من مع الإشارة إلى ذلك، بل لم يستخرجوا من قعور تلك البحور وإن غاصت فيها أفكارهم المسائل عشر ما فيها من درر الحجج وغرر المعاني والنكت ثم من الممتنع الذي لا تصور لثبوته ولا يطلق العقل إخطاره بالقلب أن يخرج رجل أمي بلغ أشده، ومضى أربعين سنة من عمره في قوم لم يكن لهم من العلم بدلالة الكلام وحدوث العالم وثبوت الصانع وتوحيده وثبوت صفاته والبعث بعد الموت حظ، ولم يخطر ببال أحد منهم من ذلك شيء، لم يقرعوا للتوحيد بابا، ويجعلون الأنداد والأصنام شيئًا عجابًا، لم يختلف إلى أحد للتعلم ولا درس كتابًا فيه شيء من ذلك ثم عرف من تلقاء نفسه جميع هذه الوجوه التي مر ذكرها بدلائلها، ثم بين على وجه قصر عن بلوغ كنهه ونهايته ممن لا يحصون كثرة من العلماء المبرزين المخصوصين برجاحة العقول والألباب وحدة الخواطر وجودة القرائح الذين زجوا أعمارهم في تعلم العلوم الملية والارتياض بالمعالم الحكمية، والبحث عن حقائق الأشياء، واكتساب العلم بقوانين الجدل وشرائط البرهان. هذا محال ممتنع.
He is able to create the like of them, certainly (1). (This means) nothing escapes His power due to its greatness, for the creation of the heavens and earth, in the estimation of our intellects, is greater than reviving the dead. Since His power is established over that, it is established over revival—indeed more indicative in your estimation. Then He drew attention by His saying: 'His command, when He wills something, is only to say to it 'Be,' and it is' (2)—that He is not one for whom anything is impossible (3) or difficult, but rather the speed of existence of what He brings into existence is like the speed of a single one of you saying 'Be.' And if the matter is thus, no aspect remains that would prevent the existence of returning and revival after death. So there is no meaning to denial here—and Allah knows best—this is the meaning of the verse, except that Allah the Exalted does not bring forth His speech in the manner of a single one of us (4) when arguing with his opponent, but rather brings it forth in the manner of addressing masters of servants and lords of slaves. So He brought out these meanings in this wondrous composition and eloquent description at which abundant intellects and perfect minds almost become confused (5) regarding its beauty, grandeur, eloquence, and clarity—indeed they are stunned by its awe and majesty. Then indeed the theologians (mutakallimun) from the predecessors of this community, since they spoke about these arguments and established their proofs in the treatises, did not add beyond what is in the Book, with reference to that; rather they did not extract from the depths of those seas—even if their thoughts dived into them—a tenth of the pearls of proofs, gems of meanings, and subtleties. Then it is impossible, with no conception of its existence and with the intellect not allowing its passing into the heart, that an unlettered man who had reached his prime and spent forty years of his life among a people who had no share of knowledge of the evidence of kalam (dialectical theology), the temporality of the world, the existence of the Maker, His oneness, the establishment of His attributes, and the resurrection after death—and nothing of that had occurred to the mind of anyone among them—they had not knocked on a door for tawhid, and they considered rivals and idols as something astounding, he did not frequent anyone for learning, nor studied any book containing any of that, then came to know on his own accord all these aspects that were mentioned with their proofs, then explained them in a way that fell short of the comprehension and ultimate limit of uncountable multitudes of distinguished scholars, characterized by soundness of intellect and minds, sharpness of thoughts, excellence of natural gifts, who spent their lives learning the religious sciences, exercising with philosophical landmarks, investigating the realities of things, and acquiring knowledge through the laws of disputation and conditions of demonstration. This is impossible and inconceivable.
Source pages p. 761

Commentary
This passage is a combined proof of the possibility of resurrection and the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) through the inimitability of the Quran. The author begins by citing the Quranic verse (36:81) that questions how the Creator of the heavens and earth could be incapable of creating the like of the dead—thus affirming His power over resurrection. He elaborates that the creation of the heavens and earth is greater in our estimation, so if that power is established, resurrection is even more indicative of that power. Then he cites verse (36:82) that Allah's command is instantaneous, so nothing is difficult for Him. Therefore, resurrection after death is not impossible. Next, the author notes that although the Quran conveys this meaning, its style is not like human argumentation; rather it is in a majestic manner suited to the divine nature. The eloquence of the Quran is such that even the most intelligent are bewildered by its beauty and awe. Then he makes a key point: the mutakallimun (early Muslim theologians) who later developed detailed proofs did not add anything beyond what the Quran already contains by way of indication; they only extracted a fraction of the depths of arguments present in it. This sets up the final proof: it is absolutely impossible for an unlettered man, raised among a people ignorant of these theological concepts, to have produced such profound knowledge on his own. He could not have learned from anyone, nor studied books. Yet he presented all these arguments with their proofs in a way that surpasses even the greatest scholars who devoted their lives to such sciences. This impossibility proves that his knowledge was from divine revelation, thus proving his prophethood.

Key Terms
قدرة
إعادة
إحياء
محال ممتنع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection is only a symbolic or metaphorical event.
Correction: The passage argues it is a literal and rationally necessary possibility given Allah's absolute power.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is resurrection logically possible?
A) Because it is a small matter for Allah compared to creation of heavens and earth
B) Because the Quran mentions it explicitly
C) Because the Prophet demonstrated it
D) Because it happens every spring

Key Takeaway
The Quranic argument for resurrection is grounded in divine omnipotence and the instantaneous nature of creation.

The Proof of Prophethood from Quranic Inimitability
Sanusi proves prophethood through the Quran's miraculous nature and the Prophet's illiteracy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the inimitability of the Quran proves the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
An unlettered man could not have produced such profound knowledge without divine revelation.

After establishing the possibility of resurrection, Sanusi turns to a broader argument for prophethood. He points to the unmatched eloquence of the Quran and the fact that even the greatest scholars only scratched its surface. Then he presents a powerful proof: the Prophet Muhammad was unlettered and lived among a people ignorant of theology, yet he produced arguments that no human could have acquired on his own. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of Quranic eloquence
Read the first part of the passage about the Quran's wondrous composition and how even the most intelligent are bewildered by it.
2
Understand the limited extraction of scholars
Notice that the early theologians, despite their expertise, only extracted a fraction of the Quran's treasures. This shows the Quran's superiority.
3
Grasp the impossibility of the unlettered Prophet
The author lists the Prophet's circumstances: unlettered, among ignorant people, no teachers, no books. Yet he produced all these arguments, surpassing learned scholars. This is impossible without revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This sets up the final proof: it is absolutely impossible for an unlettered man, raised among a people ignorant of these theological concepts, to have produced such profound knowledge on his own. He could not have learned from anyone, nor studied books. Yet he presented all these arguments with their proofs in a way that surpasses even the greatest scholars who devoted their lives to such sciences. This impossibility proves that his knowledge was from divine revelation, thus proving his prophethood.

حدوث العالم
ثبوت الصانع
توحيد

بعث
محال ممتنع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet Muhammad learned these arguments from earlier scriptures or scholars.
Correction: The passage emphasizes he was unlettered and his people were ignorant, eliminating any human source.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the author considers the Prophet's knowledge to be miraculous?
A) The Prophet was known for his intelligence
B) The Quran contains scientific facts
C) The Prophet was unlettered and his people were ignorant, yet he produced arguments surpassing scholars
D) The Prophet memorized all books

Key Takeaway
The Quran's inimitability and the Prophet's illiteracy combine to prove his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The early theologians found no need to add anything to the Quran. Have you ever felt that the Quran alone is sufficient for your faith, or have you sought other authorities to validate it? In what area of your life are you relying on something other than Allah's word as your ultimate guide?
?
If the Prophet's illiteracy made his knowledge a clear miracle, what does that imply about your own excuses for not studying the Quran deeply? How will you change your relationship with the Book so that it becomes your primary source of knowledge and conviction?

The Three Divisions of Faith in Allah
Nasafi divides faith in Allah into three sections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith in Allah according to Imam al-Nasafi comprises three essential divisions: belief in His existence, His oneness, and His attributes.

Core Idea
Faith in Allah is threefold: existence, oneness, and attributes.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi begins the detailed treatment of creedal beliefs by identifying faith in Allah as the most important pillar. He then breaks it down into three categories, emphasizing that each aspect addresses a specific form of deviation. The passage provides both the conceptual framework and scriptural evidence for the first two divisions.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to grasp the author's initial classification.
Notice the phrase 'وهو ينقسم إلى أقسام ثلاثة' – this is the key division.
2
Identify the two explicit divisions
The passage explicitly mentions faith in His existence and faith in His oneness. Understand why each is important: existence guards against atheism (ta'til), and oneness guards against polytheism (shirk).
3
Consider the implied third division
The author says three sections but only names two. The third is likely faith in His attributes, which will be discussed later. Reflect on why attributes are necessary for complete faith.
4
Examine the scriptural proof for oneness
The author cites Quran 3:64 as evidence for God's oneness. Read the verse and see how it calls to worship Allah alone.
This is a key interfaith dialogue verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنبدأ بالاعتقادات فنقول : الركن الأهم منها الإيمان بالله تعالى وهو ينقسم إلى أقسام ثلاثة أحدها : الإيمان بوجوده ليسلم عن التعطيل وقد مر أنه عليه السلام ورد بذلك وأرشد إلى الدلالة على ثبوته في كتابه الذي أتى به في مواضع على ما مر، ثم الإيمان بوحدانيته ليسلم عن الشرك، وقد ورد به فأقام الدلالة عليه وجرد القول بالتصريح بذلك فقال : تَعَالَوْا إِلَى كَلِمَةٍ سَوَاءٍ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَكُمْ أَلَّا نَعْبُدَ إِلَّا اللَّهَ
So we begin with beliefs and say: the most important pillar among them is faith in Allah Almighty, and it is divided into three sections: one of them: faith in His existence to be safe from atheism, and it has passed that he (peace be upon him) came with that and guided to the proof for its establishment in his book which he brought in places as previously mentioned, then faith in His oneness to be safe from polytheism, and he came with that and established the proof for it and declared the statement explicitly by saying: 'Come to a word that is common between us and you: that we not worship except Allah'.
Source pages p. 763

Commentary
This passage begins the detailed discussion of beliefs. The author identifies the most important pillar as faith in Allah (iman bi Allah). He then divides this faith into three sections (aqsam thalatha), but only explicitly mentions two: (1) faith in His existence (iman bi wujudihi) to avoid atheism (ta'til), and (2) faith in His oneness (iman bi wahdaniyyatihi) to avoid polytheism (shirk). He references earlier passages where the Prophet (peace be upon him) guided to proofs of divine existence in the Quran. For oneness, he cites the Quranic verse from Surah Al Imran (3:64) calling to a common word: worship none but Allah. The third division is not stated here but is presumably faith in His attributes, which the author likely addresses later.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think faith in Allah is only about believing He exists, ignoring the need to believe in His oneness and attributes.
Correction: Imam al-Nasafi shows that faith in Allah includes multiple essential elements: existence, oneness, and attributes. Each element guards against a specific error.

Checkpoint

B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you truly internalized that your faith in Allah's existence must lead you to act as if He is always watching? How does your daily life reflect this belief, and what will you change today to make it more real?
?
When you recite the Shahada, do you consciously affirm both that Allah exists and that He alone deserves your worship? Identify one area of your life where you might be associating something else — like status, comfort, or approval — with Allah, and commit to purifying it this week.
?
If you neglect learning about Allah's attributes, how can you claim to love and know Him? Set aside time this week to study one attribute (like al-Rahman) and let it transform your view of His mercy.

Belief in Allah's Existence Guards Against Denial
The author introduces belief in Allah and states the first division: belief in existence as protection against ta'til.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in Allah's existence is the first division of iman and protects against ta'til (denial of God), and that the Prophet brought evidence for it in the Quran.

Core Idea
The foundation of iman is affirming Allah's existence, which defeats atheism (ta'til).

Belief in Allah is not a single concept but has essential components. The first and most basic is affirming His existence. The author of this passage emphasizes that this belief protects against the dangerous error of ta'til, the denial of God's existence. In this lesson, we will examine this foundational division and the evidence the Prophet presented.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the flow.
2
Identify the first division
Note that the first division is belief in existence (wujud). Recognize that it is presented as a protection against ta'til.
Ta'til means denial or negation of God's existence.
3
Understand ta'til
Reflect on why denying God's existence is a grave error that must be guarded against.
4
Observe the evidence
The author mentions that the Prophet brought evidence in the Quran. Consider that this shows iman is built on rational and scriptural proof.
The specific verses are not listed here but referenced as already mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنبدأ بالاعتقادات فنقول : الركن الأهم منها الإيمان بالله تعالى وهو ينقسم إلى أقسام ثلاثة أحدها : الإيمان بوجوده ليسلم عن التعطيل وقد مر أنه عليه السلام ورد بذلك وأرشد إلى الدلالة على ثبوته في كتابه الذي أتى به في مواضع على ما مر، ثم الإيمان بوحدانيته ليسلم عن الشرك، وقد ورد به فأقام الدلالة عليه وجرد القول بالتصريح بذلك فقال : تَعَالَوْا إِلَى كَلِمَةٍ سَوَاءٍ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَكُمْ أَلَّا نَعْبُدَ إِلَّا اللَّهَ وأمر أتباعه بالتمسك به وإجراء كلمة الإخلاص على ألسنتهم، فنجدهم على اختلاف طبقاتهم يتنادون بها في البر والبحر والليل والصباح والرواح مصدقين لما وصفوا به في الكتب المنزلة بأنهم يملأون الأرض تهليلاً وتكبيرًا وتحميدًا وتسبيحا، وأهل سائر الأديان لا يذكرونها إلا بالفرط وذلك قوله تعالى: وَأَلْزَمَهُمْ كَلِمَةَ التَّقْوَى وَكَانُوا لَحَقِّ بِهَا وَأَهْلَهَا ثم الإيمان بصفاته ليسلم عن التشبيه وقد ورد به وأقام الدلالة عليه فيما جاء به من الكتابة نحو قوله: وَءَايَةٌ لَهُمُ الَّيْلُ نَسْلَخُ مِنْهُ النَّهَارَ وإلى قوله: ذَلِكَ تَقْدِيرُ الْعَزِيزِ الْعَلِيمِ وقوله: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ وما ذكر في آخر سورة الحشر.
We begin with beliefs and say: the most important pillar among them is belief in Allah Most High, and it is divided into three divisions: one: belief in His existence to be safe from negation (ta'til), and it has passed that he (peace be upon him) brought that and guided to evidence for its affirmation in his Book which he brought in places as passed; then belief in His oneness to be safe from polytheism, and he brought it and established evidence for it and made the statement explicit by saying: 'Come to a common word between us and you: that we worship none but Allah' and commanded his followers to adhere to it and utter the word of sincerity on their tongues, and we find them, despite their different classes, calling out to each other with it on land and sea, night and morning, going out, affirming what they are described with in the revealed books that they fill the earth with tahleel, takbeer, tahmeed, and tasbeeh, while people of other religions do not mention it except rarely; and that is His saying: 'And He inspired them with the word of taqwa, and they were more deserving of it and its people'; then belief in His attributes to be safe from anthropomorphism, and he brought it and established evidence for it in what he brought of the Book, like His saying: 'And a sign for them is the night: We strip from it the day' and up to His saying: 'That is the determination of the Mighty, the Knowing' and His saying: 'Nothing is like Him, and He is the Hearing, the Seeing' and what is mentioned at the end of Surah al-Hashr.
Source pages p. 763

Commentary
This passage begins the section on beliefs (i'tiqadat) and declares that the most important pillar is belief in Allah. This belief is then subdivided into three parts. The first is belief in His existence (wujud) to guard against ta'til (denial of God). The author mentions that the Prophet brought evidence for this in the Quran. The second is belief in His oneness (wahdaniyya) to guard against shirk (polytheism). The Prophet explicitly commanded people to worship Allah alone, as in the verse calling to a common word. The author describes how Muslims, unlike others, constantly proclaim the word of tawhid. The third is belief in His attributes (sifat) to guard against tashbih (anthropomorphism). The author cites verses that affirm divine attributes while negating resemblance, such as 'Nothing is like Him' and the attributes of hearing and sight, and the description at the end of Surah al-Hashr. Thus, the three aspects protect against three extremes: denial of God, polytheism, and anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
iman
wujud
ta'til

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think belief in Allah requires no evidence or that denying existence is not a serious error.
Correction: The passage shows that affirming existence is fundamental and guards against the grave error of ta'til, and that the Prophet provided evidence.

Checkpoint

A) Shirk
B) Tashbih
C) Ta'til
D) Bid'ah

Key Takeaway

?

Belief in Allah's Oneness Guards Against Polytheism
The author presents the second division: belief in Allah's oneness as protection against shirk, with evidence and description of Muslim practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the second division of iman is belief in Allah's oneness (wahdaniyya), which protects against shirk (polytheism), and see how the Prophet commanded tawhid and the Muslims' practice.

Core Idea
Affirming Allah's oneness is the core of tawhid that shields from shirk.

After establishing existence, the next essential belief is that Allah is one. The author explains how the Prophet called people to worship Allah alone and commanded his followers to proclaim the word of sincerity. This lesson explores the second division and its role in protecting against polytheism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on oneness

Examine the Quranic evidence

4

Notice how Muslims constantly glorify Allah with tahleel, takbeer, etc., unlike others.
This fulfills the description in earlier scriptures.

Belief in Allah's Attributes Guards Against Anthropomorphism
The author presents the third division: belief in Allah's attributes as protection against tashbih, with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the third division of iman is belief in Allah's attributes (sifat), which protects against tashbih (anthropomorphism), and that the Quran affirms divine attributes without resembling creation.

Core Idea
Affirming Allah's attributes without likeness preserves transcendence and avoids anthropomorphism.

The final division of belief in Allah concerns His attributes. It is crucial to affirm what Allah has described Himself with without falling into anthropomorphism (tashbih). This lesson examines the third division, its protective role, and the Quranic evidence cited by the author.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنبدأ بالاعتقادات فنقول : الركن الأهم منها الإيمان بالله تعالى وهو ينقسم إلى أقسام ثلاثة أحدها : الإيمان بوجوده ليسلم عن التعطيل وقد مر أنه عليه السلام ورد بذلك وأرشد إلى الدلالة على ثبوته في كتابه الذي أتى به في مواضع على ما مر، ثم الإيمان بوحدانيته ليسلم عن الشرك، وقد ورد به فأقام الدلالة عليه وجرد القول بالتصريح بذلك فقال : تَعَالَوْا إِلَى كَلِمَةٍ سَوَاءٍ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَكُمْ أَلَّا نَعْبُدَ إِلَّا اللَّهَ وأمر أتباعه بالتمسك به وإجراء كلمة الإخلاص على ألسنتهم، فنجدهم على اختلاف طبقاتهم يتنادون بها في البر والبحر والليل والصباح والرواح مصدقين لما وصفوا به في الكتب المنزلة بأنهم يملأون الأرض تهليلاً وتكبيرًا وتحميدًا وتسبيحا، وأهل سائر الأديان لا يذكرونها إلا بالفرط وذلك قوله تعالى: وَأَلْزَمَهُمْ كَلِمَةَ التَّقْوَى وَكَانُوا لَحَقِّ بِهَا وَأَهْلَهَا ثم الإيمان بصفاته ليسلم عن التشبيه وقد ورد به وأقام الدلالة عليه فيما جاء به من الكتابة نحو قوله: وَءَايَةٌ لَهُمُ الَّيْلُ نَسْلَخُ مِنْهُ النَّهَارَ وإلى قوله: ذَلِكَ تَقْدِيرُ الْعَزِيزِ الْعَلِيمِ وقوله: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ وما ذكر في آخر سورة الحشر.
We begin with beliefs and say: the most important pillar among them is belief in Allah Most High, and it is divided into three divisions: one: belief in His existence to be safe from negation (ta'til), and it has passed that he (peace be upon him) brought that and guided to evidence for its affirmation in his Book which he brought in places as passed; then belief in His oneness to be safe from polytheism, and he brought it and established evidence for it and made the statement explicit by saying: 'Come to a common word between us and you: that we worship none but Allah' and commanded his followers to adhere to it and utter the word of sincerity on their tongues, and we find them, despite their different classes, calling out to each other with it on land and sea, night and morning, going out, affirming what they are described with in the revealed books that they fill the earth with tahleel, takbeer, tahmeed, and tasbeeh, while people of other religions do not mention it except rarely; and that is His saying: 'And He inspired them with the word of taqwa, and they were more deserving of it and its people'; then belief in His attributes to be safe from anthropomorphism, and he brought it and established evidence for it in what he brought of the Book, like His saying: 'And a sign for them is the night: We strip from it the day' and up to His saying: 'That is the determination of the Mighty, the Knowing' and His saying: 'Nothing is like Him, and He is the Hearing, the Seeing' and what is mentioned at the end of Surah al-Hashr.
Source pages p. 763

Commentary
This passage begins the section on beliefs (i'tiqadat) and declares that the most important pillar is belief in Allah. This belief is then subdivided into three parts. The first is belief in His existence (wujud) to guard against ta'til (denial of God). The author mentions that the Prophet brought evidence for this in the Quran. The second is belief in His oneness (wahdaniyya) to guard against shirk (polytheism). The Prophet explicitly commanded people to worship Allah alone, as in the verse calling to a common word. The author describes how Muslims, unlike others, constantly proclaim the word of tawhid. The third is belief in His attributes (sifat) to guard against tashbih (anthropomorphism). The author cites verses that affirm divine attributes while negating resemblance, such as 'Nothing is like Him' and the attributes of hearing and sight, and the description at the end of Surah al-Hashr. Thus, the three aspects protect against three extremes: denial of God, polytheism, and anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
sifat
tashbih
tawhid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that affirming attributes necessarily implies anthropomorphism.
Correction: The passage shows that the Quran affirms attributes while explicitly denying likeness, so attributes are affirmed without tashbih.

Checkpoint
Which verse does the author cite that explicitly negates any likeness while affirming attributes?
A) 'And a sign for them is the night...'
B) 'That is the determination of the Mighty, the Knowing'
C) 'Nothing is like Him, and He is the Hearing, the Seeing'
D) The end of Surah al-Hashr

Key Takeaway
Belief in Allah's attributes is affirmed by the Quran without anthropomorphism, preserving divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'The Hearing, the Seeing,' do you find yourself imagining ears and eyes? What does that reveal about your understanding of tawheed? Commit to immediately following such thoughts with 'Nothing is like Him.'
?
Have you ever felt distant from Allah because you tried to picture Him and failed? How does this lesson's emphasis on affirming attributes without likeness free you from that struggle? Write down one attribute you will meditate on today without falling into tashbih.

Objection and Answer on the Impossibility of a Contrary to the Eternal
Al-Nasafi responds to an objection and entraps the Mu'tazilites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the impossibility of a contrary to the Eternal is grounded in the necessity of His permanence, and how this argument refutes the Mu'tazilite position on annihilation.

Core Idea
God's permanence is necessary, so no contrary can cause His non-existence.

In this passage, al-Nasafi addresses an objection from an anonymous critic who claims that the non-existence of the Eternal is impossible only because a contrary cannot be empowered over. Al-Nasafi corrects this by asserting that the true reason is the necessity of God's permanence. He then turns the argument against the Mu'tazilites al-Jubba'i and his son, showing that their own theory of annihilation leads to a contradiction. This lesson unpacks the logic of this objection-and-answer exchange and its implications for Maturidi theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the structure: a statement from an objector, then the author's response, and finally an entrapment against the Mu'tazilites.
The objection begins with 'فإن قيل'.
2
Identify the core argument
The author argues that the impossibility of the Eternal having a contrary is due to wujub al-baqa' (necessity of permanence), not because the contrary cannot be empowered. Understand why he emphasizes this distinction.
This is key to Maturidi theology.
3
Analyze the entrapment of al-Jubba'i
See how al-Nasafi uses the Mu'tazilite theory of annihilation (fana') against them. If annihilation is a single opposite that destroys all atoms, then they cannot consistently believe God can annihilate some atoms while preserving others.
This shows the internal coherence of the Maturidi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : إنما استحال عدم القديم لوجود ضده لاستحالة كون الضد مقدوراً عليه؛ لأن ما لم يكن مقدوراً في نفسه لم يكن له ضد يوصف به. قلنا لهم : إنما استحال أن يكون له ضد مقدور عليه لقادر لوجوب بقائه لولا ذلك لتصور وجود ضده، وهذا منا إلزام على الجبائي وابنه؛ إذ من مذهبهما أن عدم الأعراض بطريان أضدادهما عليهما وعدم الجواهر بإيجاد الله تعالى الفناء لا في محل وهو عرض مناف مضاد لجميع الجواهر فتفنى الجواهر لوجود ضدها، ولا تفنى الجواهر ما لم يوجد الفناء المضاد لها، ولهذا أنكرا قدرة الله تعالى على إفناء بعض الأجسام والجواهر مع بقاء بعضها، لأن الفناء لو لم يوجد لها لما تصور عدم جوهر ما، ولو وجد لكان ضد الجميع فيفنى الجميع.
For it is said: The non-existence of the Eternal is impossible due to the existence of its contrary only because it is impossible for the contrary to be empowered over; because that which is not empowered over in itself has no contrary ascribed to it. We say to them: It is impossible for it to have a contrary empowered over by a powerful agent only because of the necessity of its permanence; otherwise the existence of its contrary would be conceivable. And this from us is an entrapment against al-Jubba'i and his son, for from their doctrine is that the non-existence of accidents is by the advent of their contraries upon them, and the non-existence of atoms is by God's creation of annihilation (al-fana') not in a locus, and it is an opposite attribute contrary to all atoms, so atoms perish due to the existence of their contrary, and atoms do not perish unless the contrary annihilation exists for them. And for this reason they denied the power of God—exalted is God above what the wrongdoers and falsifiers say, a great exaltation—to annihilate some bodies and atoms while others remain, because if annihilation did not exist for them, the non-existence of any atom would not be conceivable, and if it existed, it would be contrary to all and would annihilate all.
Source pages p. 801

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer exchange within a larger argument about God's permanence. The objector claims that the only reason the non-existence of the eternal (God) due to a contrary is impossible is because such a contrary cannot be empowered over by a powerful agent; since a thing that is not empowered over has no contrary. The author (al-Nasafi) responds that the true reason is the necessity of God's permanence (wujub al-baqa'); otherwise, if permanence were not necessary, the existence of a contrary would be conceivable. Then the author notes that this argument is an entrapment (ilzam) against al-Jubba'i and his son, who hold that accidents cease by the advent of their contraries, and that atoms cease by God's creation of annihilation (fana')—an attribute that is opposite to all atoms. On their view, if annihilation is created, all atoms must perish simultaneously, so they cannot affirm God's power to annihilate some but not others. Thus the objection fails because it relies on a flawed conception of how things cease to exist.

Key Terms
ضد
قديم
بقاء
فناء
مقدور
جبائي
جوهر
عرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The impossibility of a contrary to God is because God is uncaused or because a contrary cannot be empowered over.
Correction: The true reason according to al-Nasafi is the necessity of God's permanence (wujub al-baqa'), which is an essential attribute. The objector's claim that the impossibility is due to the contrary not being empowered is incorrect.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is it impossible for the Eternal to have a contrary that could cause its non-existence?
A) Because the contrary cannot be created by God.
B) Because the Eternal's permanence is necessary, so a contrary cannot be conceived.
C) Because the Eternal has no opposite in essence.
D) Because the Eternal is not subject to power.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of the Eternal having a contrary is grounded in the necessity of His permanence, not merely the absence of a contrary, and this argument refutes the Mu'tazilite view on annihilation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's permanence is necessary and absolute, what does that imply about your own fleeting life? How should that reality reshape your priorities before the day ends?
?
The Mu'tazilites clung to a flawed logical system that prevented them from affirming God's full power over partial annihilation. Where in your own life do you hold onto a flawed logic or assumption that prevents you from fully submitting to Allah's power and wisdom? Will you let go today?
?
Al-Nasafi's entrapment forced his opponents to confront an inconsistency in their own beliefs. Are there inconsistencies between what you profess and how you live that you've been avoiding? What concrete step will you take within the next 24 hours to address one of them?

Proof that the Subsisting is Stronger in Existence than the Newly Originated
Second argument that the subsisting is stronger than the newly originated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof that the subsisting (al-baqi) is stronger in existence than the newly originated (al-hadith), based on necessity vs. possibility and dependency on power.

Core Idea
The subsisting is necessary in existence at the moment of the contrary; the newly originated is merely possible.

This passage presents a second argument from Imam al-Nasafi for the strength of the subsisting over the newly originated. The reasoning focuses on two key differences: the subsisting's existence is not contingent on a power that could be withheld, and at the moment the contrary arises, the subsisting is necessary in existence while the new is only possible. These distinctions reveal why what persists is ontologically stronger.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage ends mid-sentence; this is part of a larger argument.
2
Identify the two arguments
The passage contains two distinct proofs: (a) the subsisting's existence is not attached to a power that could withhold, (b) the subsisting is necessary in existence at the advent of the contrary while the new is possible. Find each one.
3
Reflect on key terms
Understand the Arabic terms: باقي (subsisting), حادث (newly originated), واجب الوجود (necessary of existence), جائز الوجود (possible of existence). How do they relate to the argument?
These terms are central to kalam reasoning about existence.
4
Consider the implication
Why does being necessary of existence imply greater strength? The author argues that necessity is not about duration but about ontological dependence. Think about how this refutes the idea that strength is merely about lasting longer.
This connects to the common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدليل على أن الباقي أقوى من الحادث في الوجود أن الباقي لم يتعلق وجوده بقدرة يصح منع القادر منه ويتوهم ذلك فيه، والحدث يتعلق وجوده بقدرة يصح منع القادر منه ويتوهم ذلك في الجملة، والدليل عليه أن الباقي واجب الوجود في حال طريان ضده عليه، والحادث جائز الوجود في حال حدوثه، ولا شك أن واجب الوجود أقوى في الوجود من جائز الوجود، على أن قوته ليس بأكثر من وجوده، ولا وجود للحادث قبل حالة الحدوث، فعدمه قبل حدوثه لا يكون موجبًا قوته في وجوده، والباقي له وجود قبل وجوده في هذه الحالة التي حدث فيه الضد فوجوده قبل وجوده موجب قوته في وجوده، والذي يقرأ هذا أن العرض الحادث
Then the proof that the subsisting (al-baqi) is stronger than the newly originated (al-hadith) in existence is that the subsisting's existence is not attached to a power from which the powerful agent could withhold and that could be imagined of it, while the newly originated's existence is attached to a power from which the powerful agent could withhold and that could be imagined of it in general. And the proof of it is that the subsisting is necessary of existence (wajib al-wujud) in the state of the advent of its contrary upon it, while the newly originated is possible of existence (ja'iz al-wujud) in the state of its occurrence, and there is no doubt that the necessary of existence is stronger in existence than the possible of existence, given that its strength is not more than its existence. And there is no existence for the newly originated before the state of occurrence, so its non-existence before its occurrence does not cause its strength in its existence. And the subsisting has an existence before its existence in this state in which the contrary occurred, so its existence before its existence causes its strength in its existence. And whoever reads this [will see] that the accident is newly originated...
Source pages p. 802

Commentary
This passage presents a second proof that the subsisting (al-baqi) is stronger in existence than the newly originated (al-hadith). The author gives two lines of reasoning: (1) The subsisting's existence is not contingent upon a power that could be withheld—meaning it is necessary, whereas the newly originated's existence depends on a power that could potentially not bring it about. (2) The subsisting is necessary in existence (wajib al-wujud) at the moment the contrary arises, while the newly originated is merely possible (ja'iz al-wujud) at the moment of its occurrence. That which is necessary is stronger in existence than that which is possible. Furthermore, the newly originated had no existence before its occurrence, so its prior non-existence does not contribute to its strength; but the subsisting had existence before the state in which the contrary appears, and that prior existence contributes to its strength. The passage ends mid-sentence referring to the accident as newly originated, continuing the argument.

Key Terms
باقي
حادث
وجود
قدرة
واجب الوجود
جائز الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Strength in existence is merely about duration or age.
Correction: The author argues it is about necessity vs possibility and dependency on power, not duration.

Checkpoint
Why does the author claim the subsisting is stronger in existence than the newly originated?
A) Because the subsisting has existed longer.
B) Because the subsisting is necessary in existence at the moment of the contrary's advent, while the new is only possible.
C) Because the subsisting does not depend on a cause.
D) Because the newly originated is weaker by nature.

Key Takeaway
The subsisting is stronger in existence because it is necessary and not contingent on a power that could withhold.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your existence is entirely dependent on a Power that could withhold it at any moment. Does that realization terrify you, or does it lead you to cling more tightly to the One whose existence is necessary? What would change in your daily life if you truly lived as a 'possible' being?
?
The subsisting gains strength from its prior existence. What in your past—your sins, your habits, your accomplishments—actually weakens you when trials come? Are you building a 'prior existence' that will give you strength in the face of life's contrary moments, or one that will crumble?
?
This proof distinguishes between the necessary and the possible. Where have you anchored your identity and security—in something that is truly necessary and unshakeable, or in something that could be taken away? What would it mean to transfer that anchor to the only Necessary Being?

The Proof from 'Khaliq Kulli Shay'' and the Mu'tazilite Objection
Al-Nasafi states the proof and the Mu'tazilite objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Haqq use the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' to prove God creates all actions, and the Mu'tazilite objection that the verse is specific to praiseworthy things.

Core Idea
God creates all things, but does the verse's purpose of praise allow evil acts?

Imam al-Nasafi first presents the central proof of Ahl al-Haqq: the Qur'anic verse 'Creator of everything' includes human actions, so God creates them. He then records the Mu'tazilite objection: the verse is meant for praise, and including sinful actions would turn praise into blame, so the verse must be specific. This lesson establishes the initial argument and the objection that the refutation must answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof
Read how Ahl al-Haqq use the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' to argue that God creates all human actions because they are 'things'.
The argument is based on the apparent generality of the verse.
2
Understand the objection
The Mu'tazilites argue that the verse is for praise; including evil actions would nullify praise. Identify the examples they give.
They list actions like slander and killing.
3
Notice the conclusion
The Mu'tazilites conclude that the verse is specific, not general, based on its purpose.
This sets up the refutation in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحجة لأهل الحق قوله تعالى : ( خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ ) وأفعال العباد أشياء فيكون الله تعالى خالقها لعموم الآية، والخصوم يعترضون على ذلك فيقولون: أفعال العباد مخصوصة من هذه الآية بدليل غرض الآية، فإنها خرجت مخرج التمدح وبدخول أفعال العباد تحتها يزول معنى التمدح بل يثبت معنى يوجب الذم، وهذا لأن من جملة أفعال العباد ما هو افتراء على الله تعالى ووصف له بما لا يليق بصفاته وشتم له وقتل أوليائه، وبسط اليد واللسان في رسله وأنبيائه، ومقابله سفرائه إلى خلقه وأمنائه على وحيه ومبلغي أمره ونهيه بكل ما قدروا عليه من المكروه ووسعه طوقهم من الجفوة، والمتعرض لشتم نفسه والافتراء عليه سفه في الشاهد الذي هو دليل يبتنى عليه أمور الغائب، فكيف الموجد لذلك والمخرج له من العدم إلى الوجود، فعلم بهذا أنه تعالى لم يرد بهذه الآية إن خرجت مخرج العموم إلا الخصوص. [ثم يرد عليهم:] يحققه أن ذات الله تعالى شيء بلا خلاف بيننا وبينكم، وكذا صفاته عند كثير منكم أشياء ولم تكن ذاته ولا صفاته داخلاً تحت هذه الآية لما في دخول ذلك فيها زوال ما سبقت له الآية من إثبات ما كان دخوله تحت الخطاب يوجب إبطال الفرض الذي سيق له الخطاب ويثبت ضد ذلك يمتنع دخوله تحته، وإن كان بحيث يتناوله اللفظ من حيث اللغة، وإن لم يخص شيء سواه مما يتناوله لفظ الخطاب فكيف وقد خص منه غيره مما هو مساو لذلك الغير في المعنى الموجب خروجه عن قضية الكلام، ولا شك أن إخراج بعض ما يتناوله اللفظ عن وضعه لمعنى يوجب إخراجه موجب إخراج يوجد فيه ذلك المعنى لاقتضاء القول التسوية في الحكم عند ثبوت المساواة في المعنى الموجب لذلك، على أن العام الذي خص منشئ يتوقف فيه عند كثير من أهل الأصول لصيرورته مجملاً، ولا يصح التعلق به لإثبات حكم جار مجرى الفروع يمكن إثباته بما لا وجه إلى إثباتها إلا الدليل القاطع الموجب للعلم الثابت بطريق التيقن، وعند أكثر أهل الأصول وإن لم ينقلب مجملاً إلا أنه يجب الحكم فيما وراء المخصوص من أفراد العموم وأحاده بطريق التيقن، بل يوجب ذلك بطريق غالب الرأي بلا خلاف بيننا وبينكم على أن هذا عندكم حكم العام وإن لم يخص منه شيء، والتعلق بمثل هذا الدليل في الأبواب الاعتقادية جهل بمواضع الحجاج ومواقع الأدلة ومراتبها في أنفسها ودرجات المحال التي يتعلق بها فيها، ويتبين بهذا أن لا متعلق بالآية في محل النزاع وموضع الخلاف.
The proof for the People of Truth is His statement, the Exalted: 'Creator of everything'. And the actions of servants are things, so God, the Exalted, is their Creator due to the generality of the verse. And the opponents object to that, saying: The actions of servants are excluded from this verse by evidence of the purpose of the verse, for it came in the form of praise, and if the actions of servants enter under it, the meaning of praise disappears; rather, a meaning that necessitates blame is established. This is because among the actions of servants are slander against God, description of Him with what does not befit His attributes, reviling Him, killing His saints, extending hand and tongue against His messengers and prophets, confronting His ambassadors to His creation and His trustees over His revelation and conveyers of His command and prohibition with all the harm they are capable of and the harshness their capacity allows. And the one who exposes himself to reviling his own soul and slander against it is foolish in the witnessed realm, which is a guide upon which matters of the unseen are based—so how about the one who brings that into existence and brings it out from non-existence to existence? So it is known by this that He, the Exalted, did not intend by this verse, if it came in the form of generality, except specificity. [Then he refutes them:] It is verified that the essence of God, the Exalted, is a thing without disagreement between us and you, and likewise His attributes according to many of you are things. Yet His essence and His attributes were not included under this verse, because if they entered it, the verse's purpose of establishing what the verse was brought for would be nullified; entering under the discourse would invalidate the purpose for which the discourse was set and establish its opposite, so their entering under it is impossible. Even if the wording encompasses them linguistically, and if nothing else among what the wording encompasses is excluded, then how [can it be] when it has excluded from it something else that is equal to that 'other' in the meaning that necessitates its exclusion from the purport of the speech? There is no doubt that excluding some of what the wording encompasses from its usage for a meaning that necessitates its exclusion necessitates excluding whatever that meaning is found in, because the statement requires equality in judgment when equality in the meaning that necessitates that is established. Moreover, the general that has been specified becomes ambiguous according to many of the scholars of usul, because it becomes a general/specified (mujmal). And it is not valid to rely on it to establish a ruling that runs in the course of subsidiary matters, which can only be established by decisive proof that necessitates knowledge established by way of certainty. According to most of the scholars of usul, even if it does not become ambiguous, it is obligatory to judge the remaining individuals and singular instances of the general beyond the specified by way of certainty; rather, it necessitates that by way of predominant opinion without disagreement between us and you—and this, according to you, is the ruling of the general even if nothing has been specified from it. Relying on such a proof in matters of belief is ignorance of the places of argumentation, the positions of proofs, their ranks in themselves, and the degrees of the topics to which they are applied. And by this it becomes clear that there is no basis for relying on the verse in the point of dispute and the locus of disagreement.
Source pages p. 858

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer argument. The author first states the proof of Ahl al-Haqq (the People of Truth) from the Qur'anic verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' (Creator of everything). Since human actions are 'things', God must be their Creator based on the generality of the verse. The Mu'tazilite opponents object: the verse is meant for praise, and including sinful human actions would spoil that praise, because actions like slander and killing would attribute blameworthy acts to God. They argue that the verse is specific, not general, based on its purpose. The author then refutes this objection by analogy: the Mu'tazilites themselves do not include God's essence and attributes under this verse, even though they are 'things', because including them would contradict the verse's purpose of establishing creation. Similarly, human actions can be excluded. The author further argues on principles of usul al-fiqh: a general that has been specified becomes ambiguous and cannot be used for certainty in foundational matters. The argument is that the Mu'tazilites are inconsistent and that their use of the verse is invalid in theological disputes.

Key Terms
أهل الحق (Ahl al-Haqq)
خلق كل شيء (Khaliq kulli shay')
العموم (al-umum)
الخصوص (al-khusus)
التمددح (al-tamadduh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' is absolutely general and includes everything without exception.
Correction: The Mu'tazilites argue that the verse's purpose (gharad) restricts its generality to praiseworthy things, because including evil actions would contradict the praise.

Checkpoint
Why do the Mu'tazilites claim the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' is specific rather than general?
A) Because the word 'shay'' is ambiguous.
B) Because including sinful actions would contradict the purpose of praise.
C) Because the verse is abrogated.
D) Because human actions are not 'things'.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite objection hinges on the purpose of the verse: praise, which excludes blameworthy actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see terrible injustices in the world, do you find any part of your heart blaming God? How does this lesson's emphasis on the purpose of praise challenge you to reconsider that tendency?
?
The Mu'tazilites argued that attributing evil acts to God would imply blame on Him. In your own life, when you sin, do you subtly shift responsibility to God? How can you honestly take full ownership of your actions while still affirming that God is the Creator of all things?
?
The objection in this lesson is based on the idea that the verse's purpose of praise (tamadduh) restricts its meaning. Think of a verse you often recite that praises God. Does your daily life reflect that praise, or do your actions contradict it? What concrete change can you make today to align your deeds with the praise of Allah?
