Refutation of the Mu'tazilite Objection: Consistency and Usul Arguments
Al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite objection with an analogy and usul arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's refutation using the analogy of God's essence and attributes, and the usul al-fiqh principles that undermine the Mu'tazilite reliance on a specified general.

Core Idea
If the Mu'tazilites exclude God's essence from the verse, they must also exclude human actions.

In this passage, al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite objection with two main arguments. First, he points out that the Mu'tazilites themselves would not include God's essence and attributes under the verse, even though they are 'things', because that would contradict the verse's purpose; similarly, human actions can be excluded. Second, he argues on usul al-fiqh grounds that a general that has been specified becomes ambiguous (mujmal) and cannot be used for certainty in foundational matters, making the verse an invalid proof for their claim.

Guided Path
1
Understand the analogy
Al-Nasafi points out that the Mu'tazilites agree God's essence and attributes are 'things' but are not included under the verse. This shows inconsistency if they insist on including human actions.
The analogy highlights that the verse's purpose overrides literal generality.
2
Grasp the usul argument
A general that has been specified becomes ambiguous (mujmal) and cannot be used for certainty. Even if not ambiguous, it only gives probable knowledge, not certainty, in theological matters.
This is a key principle from Islamic legal theory.
3
Realize the conclusion
The Mu'tazilites' own admission that God's essence is excluded shows inconsistency, and their reliance on a specified general is invalid in foundational beliefs.
Thus the verse cannot be used as proof in this dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحجة لأهل الحق قوله تعالى : ( خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ ) وأفعال العباد أشياء فيكون الله تعالى خالقها لعموم الآية، والخصوم يعترضون على ذلك فيقولون: أفعال العباد مخصوصة من هذه الآية بدليل غرض الآية، فإنها خرجت مخرج التمدح وبدخول أفعال العباد تحتها يزول معنى التمدح بل يثبت معنى يوجب الذم، وهذا لأن من جملة أفعال العباد ما هو افتراء على الله تعالى ووصف له بما لا يليق بصفاته وشتم له وقتل أوليائه، وبسط اليد واللسان في رسله وأنبيائه، ومقابله سفرائه إلى خلقه وأمنائه على وحيه ومبلغي أمره ونهيه بكل ما قدروا عليه من المكروه ووسعه طوقهم من الجفوة، والمتعرض لشتم نفسه والافتراء عليه سفه في الشاهد الذي هو دليل يبتنى عليه أمور الغائب، فكيف الموجد لذلك والمخرج له من العدم إلى الوجود، فعلم بهذا أنه تعالى لم يرد بهذه الآية إن خرجت مخرج العموم إلا الخصوص. [ثم يرد عليهم:] يحققه أن ذات الله تعالى شيء بلا خلاف بيننا وبينكم، وكذا صفاته عند كثير منكم أشياء ولم تكن ذاته ولا صفاته داخلاً تحت هذه الآية لما في دخول ذلك فيها زوال ما سبقت له الآية من إثبات ما كان دخوله تحت الخطاب يوجب إبطال الفرض الذي سيق له الخطاب ويثبت ضد ذلك يمتنع دخوله تحته، وإن كان بحيث يتناوله اللفظ من حيث اللغة، وإن لم يخص شيء سواه مما يتناوله لفظ الخطاب فكيف وقد خص منه غيره مما هو مساو لذلك الغير في المعنى الموجب خروجه عن قضية الكلام، ولا شك أن إخراج بعض ما يتناوله اللفظ عن وضعه لمعنى يوجب إخراجه موجب إخراج يوجد فيه ذلك المعنى لاقتضاء القول التسوية في الحكم عند ثبوت المساواة في المعنى الموجب لذلك، على أن العام الذي خص منشئ يتوقف فيه عند كثير من أهل الأصول لصيرورته مجملاً، ولا يصح التعلق به لإثبات حكم جار مجرى الفروع يمكن إثباته بما لا وجه إلى إثباتها إلا الدليل القاطع الموجب للعلم الثابت بطريق التيقن، وعند أكثر أهل الأصول وإن لم ينقلب مجملاً إلا أنه يجب الحكم فيما وراء المخصوص من أفراد العموم وأحاده بطريق التيقن، بل يوجب ذلك بطريق غالب الرأي بلا خلاف بيننا وبينكم على أن هذا عندكم حكم العام وإن لم يخص منه شيء، والتعلق بمثل هذا الدليل في الأبواب الاعتقادية جهل بمواضع الحجاج ومواقع الأدلة ومراتبها في أنفسها ودرجات المحال التي يتعلق بها فيها، ويتبين بهذا أن لا متعلق بالآية في محل النزاع وموضع الخلاف.
The proof for the People of Truth is His statement, the Exalted: 'Creator of everything'. And the actions of servants are things, so God, the Exalted, is their Creator due to the generality of the verse. And the opponents object to that, saying: The actions of servants are excluded from this verse by evidence of the purpose of the verse, for it came in the form of praise, and if the actions of servants enter under it, the meaning of praise disappears; rather, a meaning that necessitates blame is established. This is because among the actions of servants are slander against God, description of Him with what does not befit His attributes, reviling Him, killing His saints, extending hand and tongue against His messengers and prophets, confronting His ambassadors to His creation and His trustees over His revelation and conveyers of His command and prohibition with all the harm they are capable of and the harshness their capacity allows. And the one who exposes himself to reviling his own soul and slander against it is foolish in the witnessed realm, which is a guide upon which matters of the unseen are based—so how about the one who brings that into existence and brings it out from non-existence to existence? So it is known by this that He, the Exalted, did not intend by this verse, if it came in the form of generality, except specificity. [Then he refutes them:] It is verified that the essence of God, the Exalted, is a thing without disagreement between us and you, and likewise His attributes according to many of you are things. Yet His essence and His attributes were not included under this verse, because if they entered it, the verse's purpose of establishing what the verse was brought for would be nullified; entering under the discourse would invalidate the purpose for which the discourse was set and establish its opposite, so their entering under it is impossible. Even if the wording encompasses them linguistically, and if nothing else among what the wording encompasses is excluded, then how [can it be] when it has excluded from it something else that is equal to that 'other' in the meaning that necessitates its exclusion from the purport of the speech? There is no doubt that excluding some of what the wording encompasses from its usage for a meaning that necessitates its exclusion necessitates excluding whatever that meaning is found in, because the statement requires equality in judgment when equality in the meaning that necessitates that is established. Moreover, the general that has been specified becomes ambiguous according to many of the scholars of usul, because it becomes a general/specified (mujmal). And it is not valid to rely on it to establish a ruling that runs in the course of subsidiary matters, which can only be established by decisive proof that necessitates knowledge established by way of certainty. According to most of the scholars of usul, even if it does not become ambiguous, it is obligatory to judge the remaining individuals and singular instances of the general beyond the specified by way of certainty; rather, it necessitates that by way of predominant opinion without disagreement between us and you—and this, according to you, is the ruling of the general even if nothing has been specified from it. Relying on such a proof in matters of belief is ignorance of the places of argumentation, the positions of proofs, their ranks in themselves, and the degrees of the topics to which they are applied. And by this it becomes clear that there is no basis for relying on the verse in the point of dispute and the locus of disagreement.
Source pages p. 858

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer argument. The author first states the proof of Ahl al-Haqq (the People of Truth) from the Qur'anic verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' (Creator of everything). Since human actions are 'things', God must be their Creator based on the generality of the verse. The Mu'tazilite opponents object: the verse is meant for praise, and including sinful human actions would spoil that praise, because actions like slander and killing would attribute blameworthy acts to God. They argue that the verse is specific, not general, based on its purpose. The author then refutes this objection by analogy: the Mu'tazilites themselves do not include God's essence and attributes under this verse, even though they are 'things', because including them would contradict the verse's purpose of establishing creation. Similarly, human actions can be excluded. The author further argues on principles of usul al-fiqh: a general that has been specified becomes ambiguous and cannot be used for certainty in foundational matters. The argument is that the Mu'tazilites are inconsistent and that their use of the verse is invalid in theological disputes.

Key Terms
العام المخصوص (al-amm al-makhsus)
المجمل (al-mujmal)
الأصول (al-usul)
التيقن (al-tayaqqun)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite objection is logically sound and consistent.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows they are inconsistent because they exclude God's essence from the verse for the same reason they want to exclude human actions, yet they do not apply the same reasoning.

Checkpoint
What is the first argument al-Nasafi uses to refute the Mu'tazilite objection?
A) The verse is abrogated.
B) God's essence and attributes are also 'things' but are not included under the verse.
C) Human actions are not really 'things'.
D) The verse is clear and needs no interpretation.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi refutes by highlighting inconsistency and showing that a specified general lacks certainty for theological proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about God or His actions based on a verse you assumed was clear, without considering that later scholars specified it or that it might not yield certainty? How would your faith change if you demanded tayaqqun for every theological claim you accept?
?
The Mu'tazilites excluded God's essence from the verse to protect its purpose. Are you consistent in your own reasoning about divine texts, or do you sometimes twist meanings to fit your preferences? What would it take for you to submit to a text even when it challenges your assumptions?
?
If the only valid proofs in theology are those yielding certainty, how many of your current religious positions would survive that standard? Are you willing to say 'I do not know' and remain silent on matters where you lack decisive evidence, or do you prefer comfortable certainty that may be false?

Why Excluding Disputed Acts Preserves God's Unique Praise
Nasafi counters the objection that the verse is praise by proving exclusion preserves uniqueness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi defends the necessity of excluding human voluntary acts from the verse's generality to preserve the unique praise of God.

Core Idea
True praise requires exclusivity; if others share the quality, the praise is destroyed.

Nasafi now tackles a key objection: if the verse (e.g., 'Allah is the Creator of everything') is meant as praise, why would it specify human acts? He argues that praise only works when the quality is unique to God. Excluding the disputed acts actually preserves the praise, because including them would mean lowly creatures share in that quality, which would destroy the praise entirely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Let the author's argument flow before interpreting.
Notice the concise and forceful style of Nasafi's response.
2
Identify the core argument
Nasafi first asserts the verse is praise, then states praise requires uniqueness. He then shows that if the disputed acts are excluded, the meaning reduces to something shared by all creatures with voluntary actions, thus losing the praise.
Ask yourself: Why does Nasafi call this position 'extreme ignorance'?
3
Reflect on the consequence
Consider how this argument defends the Maturidi position that human acts are not directly created by God, while still affirming God's unique creative power.
This connects to broader discussions of divine causality and human agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجاب عن هذه الشبهات أن يقال : لا ريب أن الآية خرجت مخرج التمدح ولا شك أن معنى التمدح يحصل بما يختص هو تعالى به ولا يشاركه فيه غيره، ولو خص منه المتنازع فيه لزال هذا المعنى لأن الآية تصير في التقدير: خالق كل شيء هو فعله أو خالق كل شيء ليس بفعل غيره، وعندكم يساويه في هذا المعنى كل ما له الأفعال الاختيارية من البق والبعوض والكلب والخنزير، فإن كل شيء من هذه الأشياء عندكم خالق كل شيء هو فعل ما وليس هو يفعل غيره ولا تمدح الله تعالى بما يساويه فيه كل ما دب ودرج وإن هان وضعف في نفسه، وهذا جهل مفرط بالحقائق، فإن إبقاء ما سيقت له الآية، بإثبات أمر يوجب ثبوته إبطال ما سبقت له الآية والقصد إلى إبقاء الشيء إثبات ما يوجب إبطاله جهل لا یوازيه جهل ولا يخفى فساده على من له أدنى لب.
And one responds to these doubts by saying: There is no doubt that the verse came in the form of praising (tamadduh), and there is no doubt that the meaning of praising is attained by what is unique to Him, exalted, and in which none else shares with Him. And if the disputed [acts] were specified out of it, this meaning would be removed, because the verse would become, in estimation: 'Creator of everything is His action, or Creator of everything is not the action of another.' And according to you, every being that has voluntary actions—from fleas, mosquitoes, dogs, and pigs—equals Him in this meaning, for every one of these things according to you is the creator of everything that is its action, and it does not do the action of another, and God, exalted, is not praised by what every crawling creature, however lowly and weak in itself, equals Him in. And this is extreme ignorance of realities, for preserving what the verse was intended for, by establishing something whose establishment necessitates the invalidation of what the verse was intended for, and the intention to preserve a thing by establishing what necessitates its invalidation, is ignorance that no ignorance equals, and its corruption is not hidden from anyone with the least intellect.
Source pages p. 860

Commentary
This passage is an answer to a doubt regarding the verse being a praise. Nasafi responds: The verse was revealed as praise (tamadduh), and praise is only valid for what is unique to God, which no other shares. If the disputed acts (human actions) were excluded from the generality of the verse, the praise would be lost because the verse would then be interpreted as 'Creator of everything is His action' or 'Creator of everything is not the action of another'—a meaning that according to the opponents applies equally to all beings with voluntary actions, including lowly creatures like fleas, mosquitoes, dogs, and pigs. Each of these, according to them, is the creator of its own actions. Thus God would be praised by a quality that even the humblest creature shares, which is absurd. Nasafi calls this extreme ignorance, because preserving the intended purpose of the verse cannot be achieved by establishing something that would invalidate that very purpose. This reasoning is so clear that anyone with minimal intellect can see its corruption.

Key Terms
تمدح
اختصاص
فعل اختياري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse's praise purpose means that it must include all acts, including human voluntary acts, without exception.
Correction: Nasafi shows that praise requires exclusivity; including human acts would imply that God shares a creative quality with lowly creatures, thus destroying the praise.

Checkpoint
What happens to the meaning of praise if the disputed acts are excluded from the verse according to Nasafi?
A) The praise becomes stronger.
B) The verse becomes meaningless.
C) The praise is removed because God's uniqueness is lost.
D) The verse becomes a command.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi argues that preserving the verse's praise actually requires excluding human voluntary acts, because including them would make God share a quality with lowly creatures, destroying the praise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you praise Allah as the Creator of everything, do you truly feel that no one else deserves that praise? Or do you sometimes act as if your own efforts or abilities are independent of His creation, subtly reserving that praise for yourself? What would it mean for your worship if you fully internalized that even the smallest creature cannot share in His unique praise?
?
Nasafi argues that excluding human acts from God's creation reduces His praise to a quality shared by fleas and mosquitoes. Is there an area of your life where you are 'excluding' Allah's involvement—thinking that your success, your choices, or your righteousness is your own doing? How would your gratitude change if you recognized that even your free choices are created by Him?
?
The passage calls the attempt to preserve the verse's purpose while excluding human acts 'ignorance that no ignorance equals'. Have you ever tried to maintain a good intention (like glorifying Allah) while holding a belief that actually undermines it? Will you search your heart today for any subtle belief that, if left uncorrected, might reduce your praise of Allah to something even a mosquito could share?

Response to doubts about the verse of creation
The author responds to doubts about the verse 'Creator of everything'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse 'Creator of everything' constitutes divine praise that is exclusive to God, and why excluding certain actions from its scope would undermine that praise.

Core Idea
The verse is divine praise; if others create their own acts, God's exclusive praise is lost.

This passage tackles a subtle objection about the famous verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything' (Quran 13:16). Some argued that evil actions cannot be from God, so the verse must refer only to good actions. Here the author shows that such an exception would destroy the very praise the verse intends, because it would make every creature a creator of its own acts. Let's read his argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt and the verse's context
The doubt is that the verse 'Creator of everything' should be limited to good actions because evil cannot come from God. The author immediately notes that the verse came in the context of praise (tamadduh).
2
Understand the concept of praise and exclusivity
Praise of God can only be genuine if what is praised is exclusive to Him. If others share in it, the praise diminishes.
3
See the consequence of excluding actions
If we exclude evil acts from God's creation, then according to the opponents, every being with voluntary actions (mosquitoes, dogs, etc.) would be a creator of its own acts, making them equal to God in that respect.
This is the reductio ad absurdum.
4
Grasp the conclusion: ignorance
Trying to preserve the verse by affirming something that negates its intent is extreme ignorance. The argument shows the necessity of affirming that God creates all actions, good and evil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجاب عن هذه الشبهات أن يقال : لا ريب أن الآية خرجت مخرج التمدح ولا شك أن معنى التمدح يحصل بما يختص هو تعالى به ولا يشاركه فيه غيره، ولو خص منه المتنازع فيه لزال هذا المعنى لأن الآية تصير في التقدير: خالق كل شيء هو فعله أو خالق كل شيء ليس بفعل غيره، وعندكم يساويه في هذا المعنى كل ما له الأفعال الاختيارية من البق والبعوض والكلب والخنزير، فإن كل شيء من هذه الأشياء عندكم خالق كل شيء هو فعل ما وليس هو يفعل غيره ولا تمدح الله تعالى بما يساويه فيه كل ما دب ودرج وإن هان وضعف في نفسه، وهذا جهل مفرط بالحقائق، فإن إبقاء ما سيقت له الآية، بإثبات أمر يوجب ثبوته إبطال ما سبقت له الآية والقصد إلى إبقاء الشيء إثبات ما يوجب إبطاله جهل لا یوازيه جهل ولا يخفى فساده على من له أدنى لب.
And it is answered regarding these doubts that it is said: There is no doubt that the verse came in the context of praise, and there is no doubt that the meaning of praise is obtained by what He, exalted, is exclusively characterized by and in which no other shares with Him. And if what is disputed were specified from it, this meaning would cease, because the verse would become in estimation: 'Creator of everything is His own act' or 'Creator of everything is not the act of another'. And according to you, everything that has voluntary actions, from mosquitoes, flies, dogs, and pigs, equals Him in this meaning. For everything among these things, according to you, is a creator of everything that is its own act and not an act of another, and God is not praised by what every creeping and crawling thing, however lowly and weak in itself, equals Him in. This is extreme ignorance of realities. For preserving what the verse was intended for, by affirming a matter whose affirmation necessitates the negation of what the verse was intended for, and the intention to preserve the thing by affirming what necessitates its negation, is an ignorance which no ignorance rivals, and whose corruption is not hidden to anyone with the least discernment.
Source pages p. 860

Commentary
This passage is a response to a doubt raised about the verse 'Creator of everything'. The author argues that the verse is intended as praise (tamadduh) of God, and such praise can only be achieved by something exclusively His, in which no other shares. If one were to exclude the disputed actions (i.e., evil acts) from the verse's scope, the meaning of praise would be lost, because the verse would then imply that God creates only His own acts or that He does not create others' acts. But according to the opponents, every being with voluntary actions—even insects and animals—would equally be 'creator of its own acts', thus negating God's unique praise. The author concludes that this is extreme ignorance, as it attempts to preserve the verse's intent by affirming something that actually undermines it.

آية
تمدح
خالق كل شيء
شبهات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Limiting the verse 'Creator of everything' to only good actions preserves its praise of God.
Correction: Limiting the verse would destroy God's exclusive praise, because it would allow others (creatures) to be creators of their own acts, thereby sharing in the attribute of creatorhood.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The verse's praise of God as Creator of everything is absolute; to exclude any action would negate God's exclusive praise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you attribute your successes or failures to your own effort, are you not, in that moment, robbing God of the exclusive praise due to Him as the Creator of all things? How will you realign your heart to see His hand in every outcome?
?
Does your daily life reflect the verse 'Creator of everything' as absolute, or do you make exceptions for 'your own' actions—your choices, your good deeds, your sins? What would change if you truly believed God created even your smallest act?
?
You confess God is the Creator of everything, yet you often feel shame or pride over your own accomplishments and failures. Is this not a subtle form of shirk in His attribute of creation, as the lowly creatures claim equality? Repent and commit to seeing all as from Him alone.

The Timeless Scope of Quranic Evidence
Nasafi responds to the objection that 'Creator of all things' refers only to bodies, not actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's two arguments that the verse 'Creator of all things' is not limited to bodies but covers all entities, including human actions, and applies to all future disputes.

Core Idea
Quranic verses are timeless and address all future theological issues.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi refutes a common objection against using the verse 'Creator of all things' as evidence for God's creation of actions. The objection claimed the verse only referred to bodies, not actions, because the debate about actions arose later. Nasafi offers two compelling arguments to show the verse's universal and timeless scope.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the first part of the passage where Nasafi states the objection: that the verse is only about bodies, not actions, because the dispute over actions arose later.
Notice the claim: 'Your statement is not sound...'
2
First argument: Historical precedent
Nasafi argues that the dispute over actions already existed before Islam among Jews (the 'Anāniyya) and Christians (jabr), so the verse would cover their views.
3
Second argument: Divine foreknowledge
Even if the dispute hadn't arisen then, God foreknew it and included evidence against it in the Quran.
This emphasizes the comprehensive knowledge of Allah.
4
Conclusion: Timeless relevance
The Quran's clarifications are not limited to the time of revelation but extend to all needs until the end of the world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس يستقيم قولهم إن قوله تعالى : خَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ ورد في الأجسام دون الأعراض، لأن المنازعة في تخليق الأفعال ما كانت ثابتة في زمن النبي عليه السلام بل حدثت بعد ذلك، وإنما الخلاف في ذلك الزمان كان بين الموحدين وبين الثنوية والمجوس والزنادقة في تخليق الأجسام الضارة، فوردت الآية لبيان ذلك لأنا نقول: الخلاف في خلق الأفعال كان في ذلك الزمان وقبل ذلك الزمان، فإن طائفة من اليهود يقال لهم : العنانية كانوا على ما ذهبت إليه المعتزلة، وأكثر النصارى كانت تقول بالجبر ، فإذا هذه دعوة كاذبة، على أنا نقول : هب أن الخلاف في هذه المسألة لم يكن في ذلك الزمان، ولكن نقول : إن الله تعالى لما كان عالما بحدوث مقالتكم الفاسدة المضاهية لأقاويل أولئك الثنوية أقام الدلالة السمعية على بطلان كل من ذلك ما كان من ذلك ثابتا وما سيحدث ما يضاهيه وهو من نتائجه، وليس بيان الكتاب بمقتصر على ما وقع في ذلك الزمان بل تضمن الكتاب بيان ذلك وبيان ما يحتاج إليه ويبتلى به إلى انقراض الدنيا وفنائها.
And their statement is not sound that His saying, the Exalted, 'Creator of everything' came concerning bodies (ajsām) without accidents (a'rāḍ), because the dispute over the creation of acts was not established in the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him, but occurred after that. Rather, the disagreement in that time was between the monotheists and the dualists, the Magians, and the heretics over the creation of harmful bodies. So the verse came to clarify that. For we say: The disagreement over the creation of acts existed in that time and before that time. Indeed, a group of Jews called the 'Anāniyya held the same view as the Mu'tazila, and most Christians held to jabr (compulsion). So this claim is false. Moreover, we say: Grant that the disagreement over this issue did not exist at that time, but we say: Since God, the Exalted, knew of the occurrence of your corrupt opinion that imitates the statements of those dualists, He established the scriptural evidence (al-dalāla al-sam'iyya) for the invalidity of all that—what was established of that and what will occur that imitates it, and it is from its consequences. And the clarification of the Book is not restricted to what occurred in that time, but the Book included clarification of that and clarification of what is needed and will be tested thereby until the end and extinction of the world.
Source pages p. 866

Commentary
This passage responds to the objection that the verse 'Creator of all things' (Quran 6:101 or similar) was revealed only about bodies, not actions, because the dispute over actions arose later. Nasafi first argues that the claim is unsound; he points out that the dispute over actions actually existed in that time and before, citing the Jewish 'Anāniyya sect (who held Mu'tazilite views) and Christian proponents of jabr. He then offers an even stronger argument: even if the dispute had not yet arisen, God foreknew it and established scriptural evidence that covers all future events and their imitations. Therefore, the Quran's clarification is not limited to its immediate context but extends to all times until the end of the world. This shows the comprehensive and timeless relevance of the Quranic text.

Misconception: The verse 'Creator of all things' (Quran 6:101) was only meant to address the dispute about bodies that existed at the time of revelation, and therefore does not apply to human actions or later theological debates.
Correction: Nasafi demonstrates that the dispute about actions already existed before Islam, and even if it had not, God's foreknowledge means the verse encompasses all future related disputes. Thus the verse is universally applicable.

Direct Proof from Quran 37:96
Nasafi presents Quranic evidence that Allah creates both humans and their actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses Quran 37:96 as direct evidence that Allah creates both humans and their actions.

Core Idea
The Quran explicitly states that Allah creates both you and your actions.

Nasafi now presents a clear Quranic proof for the Maturidi position on human acts. The verse from Surah as-Saffat leaves little room for interpretation: Allah is the Creator of both humans and their deeds. This direct citation serves as a powerful counterargument to those who separate human agency from divine creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic sentence carefully, then its literal translation. Notice that Nasafi presents this as an indication ('دل') of the correctness of his school's position.
The Arabic is a single compound sentence ending with the verse.
2
Identify the cited verse
The verse is Quran 37:96: وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ. It appears in the story of Prophet Ibrahim addressing his people about idols.
Context: Ibrahim is arguing against idol worship, stating that Allah creates both them and their actions.
3
Understand the argument
Nasafi uses this verse to prove that human acts are created by Allah. The phrase 'what you do' (ما تعملون) encompasses all human actions. Therefore, acts are part of Allah's creation.
This supports the Maturidi doctrine of kasb (acquisition) where actions are created by Allah but acquired by humans.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Some interpret 'what you do' as referring to idols rather than actions. But the verse's context (Ibrahim speaking to idol worshippers) and parallel verses show it means 'what you do' as acts.
The correct interpretation is essential to uphold the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يدل على صحة ما ذهبنا إليه قوله تعالى: وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ
And among what indicates the correctness of what we hold is His saying, the Exalted: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' (Quran 37:96)
Source pages p. 867

Commentary
This passage provides a direct Quranic proof for the Maturidi position that human acts are created by Allah. The verse (Surah as-Saffat 37:96) explicitly states that Allah creates both humans and their actions ('what you do'). This is presented as a decisive evidence supporting the doctrine that all acts, including those of human beings, are created by God. The verse is clear and needs little interpretation, making it a strong argument against those who deny the creation of human acts.

Key Terms
خلق
ما تعملون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some interpret 'what you do' in the verse as referring to idols (i.e., 'what you make' as in carved idols) rather than general actions.
Correction: The context of the verse—Ibrahim addressing idol worshippers—indeed mentions idols, but the phrase 'ما تعملون' is general for actions. Parallel Quranic usage (e.g., 37:95) uses 'تعملون' in the sense of 'do' or 'make', and the broader argument of the sura supports the creation of human acts.

Key Takeaway

Inconsistency of Opponents in Interpreting Scripture
Nasafi criticizes opponents for contradictory use of Quranic verses to deny creation of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi exposes the contradiction in his opponents' selective use of Quranic verses to deny divine creation of actions.

Core Idea
The Quran refutes all future falsehoods; opponents twist it to suit their pre-existing beliefs.

In this passage, Nasafi defends the eternal relevance of the Quran by asserting that it provides evidence against all false statements, past and future. He then highlights the audacity of his opponents who selectively apply verses to deny the creation of actions while rejecting other verses that clearly affirm it, revealing their arbitrary and contradictory approach to divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the principle of universal Quranic explanation
Nasafi begins by stating that the Quran's explanation is not limited to the time of revelation; it covers all times and all necessary doctrines, including the refutation of future heresies.
This principle undercuts any argument that restricts Quranic verses to their immediate context.
2
Identify the opponents' misuse of specific verses
Nasafi points out that opponents cite verses like 3:78 (condemning those who twist scripture) and 5:103 (declaring certain animal practices not legislated) to deny the creation of actions, even though these verses deal with false claims and legal rulings, not ontology.
3
Recognize the double standard
Nasafi notes that the same opponents reinterpret the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' (37:96) to refer to idols rather than actions, claiming the dispute was about idol worship. This selective application is a clear contradiction.
This reveals their arbitrary imposition (التحكم على الكتاب) on the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة لم يكن في ذلك الزمان، ولكن نقول : إن الله تعالى لما كان عالما بحدوث مقالتكم الفاسدة المضاهية لأقاويل أولئك الثنوية أقام الدلالة السمعية على بطلان كل من ذلك ما كان من ذلك ثابتا وما سيحدث ما يضاهيه وهو من نتائجه، وليس بيان الكتاب بمقتصر على ما وقع في ذلك الزمان بل تضمن الكتاب بيان ذلك وبيان ما يحتاج إليه ويبتلى به إلى انقراض الدنيا وفنائها. والعجب من وقاحتهم حيث يتعلقون في المسألة بقوله : وَإِنَّ مِنْهُمْ لَفَرِيقًا يَلْوُونَ أَلْسِنَتَهُم بِالْكِتَبِ لِتَحْسَبُوهُ مِنَ الْكِتَبِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَيَقُولُونَ هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ وقالوا : نفى أن يكون ليهم ألسنتهم من عند الله، وكذا قوله تعالى: مَا جَعَلَ اللهُ مِنْ بَحِيرَةٍ وَلَا سَائِبَة الآية، ويتعلقون به في نفي خلق الأفعال مع أن الخصوم كانوا يدعون ذلك شرعًا، والآية وردت لبيان أنها ليست بمشروعة من الله تعالى ولا يبالون من صرف الآية إلى أفعال العباد وإن لم تكن المنازعة واقعة في ذلك الزمان في تخليقها، ثم يصرفون الآية التي نتعلق بها نحن إلى غير الأفعال لانعدام المنازعة فيها في ذلك الزمان، وهذا هو عين التناقض وغاية الوقاحة والتحكم على الكتاب بآرائهم الفاسدة - عصمنا الله تعالى عن ذلك.
The issue: It did not exist in that time. But we say: Since Allah Almighty was Knower of the occurrence of your corrupt statement resembling the sayings of those dualists, He established the scriptural evidence for the falsehood of each of that—what was established from that and what will later occur that resembles it and is of its consequences. And the explanation of the Book is not restricted to what occurred in that time; rather, the Book included the explanation of that and the explanation of what is needed and tested by until the end and annihilation of the world. And astonishing is their impudence in that they cling in the issue to His saying: 'Indeed, among them is a party who twist their tongues with the Book so that you may think it from the Book, but it is not from the Book, and they say, 'It is from Allah,' but it is not from Allah.' And they said: He denied that their tongues are from Allah. And likewise His saying: 'Allah has not made a Bahirah or a Sa'ibah'—the verse. And they cling to it to deny the creation of actions, even though the opponents were claiming that as religiously legislated, and the verse was revealed to clarify that they are not legislated from Allah. And they do not care that they turn the verse to the actions of servants—even though the dispute was not occurring in that time about their creation—then they turn the verse that we cling to to other than actions due to the absence of dispute about them in that time. Commentary
This passage is a refutation wherein Nasafi exposes the inconsistency of his opponents (likely Mu'tazila or other rationalists) in interpreting Quranic verses. The passage begins by affirming that the Book (Quran) provides evidence for all times, not just the immediate context of revelation. Then Nasafi expresses astonishment at their impudence: they cite verses like 3:78 (which condemns those who twist scripture) and 5:103 (which declares certain animal practices not legislated) to argue that actions are not created by Allah. However, these verses are about false claims and legal rulings, not about the ontological status of actions. The opponents apply these verses to deny creation of actions even though the original dispute was about legal legislation, not creation. Yet when Nasafi and his school cite the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' (37:96) to prove creation of actions, the opponents divert its meaning to refer to idols (the objects made) instead of actions, claiming the dispute in that time was about idol worship, not creation of actions. Nasafi calls this a clear contradiction and arbitrary imposition on the Book.

الدلالة السمعية
الثنوية
التحكم على الكتاب
التناقض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Opponents think that Quranic verses revealed in specific historical contexts cannot be applied to later theological disputes, or that verses about legal rulings can be directly extrapolated to ontological matters.
Correction: Nasafi argues that the Quran's guidance is universal and that verses must be interpreted according to their intended meaning and context, not selectively to support pre-existing doctrines.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi demonstrates that his opponents' selective and decontextualized use of Quranic verses reveals a fundamental inconsistency in their denial of divine creation of actions.

The Linguistic Proof from Quran 37:96 for Creation of Actions
Nasafi presents the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' as proof and defends its linguistic interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the grammatical rule of 'ma' attached to a verb to prove that Allah creates human actions, and how he defends this interpretation against objections.

Core Idea
Allah created you and what you do – the grammar proves He creates the action itself, not just the product.

Nasafi presents a key Quranic verse as evidence for the Maturidi position on the creation of human actions. Opponents interpret the verse differently, claiming it refers to the objects made (idols). Nasafi relies on a grammatical rule established by Sibawayh to show that the verse speaks of actions, not objects. In this lesson, we will follow his argument verse by verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and Nasafi's claim
Start by reading the verse 'And Allah created you and what you do' and notice how Nasafi immediately explains that 'what you do' means 'your action'. This is his opening claim.
The verse is central to the Maturidi proof for the creation of human acts.
2
Understand the linguistic rule
Nasafi introduces the grammatical principle: when 'ma' is attached to a verb without a resumptive pronoun, the combination expresses the verbal noun (masdar). He gives an example: 'a'jabani ma sana'ta' means 'your making pleased me'.
This rule comes from Sibawayh, the leading grammarian.
3
Examine the objection and parallels
The opponents object that 'ma ta'malun' refers to the product (idols), citing similar verses like 'Do you worship what you carve?' (37:95). Identify how they argue that the verse is about the created objects, not actions.
The objection is plausible at first glance, so it needs a strong rebuttal.
4
Analyze Nasafi's response
Nasafi responds by insisting on the default rule: without the resumptive pronoun (ha'), 'ma' + verb means the action. He also provides a proof from another verse: 'Recompense for what they used to do' – here the recompense is for the deed, not the product.
The final proof clinches the argument by showing that even opponents must accept the action meaning in other contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يدل على صحة ما ذهبنا إليه قوله تعالى: وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ أي وعملكم فإن كلمة ما إذا اتصلت بالفعل صارا عبارة عن المصدر تقول: أعجبني ما صنعت أي صنعك ، والخصوم يعترضون على هذا ويقولون: المراد منه المعمول أي خلقكم ومعمولكم وهي الأصنام المعمولة وهي أجسام ولا خلاف في كونها مخلوقة نظيره قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ وهم ما كانوا يعبدون فعلهم الذي هو النحت بل كانوا يعبدون المنحوت، وكذا قوله: تَلْقَفُ مَا يَأْفِكُونَ . والجواب أن كلمة ما إذا اتصلت بالفعل كان مجموعها عبارة عن المصدر عند الإطلاق هذا هو مذهب سيبويه وإن خالفه الأخفش في ذلك حيث جوز سيبويه أن يقال أعجبني ما قمت أي قيامك، ولو كان ذا عبارة عن المفعول لما جاز ذلك إلا في الفعل المتعدي، والأخفش لا يجوزه إلا في المتعدي، غير أن العارفين بكلام العرب المتبحرين في علم النحو مالوا إلى تصحيح قول سيبويه، وإذا ذكر العائد وهو الهاء فقيل : أعجبني ما صنعته حينئذ تكون عبارة عن المفعول، وفي كل موضع جعل عبارة عن المفعول كان بإضمار الهاء وهو عدول عن ظاهر الكلام بالدليل ولا دليل فمن ادعى قيام الدليل فليبرزوه، والدليل على أنه عند الإطلاق ينصرف إلى ما بينا قوله تعالى : جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ أي بعملهم دون
And among what indicates the correctness of what we have held is His saying: 'And Allah created you and what you do'—that is, and your action. For the word 'ma' when connected to a verb, both together become an expression for the verbal noun (masdar). You say: 'Pleased me what you made'—i.e., your making. And the opponents object to this and say: The intended meaning is the object (ma'mul)—i.e., He created you and your product—which are the idols that are made, and they are bodies; there is no dispute that they are created. The parallel is His saying: 'Do you worship what you carve?' And they used to worship not their action which is carving, but rather they worshipped the carved. And likewise His saying: 'It swallows what they faked.' The answer is that the word 'ma' when connected to a verb, both together become an expression for the verbal noun in unrestricted usage; this is the view of Sibawayh, although Al-Akhfash disagreed with him in that. For Sibawayh permitted saying: 'Pleased me what you stood'—i.e., your standing. And if it were an expression for the object, that would be permissible only in transitive verbs. Al-Akhfash does not permit it except in transitive verbs. However, the experts in Arabic speech, the profound in the science of grammar, inclined to accept Sibawayh's statement. And when the resumptive pronoun, which is the ha', is mentioned, and it is said: 'Pleased me what you made it' then it becomes an expression for the object. And in every place it is made an expression for the object, it is by implication of the ha', and that is a departure from the apparent meaning with a proof; and there is no proof. So whoever claims the existence of a proof, let them produce it. And the proof that in unrestricted usage it refers to what we have explained is His saying: 'Recompense for what they used to do'—i.e., for their action, not
Source pages p. 867

Commentary
This passage is a proof and defense of the interpretation of the Quranic verse 37:96 'Wa-Allahu khalaqakum wa ma ta'malun' (And Allah created you and what you do) as evidence that Allah creates human actions. The author begins by presenting the verse as a proof for his school's position. He explains that the phrase 'ma ta'malun' means 'your action' because the word 'ma' when attached to a verb forms a verbal noun (masdar). He gives a linguistic example: 'a'jabani ma sana'ta' means 'your making pleased me.' Then the objection from opponents is stated: they claim that 'ma ta'malun' means 'what you make' (the product), i.e., the idols that they carved, and that the verse is about the creation of those idols, which are bodies, and there is no dispute that they are created. They support this by citing similar verses like 'Do you worship what you carve?' (37:95) and 'It swallows what they faked' (20:69 or similar), arguing that the worship was of the carved object, not the act of carving. Nasafi then provides the answer: according to the leading grammarian Sibawayh, when 'ma' is connected to a verb without a resumptive pronoun (ha'), the combination expresses the verbal noun (the action), not the object. If it was meant to be the object, a pronoun would be required, as in 'a'jabani ma sana'tahu' (what you made it). Since the verse lacks such a pronoun, the default interpretation is the action. Sibawayh's opinion is preferred by most grammarians. Al-Akhfash disagreed, but the majority side with Sibawayh. The author concludes by offering another proof: in the verse 'Jaza'an bima kanu ya'malun' (Recompense for what they used to do), the phrase 'bima kanu ya'malun' clearly means their action, not the product of their action, because the recompense is for the deed, not the object. Thus, the original interpretation stands.

Key Terms
خلق الأفعال
ما المصدرية
سيبويه
الأخفش
المصدر
المفعول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'ma ta'malun' in 37:96 refers to the objects made (idols), based on similar verses.
Correction: The grammatical rule of 'ma' + verb without a resumptive pronoun indicates the action, not the object, as established by Sibawayh and supported by other verses like 'Jaza'an bima kanu ya'malun'.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does the phrase 'ما تعملون' (ma ta'malun) in Quran 37:96 grammatically refer to?
A) The objects made (idols)
B) The action of the servants
C) Both the action and the object
D) The carvers themselves

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Allah created you and what you do' definitively refers to the creation of human actions according to the grammatical rule that 'ma' + verb without a resumptive pronoun expresses the verbal noun, a rule supported by leading grammarians and other Quranic verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The opponents resisted the plain meaning of the verse to avoid admitting that Allah creates actions. Are there any areas of your life where you resist surrendering the belief that you are the sole agent of your choices? ?

The Consequence of Denying God's Power Over Actions
A reductio ad absurdum argument for God's power over all actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi argument insists that all actions must be within God's power to avoid invalidating the proof for the existence of the Creator.

Core Idea
Without God's power over all actions, the argument for His existence collapses.

This passage presents a crucial logical consequence: if actions could occur without being subject to anyone's power, the entire rational proof for a Creator would be undone. The author forces the opponent to consider the implications of denying God's control over all events.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opponent's claim
The opponent asserts that certain actions are not under the servant's power due to a missing condition, and also not under God's power. Recognize this as the starting point of the argument.
2
Trace the first consequence
The author argues that if actions occur without an agent, they would be self-subsistent. This would logically extend to the entire world being self-subsistent.
3
Identify the second consequence
If the world were self-subsistent, the proof for the existence of the Maker (al-Ṣāniʿ) would be invalidated. This is a direct reductio ad absurdum.
4
Consider the moral implications
Obligation, reward, and punishment become meaningless if actions are outside God's power. The author asks rhetorically: what difference does it make to the servant if the action is under God's power or under no one's power?
5
Conclude the argument
The condition for the servant's creative power is absent, so the opponent's objection fails. The argument supports the Maturidi position that all actions are within God's power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أيضا عن شهادات المعارف، وإن زعموا أن الأفعال من هذه الوجوه ليست بداخله تحت قدرة العبد لانعدام شريطة القدرة وليست بداخله أيضا تحت قدرة الله ولا حاصلة بها، فقد جعلوا حصول الفعل من هذه الوجوه بذاته من غير حاجة إلى مع كونه حدثًا، ولو جاز ذا في الفعل لجاز في جميع المعالم، ولو جاز ذا في جميع العالم لبطلت الدلالة على ثبوت الصانع مع أن التكليف بهذا الفعل، والثواب والعقاب عليه لما جاز ولم يقبح مع أنه من هذه الوجوه غير داخل تحت قدرته لماذا لم يجز لو كان الفعل من هذه الوجوه داخلاً تحت قدرة الله تعالى؟ فأي فرق في حق العبد بين أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه داخلاً تحت قدرة الله تعالى وبين أن لا يكون داخلاً تحت قدرة أحد إذا كان خارجا عن قدرته من هذه الوجوه؟ فإذا تقرر بما ذكرنا ما ادعينا من انعدام شريطة ثبوت قدرة التخليق للعبد والله الموفق.
Also from the testimonies of [rational] cognitions: if they claim that actions in these respects are not included under the servant's power due to the absence of the condition of power, and they are also not included under God's power nor occur by it, then they have made the occurrence of the action in these respects by itself without need for an agent despite being an event. And if this were permissible for the action, it would be permissible for all [parts of] the world, and if it were permissible for all the world, the proof for the existence of the Maker would be invalidated. Moreover, the obligation (taklīf) with this action, and the reward and punishment for it, would not be permissible and would not be considered evil [i.e., would be unreasonable] even though in these respects it is not under His power. Why would it not be permissible if the action in these respects were under the power of God Most High? What difference is there for the servant between the action being in these respects under God’s power and its not being under anyone’s power if it is outside his power in these respects? When it is established, through what we have mentioned, what we claimed concerning the absence of the condition for the servant’s possession of the power of creation (qudrat al-takhlīq). And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 877

Commentary
This passage is a concluding argument against those who claim that actions in certain respects are not under the servant's power (due to missing condition) and also not under God's power, thereby implying they occur without a creator. The author shows the absurd consequences: if such self-subsistent actions were possible, then the entire world could be self-subsistent, which would invalidate the proof for the existence of the Maker (al-Ṣāniʿ). Moreover, moral obligation (taklīf), reward, and punishment would become meaningless if the action were not within God's power, because then it would be impossible to hold anyone accountable. The author asks rhetorically: what difference does it make to the servant whether the action is under God's power or under no one's power? The conclusion is that the condition (sharīṭa) for the servant's possession of creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq) is absent, and thus the argument against the servant's power is established.

قدرة التخليق
ثبوت الصانع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument denies all human capacity for action.
Correction: It specifically targets the capacity to create (ikhtirāʿ) from nothing, not the acquired capacity (kasb) affirmed by the Maturidi school.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, if an action could occur without being under the power of either the servant or God, what would be invalidated?
A) The concept of human free will
B) The proof for the existence of the Maker
C) The reality of the action itself
D) The servant's ability to acquire actions

Key Takeaway
All actions must ultimately be under God's power; otherwise the rational proof for His existence is undermined.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

If the proof for God's existence collapses when we deny His power over actions, then your very conviction in God's existence depends on acknowledging His control. Have you ever felt that your actions are 'your own' in a way that excludes God? How can you cultivate a constant awareness that all power belongs to Him alone?

Proof from Contrary Outcomes
Nasafi proves evil outcomes require a creator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi argues that actions occurring contrary to the agent's will prove the existence of a divine creator.

Core Idea
When actions go against our will, they reveal a greater Will behind them.

This lesson presents a philosophical argument from experience: we often intend good but outcomes are evil. Nasafi uses this to prove that there must be an external creator who brings about the actual quality. This argument, known as the 'proof from contrary outcomes', is a cornerstone of Maturidi theology.

Guided Path
1
Observe the empirical evidence
Read how continuous walking leads to pain, unintended. This shows that actions can have qualities opposite to what the agent intended.
Nasafi uses simple physical examples to ground his argument.
2
Apply to the case of disbelief
The disbeliever intends his disbelief as good and obedience, but it is actually evil and opposed to wisdom. This confirms the pattern.
3
Analyze the trilemma
Three possibilities are considered for the cause of the evil quality: the agent himself, the action itself, or another freely chosen agent. Only the third is coherent.
The first two lead to absurd consequences (naturalism/astral determinism or self-causation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويباشر ذلك بجوارحه يريد حصول ذلك كله على صفة الحسن دون القبيح ومعلوم دون أن حصول ذلك على ما يضاد الحسن وهو القبح لا على الحسن الذي قصده. وأما ما يعرف ذلك فيه بالحس فإن الإنسان يتأذى بالمشي الدائم ويتألم بالقيام الممتد اللازم، وكذا بكل فعل ثابر المرء على اكتسابه وواظب على ارتكابه، ولا شك أن الفعل لا يقصد إليه الفاعل ليتألم به ويتأذى، ومع هذا حصل مؤذيًا متعبًا فصح ما ادعينا من خروج الفعل على ضد ما يقصده العبد من الوصف ما لم يقصده، فإذا لم يوجد على ذلك دل أن له موجد خرج الموجود على ما أراده. يحقق هذا أن خروج الكفر وعبادة الصنم على ما يقصده الكافر من الحسن وصوابًا وطاعة الله تعالى يتقرب بها إليه يضاد الحكمة وينافيها، وخروجه على ما خرج عليه من القبح مما يقتضيه التدبير الصائب والحكمة البالغة. وجوده على هذا الوصف وإن لم يقصده الكافر إما إن كان بالكافر أم بالفعل نفسه بموجب مختار تولى إيجاده عليه، فإن كان بالكافر أوجب ذا جواز حصول جميع الأفعال الحكمية ممن لا يقصد تحيلها، وذا يؤدي إلى القول بالطبائع والنجوم وهو فاسد على أن فساد ذلك متقرر في البداهة وإن لم يؤد ذلك إلى مذهب باطل. وإن كان بالفعل نفسه أوجب ذلك جواز وجود جميع الأفعال الحكمية من السماوات والأرضين بلا موجد قصد إيجادها وتحصيلها، وذا محال. وإن كان بفاعل مختار تولى إيجاده على ما هو عليه من الوصف لصح ما ذهبنا إليه.
He pursues that with his limbs, meaning all that occurs with the attribute of good without evil. It is known without that its occurrence in what contradicts good, which is evil, not in the good that he intended. As for what is known by sense: a person is harmed by continuous walking and pained by prolonged standing, and likewise every action a person persists in acquiring and continues in committing. There is no doubt that the agent does not intend the action to be pained and harmed by it, yet it occurs harmful and tiring. So our claim is proven that the action emerges opposite to what the servant intended of the description, without him intending it. When it is not found accordingly, it indicates that it has an originator who brings about the existent according to His will. This is confirmed by the fact that the emergence of disbelief and idol worship upon what the disbeliever intends of good, correctness, and obedience to God thereby, contradicts wisdom and is incompatible with it, while its emergence upon what it emerges of evil is required by sound management and perfect wisdom. Its existence on this description, even though the disbeliever did not intend it, is either from the disbeliever or from the action itself by a freely chosen agent who undertakes its origination. If it is from the disbeliever, it necessitates the possibility of all voluntary actions occurring from one who does not intend their change, and this leads to the doctrine of natures and stars, which is invalid, and its invalidity is established in immediate intuition even if it does not lead to a false doctrine. If it is from the action itself, it necessitates the possibility of all voluntary actions occurring from the heavens and earths without an originator who intends their existence and acquisition, and that is impossible. If it is from a freely chosen agent who undertakes its origination upon what it is of description, then what we have held is correct.
Source pages p. 879

Commentary
This passage is a proof (istidlāl) that human actions which occur contrary to the agent's intention must have an external cause, namely God. Nasafi begins by stating the empirical observation: a person walking continuously experiences harm and pain, even though they did not intend harm. This shows that the action has taken on a quality opposite to what was intended. From this he concludes that there must be an originator (mūjid) who brings about the action with that quality. He then applies this to the case of disbelief (kufr) and idol worship: the disbeliever intends these acts to be good and pleasing to God, but they are actually evil and opposed to wisdom. The evil quality must come from an external cause. He then analyzes three possibilities: (1) the cause is the disbeliever himself, (2) the cause is the action itself, (3) the cause is another freely chosen agent (fāʿil mukhtār). The first leads to absurd consequences, like the possibility of all voluntary actions occurring without intention, which implies naturalism or astral determinism, both invalid. The second leads to the absurdity of things causing themselves. The third alone is coherent, and that is the position of the Ahl al-Sunnah, that God is the creator of all actions, including their qualities.

موجد
فاعل مختار
طبائع

Correction: Nasafi proves they require an external creator, not accident or self-causation.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does the occurrence of an action with a quality opposite to the agent's intention prove?
A) The agent is ignorant
B) There is another creator
C) The action is self-caused
D) The agent is forced

Key Takeaway
Evil outcomes contrary to intention point to a divine creator who brings about the actual quality.

You may have good intentions when you speak or act, but sometimes the result is harmful or sinful. Will you now examine your actions more carefully, knowing that their actual quality is from God, and ask yourself: what is He teaching you through that outcome?
?

The Dilemma of Divine Freedom and Coercion
Author presents a logical dilemma forcing the opponent into absurdity or blasphemy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma that undermines the Mu'tazili position on the creation of acts and their moral qualities.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazili split of act and ugliness leads to an impossible dilemma.

The author now presents a forced argument (ilzām) that traps the Mu'tazila between two unacceptable alternatives. By assuming their own framework, he shows that their position leads either to an absurdity—an act of disbelief without its essential ugliness—or to blasphemy by implying God is under coercion. This dilemma highlights a key weakness in their theory of divine and human agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: 'if... then... either... or...'.
The dilemma is a classic ilzām (binding argument).
2
Identify the two horns
Identify the two options: God is free or compelled. Understand the consequence of each.
3
Analyze the first horn
If God is free, He could refrain from creating ugliness, leading to an act without ugliness—impossible.
This contradicts the opponent's own view that ugliness is essential.
4
Analyze the second horn
If God is compelled, He is under coercion, which is blasphemy.
This implies divine impotence (i'jāz).
5
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider how this refutes the Mu'tazili view without assuming the opponent's framework.
The argument uses the opponent's own premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنا نلزمكم فنقول : لو كان العبد أوجده من حيث إنه فعل والله تعالى أوجده من حيث إنه قبح كما تزعمون للزم أحد أمرين كل واحد منهما محال. وبيانه أن العبد إذا قصد تحصيل الكفر فأوجده إما أن يكون الله تعالى مختارًا من إيجاده من حيث إنه قبح أو مضطر إلى ذلك؟
فإن قالوا: هو مختار نقول : كأن من الجائز أن يمتنع عن إيجاده من حيث إنه قبح فيوجد الكفر بدون صفة القبح وهو محال.
وإن قالوا: هو مضطر في إيجاده فهو كفر لما فيه من دعوى المعجز على الله تعالى وإدخاله تحت قدرة الغير وقهره.
Moreover, we constrain you and say: If the servant created it in terms of being an act and God created it in terms of being ugly as you claim, then one of two things necessarily follows, each impossible. Its explanation: When the servant intends to achieve disbelief and creates it, either God is free in creating it in terms of being ugly or compelled to do so. If they say: He is free, we say: Then it is possible that He could refrain from creating it in terms of being ugly, so disbelief would exist without the attribute of ugliness, which is impossible. If they say: He is compelled in creating it, then that is disbelief because it implies imposing incapacity (i'jāz) on God and bringing Him under the power and coercion of another.
Source pages p. 881

Commentary
This passage is a further argument (ilzām) that forces the Mu'tazila into an impossible dilemma. The author assumes their position that the servant creates the act itself while God creates its ugliness. Then he asks: When the servant creates disbelief, is God free to create the ugliness or compelled? If God is free, He could choose not to create the ugliness, which would mean an act of disbelief exists without being ugly—an absurd impossibility. If God is compelled to create the ugliness, then God is under coercion, which is blasphemy (kufr) because it implies that God is forced by another, which is a form of incapacity and subjection. Thus, either horn is unacceptable, refuting the Mu'tazili view.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God being free to create ugliness is a valid option that avoids contradiction.
Correction: If God is free, then He could choose not to create ugliness, which would mean an act of disbelief exists without ugliness—an impossibility given the opponent's own assumption that ugliness is essential to disbelief.

Checkpoint

B) Disbelief could exist without ugliness

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili separation of act and moral quality leads to an inescapable dilemma: either disbelief exists without ugliness or God is coerced—both impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that God was compelled to allow your sin, as if He had no choice? This lesson shows that such a thought is actually disbelief. Do you truly believe God is completely free in every action, even when you fall into sin? How will you remind yourself of this the next time you sin?
?
If the Mu'tazili view is false, then God creates both the act and its ugliness. Does that make you question His justice? The dilemma forces you to accept that either disbelief exists without ugliness (impossible) or God is coerced (blasphemy). So you must accept God's full control. Are you willing to submit to that without reservation? What part of you resists?
?
The author calls the second horn 'disbelief' because it implies incapacity on God. Have you ever, in moments of frustration, blamed God for your bad choices as if He was forced to create them? Confront that thought now: Can you say with certainty that God is free and you alone are responsible for your actions? Make a firm intention to reject any notion that God is under compulsion.

The Impossibilities of Creaturely Creative Power
The author enumerates six impossibilities and explains the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six impossible consequences that follow from attributing creative power to any creature, and how the first impossibility is argued.

Core Idea
Attributing creative power to creatures leads to logical absurdities that undermine God's unity and power.

In this passage, the author presents a crucial argument for divine uniqueness: if any being other than God could create, it would lead to a cascade of impossibilities. He enumerates six and begins to unpack the first—a demonstration of why such a claim is rationally untenable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Notice the author's structure: a claim, a list, then an explanation.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the six impossibilities
The author lists six 'kinds of the impossible.' Find each one and note how they relate to tawhid.
They start with 'منها:' clauses.
3
Focus on the first impossibility
The author begins to explain the first impossibility involving conflicting acts in the same locus. Understand the logical argument.
This shows why two independent creators cannot coexist.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how this passage defends God's exclusive creativity and why it is central to Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث: إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تؤدي إلى مجموعة من المحالات وأما دعوانا أن إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى يؤدي إلى المحال فدعوى صحيحة، وعند الكشف عن ذلك تبين أن ذلك يؤدي إلى ضروب من المحال منها: أنه يؤدي إلى القول بتعجيز الله تعالى أو كونه ممنوعًا. ومنها: أنه يؤدي إلى إبطال دلائل الموحدين على توحيد الصانع وتعجيز الموحدين عن إثبات وحدانية الصانع جل وعلا ومنها : أن وجود محدث لم يوجده الله تعالى ولم يكن له عليه القدرة يؤدي إلى كون العالم بصانعين ومنها : أنه يؤدي إلى أن تكون القدرة من صفات الفعل على مذاهب الخصوم، ويلزم على ذلك أنه لم يكن في الأزل قادرًا عندهم ومنها أنه يؤدي إلى وقوع التشابه بين فعل القديم والمحدث، ومنها: أنه يؤدي إلى جواز عبادة الله تعالى. ونبين كيفية كون كل من ذلك مؤديا إلى كل وجه من هذه الوجوه بعون الله وتوفيقه. أما الأول فإنا قلنا: إن ذلك يؤدي إلى تعجيز الباري جل وعلا فإن الباري لو كان قادرا على أن يخلق مثلاً في يد العبد حركة ، والعبد قادر على أن يخلق فيه سكونًا ثم من المحال أن يوجد مقدور كل واحد منهما في المحل في وقت واحد
Third: Establishing creative power for other than God leads to a group of impossibilities. As for our claim that establishing creative power for other than God Almighty leads to the impossible, it is a valid claim. Upon uncovering that, it becomes clear that it leads to kinds of the impossible, among them: that it leads to the claim of declaring God Almighty incapable or that He is prevented. Among them: that it leads to invalidating the proofs of the monotheists concerning the oneness of the Maker and incapacitating the monotheists from establishing the oneness of the Maker, glorified and exalted. Among them: that the existence of an originated thing that God Almighty did not bring into existence and over which He had no power leads to the world having two makers. Among them: that it leads to power being among the attributes of action according to the doctrines of the opponents, and it follows from that that He was not powerful in pre-eternity according to them. Among them: that it leads to the occurrence of similarity between the act of the Eternal and the originated. Among them: that it leads to the permissibility of worshipping other than God Almighty. And we will clarify how each of these leads to each of these aspects with the help of God and His granting of success. As for the first: we said that it leads to declaring the Creator incapable, for if the Creator was able to create, for example, a motion in the servant's hand, and the servant is able to create a rest in it, then it is impossible that both of their empowered acts exist in the same locus at the same time.
Source pages p. 882

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the impossible consequences that follow from attributing creative power (takhlīq) to any being other than God. The author first asserts the claim and then lists six kinds of impossibilities: (1) declaring God incapable or prevented; (2) invalidating the proofs of tawḥīd and incapacitating the monotheists from proving God's oneness; (3) leading to the existence of an originated thing not created by God, implying two creators; (4) making power an attribute of action, which would mean God was not powerful in pre-eternity according to the opponents' own doctrine; (5) causing similarity between the act of the Eternal and the originated; (6) allowing the worship of other than God. The author then begins to explain the first impossibility: if both God and the servant have creative power, and they create opposite acts in the same locus (e.g., motion and rest), both acts cannot coexist, so one must be impossible, implying incapacity for either. This demonstrates the impossibility of creaturely creative power.

Key Terms
قدرة التخليق
تعجيز
وحدانية
صفات الفعل
تشابه
محال
صانع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the argument denies any form of secondary causality or human agency.
Correction: In fact, it only denies independent creative power ex nihilo, not the ordinary causation we observe.

Checkpoint
How many kinds of impossibilities does the author initially list from attributing creative power to other than God?
A) Four
B) Five
C) Six
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Attributing creative power to any creature leads to multiple logical contradictions that uphold the necessity of God's unique creative power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

If you truly believe that only God has the power to create, why do you still feel anxious about events that are out of your control? Are you attributing power to yourself or others that belongs only to Him? This week, identify one worry you habitually carry and consciously affirm, 'Only God creates its outcome.'
?
When you succeed at something, do you ever think 'I did it' without immediately acknowledging that God created that success? The first impossibility of this lesson shows that claiming creaturely power logically leads to declaring God incapable. Examine your heart: in what area of your life are you most tempted to claim independent effectiveness, and how will you repent of that today?

Incapacitating God and the Threat to Tawhid
A brief argument that a view incapacitating God leads to multiple creators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the view that God can be incapacitated by others contradicts the concept of tawhid and logically implies the possibility of multiple creators.

Core Idea
Allowing God to be incapacitated destroys the basis for monotheism.

This short but potent argument from Imam al-Nasafi demonstrates the theological danger of any view that attributes weakness to Allah. The author connects the dots between incapacity and the very idea of multiple gods, showing that if one creator can be rendered weak without losing his status as creator, then the door is opened to polytheism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the concise logical structure.
This is a summary argument; the author references a fuller discussion elsewhere.
2
Identify the key claim
The author states that incapacitating God nullifies the proofs of monotheism.
3
Trace the logical implication
If God can be incapacitated, then multiple creators become possible. Understand why this follows.
The conditional structure: if incapacitation is allowed without nullifying lordship, then multiple creators are possible.
4
Reflect on the broader context
Consider that this argument is part of a larger discussion on proving God's oneness.
The author refers to earlier sections for a fuller treatment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قلنا: إنه يؤدي إلى إبطال دلائل الموحدين، لأنه يؤدي إلى تعجيز الباري على ما بينا، ولو جاز أن يكون الباري جل وعلا عاجزا بتعجيز الغير إياه ولا تبطل ربوبيته لجاز أن يكون للعالم صانعان وأكثر، وإن كان البعض يعجز بعضا، وقد قررنا هذا الفصل على الاستقصاء في مسألة إثبات وحدانية القديم جل جلاله فلا نعيدها هاهنا.
And we only said: It leads to nullifying the proofs of the monotheists, because it leads to incapacitating the Creator (al-Bāri') as we have shown. And if it were permissible for the Creator, exalted and majestic, to be incapacitated by the incapacitation of another without His lordship being invalidated, then it would be permissible for the world to have two or more creators, even if some incapacitate others. And we have fully established this chapter in the issue of proving the Oneness of the Eternal, exalted His majesty, so we do not repeat it here.
Source pages p. 888

Commentary
This passage is a concise argument against a view (likely that of the Mu'tazila) that implies God can be incapacitated by others. The author states that such a view nullifies the proofs of monotheism because it allows for multiple creators. He references a previous detailed discussion and does not repeat it. The core logic: if God can be incapacitated without losing lordship, then two or more creators could exist even if they partially incapacitate each other, which undermines the fundamental Islamic belief in the oneness of God.

Why Denying Allah's Creation of Accidents Destroys All Proofs
Author argues that denying divine creation of accidents destroys proofs of creation and prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying that Allah creates accidents logically undermines both the proof of the world's temporal origination and the prophetic miracles as evidence of truthfulness.

Core Idea
Accidents are the linchpin; without Allah creating them, proofs for God and Prophet fail.

This passage presents a powerful reductio ad absurdum. The author shows that anyone who denies that Allah directly creates accidents must face a catastrophic consequence: the very proofs for Allah's existence and the Prophet's truthfulness become impossible. Understanding this argument is crucial for grasping the Maturidi insistence on Allah's continuous creative act.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage once silently, then again aloud. Let the logical flow sink in before you analyse it.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two consequences
Notice that the author draws two separate but connected consequences: one about the proof of the world's creation, and one about the proof of prophethood through miracles.
Both depend on the same premise: accidents are created by Allah.
3
Reflect on the conclusion 'kufr'
Consider why the author calls such a view disbelief (kufr). It's not just a theological error but a fundamental failure to recognize Allah's role as the sole Creator of all things, including accidents.
This shows the high stakes of this debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم العلم بحدوث الأجسام يحصل بمعرفة حدوث الأعراض، والأعراض ليست بمخلوقة الله فلم يكن الله تعالى مثبتاً دلالة حدوث العالم ولا قادراً على إثباته. وإنما أثبت ذلك غيره وهو الأجسام، وكذلك ما أثبت الرسول دلالة الصدق إذ ما يثبت في العصا من الجيئة والذهاب، وفي اليد من النور، وفي الماء من الانفلاق، وفي الميت من الحياة، وفي الأكمة والأبرص من البرء، وفي الخشب من الحنين، وفي الشاه المسمومة من الكلام كل ذلك أعراض لا صنع الله تعالى فيها، والقول به كفر.
Then, knowledge of the temporal origination of bodies is attained by knowledge of the temporal origination of accidents, and if accidents are not created by Allah, then Allah Almighty would not have established the proof of the world's temporal origination, nor would He be able to prove it. Rather, something else established that—namely, the bodies. Similarly, the Messenger did not establish the proof of truthfulness, for what manifests in the staff of coming and going, in the hand of light, in the water of splitting, in the dead of life, in the blind and leper of healing, in the wood of yearning, and in the poisoned sheep of speech—all of these are accidents in which Allah Almighty has no creative act, and holding such a view is disbelief.
Source pages p. 890

Commentary
This passage is a logical argument demonstrating the necessary consequence of denying that Allah creates accidents. The author first states the known fact: knowledge of the temporal origination (ḥudūth) of bodies depends on knowledge of the temporal origination of accidents. If accidents are not created by Allah, then Allah Himself would not be the one who established the proof of the world's creation; instead, something else (the bodies) would have established it—a clear absurdity. Then the author applies this to the miracles of the Prophet: the staff's movement, the hand's light, the sea's splitting, the revival of the dead, healing of the blind and leper, the wood's yearning, and the poisoned sheep's speech are all accidents. If these are not created by Allah, they cannot serve as proofs of the Prophet's truthfulness. The author concludes that holding such a view amounts to disbelief (kufr).

Key Terms
حدوث الأجسام
حدوث الأعراض
دلالة حدوث العالم
الرسول
دلالة الصدق
أعراض
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument only concerns physical creation and has nothing to do with epistemology or prophethood.
Correction: The argument actually focuses on the epistemological dependence of proofs upon divine creation of accidents. If Allah does not create accidents, then neither the proof of the world's creation nor the proof of prophethood can be established.

Checkpoint

A) The proof of the world's creation becomes stronger because bodies prove it.
B) Allah would have no role in proving the world's creation, rendering the proof defective.
C) Miracles would still prove prophethood because they are visible.
D) Only the Magians would be affected by this view.

Key Takeaway
Denying that Allah creates accidents destroys the rational proofs for both the world's creation and the Prophet's truthfulness, making such a denial tantamount to disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The author says that if accidents are not created by Allah, then the very proofs for His existence would be attributed to something else.
