The passage lists miracles—the staff moving, the sea splitting. If you were to deny that Allah created those events, you would be denying the proof of prophethood. Do you truly believe that every single event, even the smallest in your day, is created directly by Allah? Or do you unconsciously assume some things happen by themselves? What would change in your worldview if you lived with full awareness that Allah creates every accident?

The Limitation of Wahm in Perceiving the Creator
Explains the incapacity of wahm to grasp the Creator and the need for rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why wahm (imagination) cannot grasp the Creator and why rational proof is essential for affirming His existence.

Core Idea
The Creator is real but not imaginable—proof, not imagination, leads to Him.

This passage tackles a key epistemological challenge in theology: can our imagination (wahm) help us understand the Creator? Imam al-Nasafi argues it cannot, because the Creator is beyond the categories that wahm can picture. He warns that relying on wahm leads to denial of the Creator and urges us to use rational proof instead.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how the author links the limitation of wahm to the denial of the Creator.
2
Identify what wahm cannot grasp
Look for the list of things wahm cannot conceptualize: spirit, intellect, and especially the Creator who is not a substance, body, accident, etc.
This list highlights the boundaries of imagination.
3
Understand the consequence of relying on wahm
See what happens if someone insists on using wahm for knowledge of the Creator: denial of His existence.
The author says the first thing that follows is denial.
4
Grasp the role of proof
Note the alternative: one who affirms the Creator through proof (dalīl) must accept other rational proofs even if not imaginable.
This establishes the primacy of reason over imagination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محيط بثبوت الروح في البدن ووجود العقل فيه، وإن كان لا يتقرر في الوهم معنى تحيا به هذه الأعضاء ولا معنى يوقف به على ما غاب عن الحواس من حقائق الأشياء لخروجه عن الحواس، وقد مر أن من رام أن يعرف بالوهم ما سبيل معرفته العقل فقد حاد عن الطريق، ومن يتبع الوهم ولم يفقد الدليل فيما يجره إلى معرفته لخروجه عن الوهم، فأول ما يلزمه إنكاره ثبوت الصانع إذ لا تصور في الوهم لما ليس بجوهر ولا جسم ولا عرض ولا قائم بنا ولا بجهة من الجهات منا ولا اتصال له بنا ولا انفصال له عنا، ويلزمه أن يخرج ثبوت الصانع عن العقل لخروجه عن الوهم، ويقول إنه ليس ثبوته بمعقول لما أنه ليس بموهوم، فمن أقر بثبوت الصانع اتباعًا للدليل وإن لم يتقرر ذلك في الوهم يلزمه الإقرار بما بينا من الدليل وإن لم يتصور ذلك في الوهم.
It encompasses the establishment of the spirit in the body and the existence of the intellect in it, even though there is not established in wahm (imagination) a meaning by which these limbs live, nor a meaning by which one perceives what is hidden from the senses of the realities of things, because it [wahm] is beyond the senses. It has already passed that whoever seeks to know by wahm that whose way of knowledge is the intellect has deviated from the path. And whoever follows wahm and does not lose the proof (dalīl) in what it [wahm] drags him to know, because it is beyond wahm, then the first thing that necessarily follows is his denial of the existence of the Maker (al-Ṣāniʿ), for there is no conceptualization in wahm for that which is not a substance (jawhar), nor a body (jism), nor an accident (ʿaraḍ), nor subsisting in us, nor in any direction from us, nor having connection with us, nor separation from us. And he is forced to remove the existence of the Maker from the intellect because of its removal from wahm, and he says that its existence is not intelligible (maʿqūl) because it is not imaginable (mawhūm). So whoever affirms the existence of the Maker in following the proof, even if that is not established in wahm, he must affirm what we have explained of the proof, even if that is not conceptualized in wahm.
Source pages p. 901

Commentary
This passage discusses the epistemological limitation of wahm (imagination) in grasping certain realities, specifically the existence of the Creator. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, begins by noting that wahm cannot perceive the spirit or the intellect, as these are beyond sensory experience. He then states that anyone who tries to know through wahm what should be known through the intellect has deviated from the correct path. Following wahm leads to denying the Creator, because wahm cannot conceptualize anything that is not a substance, body, accident, or spatially related to us. Consequently, such a person would also deny that the Creator's existence is rationally known, since it is not imaginable. The author concludes that one who affirms the Creator on the basis of proof (dalīl), even if wahm cannot grasp it, must also accept other rational proofs that may not be imaginable. The passage thus establishes the primacy of rational proof over imagination in theology.

Key Terms
وهم (wahm)
دليل (dalīl)
صانع (Ṣāniʿ)
عقل (ʿaql)
جوهر (jawhar)
جسم (jism)
عرض (ʿaraḍ)
معقول (maʿqūl)
موهوم (mawhūm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Everything real must be imaginable (capable of being pictured in the mind).
Correction: The passage clarifies that the Creator is real but not imaginable; rational proof is required to affirm His existence.

Checkpoint
What does the author identify as the first consequence of relying solely on wahm (imagination) for knowledge of the Creator?
A) It leads to affirming the Creator incorrectly.
B) It leads to denying the existence of the Creator.
C) It leads to confusion about the attributes of the Creator.
D) It leads to asserting that the Creator is a substance.

Key Takeaway
Wahm cannot perceive the Creator; only rational proof can lead to affirming His existence.

Divine Wisdom in Creating Evil Actions
Nasafi defends God's creation of evil actions as wise by appealing to praiseworthy consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi defends God's creation of evil actions as wise by appealing to praiseworthy consequences and the nature of disbelief.

Core Idea
God's creation of evil is wise because it serves His knowledge and justice, not because evil is good.

In this passage, Nasafi tackles a challenging theological question: If God is all-wise, why does He create evil actions like disbelief? He argues that the wisdom lies not in the evil act itself but in the overall outcome—the realization of God's foreknowledge and His just punishment. Nasafi also clarifies that we do not say God created disbelief absolutely; rather, disbelief is inherently evil, and God creates it as such, which is exactly what wisdom requires.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument.
Notice the phrase 'ومنها' indicating this is one of many points.
2
Identify the main argument
Find the sentence where Nasafi states that God's creation of evil in the disbeliever achieves His knowledge and justice. This is the core of his defense.
Look for the word 'موجدًا' which introduces the consequence.
3
Understand the analogy with foul bodies
Nasafi compares creating evil actions to creating foul bodies. Both can have praiseworthy consequences. Think about how a foul body might serve a good purpose.
This analogy helps show that intrinsic foulness doesn't negate wisdom.
4
Analyze the clarification about disbelief
Nasafi insists we do not say God created disbelief absolutely. Instead, the creation of disbelief as evil is wise. Contrast this with the disbeliever who intends it as good.
This nuance is crucial: God's creation of evil is not approval of evil.
5
Reflect on the overall lesson
Consider how this argument defends God's wisdom without denying the reality of evil. Ask yourself how this fits into broader Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : أنه تعالى لما علم أن بعض عباده يعصونه فيما يأمرهم ويكفرون نعمه، وأنه يعذبهم في النار ويملأ منهم جهنم، كان تعالى بتخليقه ذلك فيهم عند اختيارهم لأنفسهم ذلك، موجدًا ما فيه تحقيق علمه وتقرير عدله عند تعذيبه إياهم عليه، وهذه عاقبة للفعل حميدة ()، ثم كان إيجاد ما خبث من الأجسام حكمة لما تعلقت بها عاقبة حميدة، فكذا إيجاد ما قبح من الأفعال. على أنا لا (۲) نقول على الإطلاق أنه خلق الكفر بل نقول بأن خلق الكفر قبيحًا باطلاً شرا فاسدًا، والحكمة تقتضي كون الكفر على هذه الصفات، فمن أوجده على ما تقتضي الحكمة وجوده عليه كان حكيمًا، وإنما كان سفيها من يقصد تحصيلها حكمةً حسنًا صوابًا كما يقصده الكافر إذ الحكمة تقتضى كونه (۳) على ما يضاد هذه الأوصاف فكان الله تعالى بإيجاده على هذه الصفات حكيماً ، والكافر باكتسابه قاصد تلك الصفات سفيها كمن علمه على ما هو عليه من الصفات من القبح والبطلان وغير ذلك كان عالما به، ومن يعلمه على ما يقصده الكافر من الصفات كان جاهلاً به، فكذا في الحكمة والسفه.
And among them: that He, exalted, when He knew that some of His servants disobey Him in what He commands them and disbelieve in His blessings, and that He will punish them in the Fire and fill Hell with them, He, exalted, by creating that in them at the time of their choice of that for themselves, brings into existence that in which is the realization of His knowledge and the establishment of His justice when He punishes them for it. And this is a praiseworthy consequence for the act. Then, the bringing into existence of what is foul among bodies was wisdom due to the praiseworthy consequence attached to it, so likewise the bringing into existence of what is evil among actions. However, we do not absolutely say that He created disbelief, but we say that the creation of disbelief is evil, false, harmful, corrupt, and wisdom requires that disbelief be upon these attributes. So whoever brings it into existence as wisdom requires its existence to be is wise. And only the one who intends to acquire it as good, sound, and wise—as the disbeliever intends—is foolish, since wisdom requires it to be contrary to these attributes. Thus God, by bringing it into existence upon these attributes, is wise, and the disbeliever, by his acquisition intending those attributes, is foolish. It is like one who knows it as it is in terms of attributes—evil, false, etc.—is knowledgeable of it, and one who knows it as the disbeliever intends it to be is ignorant of it. And similarly in wisdom and foolishness.
Source pages p. 930

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God's creation of evil actions is wise. Nasafi argues that because God foreknows that some will disobey and disbelieve, and He will justly punish them, the creation of those evil acts in them at the moment of their choice achieves His knowledge and justice. This praiseworthy consequence makes the creation wise, just as creating foul bodies can be wise due to a good outcome. However, Nasafi clarifies that we do not say God created disbelief absolutely; rather, disbelief is evil and false by nature, and wisdom requires it to be so. The one who brings it into existence as wisdom requires (i.e., as evil) is wise, while the one who intends it as good (i.e., the disbeliever) is foolish. He draws an analogy: knowing something as it truly is (evil) is knowledge, while knowing it as the disbeliever wishes it to be (good) is ignorance. Thus, God is wise in creating evil as evil, and the disbeliever is foolish in pursuing it.

Key Terms
خلق الكفر
الحكمة
السفه
العاقبة الحميدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's creation of evil implies He is evil or foolish.
Correction: God's creation of evil is wise because it realizes His knowledge and justice, and He creates evil as it truly is – evil – which is exactly what wisdom requires.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why is God's creation of evil actions wise?
A) Because evil actions are actually good when performed by God.
B) Because it achieves God's knowledge and justice, leading to a praiseworthy consequence.
C) Because God does not actually create evil; it is only attributed to Him metaphorically.
D) Because evil actions are necessary for the world to exist.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi defends God's wisdom in creating evil by arguing that the praiseworthy consequence (realizing His knowledge and justice) and the inherent nature of evil as evil make the creation wise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that God's creation of evil is wise because it fulfills His knowledge and justice. When you face evil or suffering in your life, do you truly believe that God has a wise purpose, or do you question His wisdom? What would change in your daily trust if you accepted that even your own sins are created by God as evil, yet He is wise?
?
Nasafi says the disbeliever is foolish because he intends evil as good. Examine your own heart: are there sins you try to justify or rationalize as 'not that bad'? How does this lesson expose your need to see your actions as God sees them—truly evil—and repent?
?
If God's wisdom in creating evil is tied to His justice in punishing, how does this affect your view of divine justice? Do you fear God's punishment, or do you take His mercy for granted? Commit to one concrete change in how you seek forgiveness today.

intermediate
5 min
Maturidi View on Takwin and the Irrelevance of Aspects
Nasafi argues why Maturidis do not need the theory of aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi distinction between takwin and mukawwan eliminates the need for the theory of aspects (jihaat) in evaluating divine acts.

Core Idea
The Maturidi distinction between making and the thing made removes the need for aspects.

This passage presents a pivotal Maturidi argument: because takwin (the act of bringing into existence) is distinct from the thing brought into existence (mukawwan), the ugliness of a created thing does not reflect on the act of creation. This avoids having to posit multiple aspects or perspectives for a single act, a move only necessary for those who identify takwin with the created thing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the flow from rejecting denial of ugliness to explaining the Maturidi position.
2
Understand the denial of necessity
Nasafi begins by arguing that denying the ugliness of certain things is a denial of necessity (ḍarūra), and would lead to denying the ugliness of disbelief. Recognize this as a foundational point.
This establishes that some things are necessarily known as ugly.
3
Grasp the Maturidi distinction and its consequence
Focus on the core claim: takwin is other than mukawwan. Therefore, disbelief is a created thing (maf'ūl), not God's act. Its ugliness does not entail ugliness of the act of creating, especially if that act has a praiseworthy outcome. Hence, no need for aspects.
The theory of aspects is only needed by those who equate takwin with the thing made.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا وجه لإنكارهم قبح هذه الأشياء كما لا وجه لإنكار حسن كثير من الأجسام؛ لأنه إنكار الضرورة ولو جاز له هذا جاز لغيره إنكار قبح الكفر، وذلك باطل. واعلموا - رحمكم الله - أن أصحابنا - رحمهم الله – لما كان من مذهبهم أن التكوين غير المكون والكفر مكون وتكوينه غيره فلم يكن هو عندنا فعل الله تعالى بل هو مفعوله وكون المفعول قبيحًا لا يوجب قبح التكوين إذا كانت فيه عاقبة حميدة، فلم يكن بنا على هذا المذهب حاجة إلى القول بجهات الفعل وأنه بجهة أنه فعل الله تعالى ليس بقبيح وبجهة أنه فعل العبد قبيح، وإنما الحاجة إلى ذلك لمن يزعم أن التكوين هو عين المكون.
And there is no justification for their denial of the ugliness of these things, just as there is no justification for the denial of the beauty of many bodies, because it is a denial of necessity. If this were permissible for him, it would be permissible for another to deny the ugliness of disbelief, and that is false. And know – may God have mercy on you – that our companions – may God have mercy on them – since their doctrine is that takwin (bringing into existence) is other than the thing brought into existence (mukawwan), and disbelief is a thing brought into existence and its bringing into existence is other than it, therefore disbelief is not, according to us, the act of God Most High, but rather His object. And the fact that the object is ugly does not necessitate the ugliness of the bringing into existence when it has a praiseworthy outcome. So we, according to this doctrine, have no need to speak of the aspects (jihaat) of the act, that it is by one aspect not ugly because it is the act of God Most High and by another aspect ugly because it is the act of the servant. Rather, the need for that is for one who claims that the bringing into existence is identical to the thing brought into existence.
Source pages p. 934

Commentary
This passage first rejects the denial that certain things are ugly, calling it a denial of necessity (ḍarūra). If one denies the ugliness of beetles, etc., another could deny the ugliness of disbelief, which is false. Then the author addresses the reader directly ('And know...') to explain the Maturidi position on why they do not require the theory of 'aspects' (jihaat) of an act. The core Maturidi doctrine is that takwin (the act of bringing into existence) is distinct from mukawwan (the thing brought into existence). Disbelief (kufr) is a mukawwan, not the act of God; it is His object (maf'ūl). The ugliness of the object does not entail the ugliness of the act of bringing it into existence, especially if that act has a praiseworthy outcome. Therefore, Maturidis do not need to posit that an act has different aspects such that it is good from God's perspective and bad from the servant's. This theory is only needed by those who hold that takwin is identical to the thing brought into existence (i.e., that God's act is the same as the created thing).

Key Terms
تَكْوِين
مُكَوَّن
مَفْعُول
جِهَة
ضَرُورَة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The ugliness of a created thing implies that the act of creating it is also ugly.
Correction: Maturidis hold that the act of creating (takwin) is distinct from the created thing (mukawwan). The ugliness of the object does not necessitate the ugliness of the act, especially when the act has a praiseworthy outcome.

Checkpoint
Why do Maturidis not need the theory of aspects (jihaat) for actions?
A) Because they deny that actions have any ugliness.
B) Because they hold that takwin is the same as the thing made.
C) Because they distinguish between the act of creating and the created thing.
D) Because they believe God's act is always good regardless.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi distinction between takwin and mukawwan means that the ugliness of a created thing does not affect the act of creating, thereby removing the need for a theory of aspects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every evil in the world—including your own sins—is a created object from God, yet His act of creating it is pure? How does this distinction change the way you view your own wrongdoings—are you more prone to blame God or to take responsibility?
?
When you see something ugly in the world—injustice, suffering, or your own moral failures—do you instinctively question God's goodness? After learning that the ugliness of the object does not taint the act of creating, will you now train your heart to separate God's perfect action from the flawed created thing?
?
The Maturidis rejected the theory of aspects because they had a deeper distinction. Have you ever relied on a convenient theological excuse to avoid taking full ownership of your faith? What 'aspects' or rationalizations have you used to soften the hard truths about your relationship with God, and will you now discard them in light of the clarity of tawḥīd?

Refuting Mu'tazilite Views on Guidance and Misguidance
Al-Nasafi refutes al-Ka'bi and Basrian interpretations of verse 6:125.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi refutes Mu'tazilite interpretations of Quran 6:125 by establishing the correct cause-effect relationship between God's will and the spiritual states of faith and disbelief.

Core Idea
God's will directly causes spiritual states; Mu'tazilites reversed cause and effect.

In this passage, Al-Nasafi interprets a key Quranic verse (6:125) and defends the Ash'ari-Maturidi position that God's will is the direct cause of guidance or misguidance. He then refutes two Mu'tazilite misinterpretations: that of al-Ka'bi, who reversed the causal order, and that of the Basrians, who reduced guidance to mere clarification. This lesson will walk through his argument and refutations.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and explanation
Read the Arabic verse and the author's explanation of the cause-effect relationship between God's will and the state of the chest.
2
Identify al-Ka'bi's error
Notice how al-Ka'bi reinterprets the verse to mean that expansion of chest is a reward after faith, not a cause. The author calls this a distortion.
3
Understand the reversal
The author points out that al-Ka'bi swapped cause (expansion) and effect (faith). Work through the logic of why this is corrupt.
4
Refute the Basrian view
The Basrians say 'guidance' means only clarification and 'misguidance' means only naming. See why the author dismisses this as utterly invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال تعالى : { فَمَن يُرِدِ (٥) اللَّهُ أَن يَهْدِيَهُ يَشْرَحْ صَدْرَهُ لِلْإِسْلَامِ وَمَن يُرِدْ أَن يُضِلَّهُ يَجْعَلْ صَدْرَهُ ضَيِّقًا حَرَجًا } (١) فجعل شرح الصدر سببًا يحصل به الإيمان، وضيق الصدر وحرجه سببًا يحصل به الضلال وأخبر أنه متى أراد أن يهدي إنسانا يشرح صدره ليهتدي، ومتى أراد ضلاله يجعل صدره ضيقًا حرجًا لئلا يؤمن فيبقى على الكفر.
والكعبي لتحيره اعترض بما كانت المداواة أولى به لو كان ظن هذا الاعتراض صحيحًا فقال : معنى الآية أن من أسلم آتاه الله من لطائف ما لا يقدر عليه غيره ثوابًا لطاعته، ومن كفر ضيق الله صدره عقابًا لذلك، وهو تحريف للكتاب ونقل للكلم (١) عن مواضعها وليس بتأويل وذلك لأن الله تعالى أثبت له الإسلام إذا شرح صدره، والكفر إذا صير قلبه ضيقًا حرجًا ولم يوجب شرح القلب لأنه أسلم، ولا ضيق القلب لأنه لم يؤمن، فكان ما قاله جعل ما هو جار مجرى الحكم علة، وجعل ما هو جار مجرى العلة حكما وفساده لا يخفى
واعتراض البصريين أنه أراد بالهداية البيان وبالإضلال التسمية (٢) فاسد جدًا.
And He, exalted, said: {So whoever Allah wills to guide, He expands his chest for Islam; and whoever He wills to misguide, He makes his chest tight and constricted.} He made the expansion of the chest a cause by which faith occurs, and the tightness and constriction of the chest a cause by which misguidance occurs, and He informed that whenever He wills to guide a person, He expands his chest so that he may be guided, and whenever He wills his misguidance, He makes his chest tight and constricted so that he does not believe and remains upon disbelief. And al-Ka'bi, due to his confusion, objected—though treating himself with medicine would have been more befitting had his suspicion of this objection been correct—and said: 'The meaning of the verse is that whoever becomes Muslim, Allah gives him subtle favors that no one else can give as a reward for his obedience; and whoever disbelieves, Allah constricts his chest as a punishment for that.' This is a distortion of the Book and a removal of words from their places, not a valid interpretation. This is because Allah, exalted, established Islam for him when He expanded his chest, and disbelief when He made his heart tight and constricted; He did not make the expansion of the heart because he became Muslim, nor the tightness of the heart because he did not believe. So what he said makes what is in the position of the effect a cause, and what is in the position of the cause an effect. Its corruption is not hidden. And the objection of the Basrians that He intended by 'guidance' (hidaya) clarification (bayan) and by 'misguidance' (idhal) naming (tasmiya) is utterly invalid.
Source pages p. 962

Commentary
This passage interprets Quran 6:125 and refutes two Mu'tazilite interpretations. The author first quotes the verse and explains its straightforward meaning: Allah's will to guide results in the expansion of the chest for Islam, which is the cause (sabab) for faith; His will to misguide results in constriction, which is the cause for disbelief. The cause-and-effect relationship is direct: where Allah's will goes, the spiritual state follows. Then the author refutes al-Ka'bi, who claimed that the verse means God rewards believers with subtle favors after they choose faith, and punishes disbelievers after they choose disbelief. The author argues this is a distortion because the verse clearly places expansion before faith, not after; it is the means by which faith occurs. Al-Ka'bi reversed the order, making the effect (Islam) a condition for the cause (expansion), and the cause a result. Then the author refutes the Basrian view that 'guidance' means mere clarification (bayan) of the truth, and 'misguidance' means merely naming them as misguided (tasmiya). This is dismissed as utterly invalid because the verse speaks of a direct act of making the chest narrow or wide, which is a real effect, not just a label.

Key Terms
شرح الصدر
ضيق الصدر
الهداية
الإضلال
البيان
التسمية
السبب
الحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's guidance in the verse means a reward for choosing faith, or that it merely clarifies the truth without affecting the heart.
Correction: The verse shows that God's will directly causes the spiritual state—expansion of the chest is the means by which faith occurs, not the result of faith.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what error does al-Ka'bi commit in his interpretation of Quran 6:125?
A) He claims that expansion of the chest is a reward for faith.
B) He says that guidance means clarification.
C) He reverses the cause and effect in the verse.
D) He denies that God wills misguidance.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi argues that the Quranic verse clearly shows God's will as the direct cause of faith or disbelief, and any interpretation that reverses this causal order or reduces it to mere clarification is invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'Whoever Allah wills to guide, He expands his chest for Islam,' do you truly feel that your faith is a direct gift from Allah, or do you secretly believe it is your own achievement? What would change in your prayer if you genuinely believed that without His expansion of your chest, you would remain in darkness?
?
The Mu'tazilites reversed cause and effect. Are there areas in your life where you have reversed the true order, claiming credit for what Allah has done, or blaming yourself for what He has decreed? How can you realign your heart to His sovereignty?
?
If Allah constricts a person's chest as a punishment, do you feel fear that your own hardness of heart might be a sign of His turning away? What would you do today to seek His expansion of your chest?

Refuting al-Aslah in Reward for Believers
Nasafi refutes al-aslah in reward by showing its logical dead ends.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi argument refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that God must reward believers in the most beneficial way.

Core Idea
God's reward is not constrained by human notions of 'most beneficial'.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi employs a dialectical method to challenge the Mu'tazilite doctrine of al-aslah. The opponents argue that God must act for the most beneficial outcome for individuals. Nasafi questions whether the reward itself provides a surplus of assistance towards obedience, leading to contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two branches
Read the passage and note the two possible answers about the reward's surplus assistance (fadl mu'awana). The opponent must answer yes or no.
The argument proceeds by showing each answer leads to a problem.
2
Trace the consequences of 'yes'
If they say yes, then why did God not give it before entitlement? That would be more beneficial. Opponent fails to explain why God delayed.
3
Trace the consequences of 'no'
If they say no, then the reward has no benefit and is not a real blessing, so it cannot be considered a proper reward.
The argument extends to the disbeliever similarly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المثوبة للمؤمنين وبطريق العقوبة للكافرين فاسد لأنا نقول ما فعل من ذلك بطريق الثواب هل كان به فضل معونة على الخير والطاعة أم لا فإن قالوا نعم قيل ولم لم يعطه ذلك قبل استحقاقه بطريق الثواب وهو أنفع له وأصلح فقد منع الأصلح إذا قبل استجابة ذلك بفعله وإن قالوا ليس يحصل به فضل معونة قيل لا فائدة إذا به ولا منه ولم يكن هو نعمة فلا معنى لجعله ثوابا وكذا يقال هل هذا المعنى بحيث لو فعل الكافر لآمن إن قالوا لا فإذا لا فائدة فيه فلا يصلح ثوابا وإن قالوا نعم قيل فقد منع الكافر ذلك فأما ما فعل بالكافر فنقول أبقى الكفار بعد ما فعل بهم من الختم والطبع وما ذكرنا ممتحنين أم لا فإن قالوا لا فقد جعلوهم فيما يعتقدونه ويفترون به على الله تعالى ويرتكبون من أنواع المعاصي معذورين وجعلوا هذه الأفعال لهم غير جائزة المؤاخذة والقول بذلك كفر وخروج أيضا عن إجماع أهل القبلة وإن قالوا هم بعد ما فعل بهم من الختم والطبع وغير ذلك ممتحنون قلنا فإذا كانوا ممتحنين فأي الأمرين أصلح لهم في الدين وجود هذه المعاني أم ارتفاعها فإن قالوا وجودها جعلوا ما هو من الله تعالى عقوبة لهم من ختم القلوب وطبعها وجعل الغشاوة على أبصارهم أصلح لهم في الدين من تركها وهذا جهل عظيم وإن قالوا عدمها فقد أقروا أنه تعالى يفعل بالممتحنين ما ليس بأصلح لهم في الدين وقد هدموا جميع قواعدهم ثم يقال وأي ضرر عليهم في الختم والطبع ولم يتألموا بهما في الدنيا بل انتقموا بهما حيث كانا أصلح لهم في أمر دينهم حتى ليعاقبهم الله بذلك على ارتكابهم معصية وكفرهم بآياته ولا ضرر عليهم في الآخرة بهذا الختم الموجود في الدنيا إذ صار أصلح في الدين وما هو أصلح في الدين سبب نفع الآخرة ولا جواب لهم عنه بأفصح من السكوت والله الموفق
Reward for believers and by way of punishment for disbelievers is false, for we say: What He did by way of reward, was there in it a surplus of assistance towards good and obedience or not? If they say: Yes. It is said: Then why did He not give it to him before his entitlement by way of reward, while it is more beneficial and more suitable for him? So he prevented the most suitable, since he accepted [the response] to that by his action. And if they say: There does not occur by it a surplus of assistance. It is said: Then there is no benefit in it at all, nor from it, and it is not a blessing, so there is no meaning in making it a reward. And similarly it is said: Is this meaning such that if the disbeliever did it he would believe? If they say: No. Then there is no benefit in it, so it is not suitable as a reward. And if they say: Yes. It is said: Then he prevented the disbeliever from that. As for what He did with the disbeliever, we say: Do the disbelievers remain, after what was done to them of sealing and stamping and what we mentioned, tested or not? If they say: No. Then they have made them, in what they believe and fabricate against God Almighty and commit from types of sins, excused, and they have made these acts for them not subject to accountability, and saying that is disbelief and also departure from the consensus of the people of the qibla. And if they say: They are, after what was done to them of sealing and stamping and other than that, tested. We say: If they are tested, then which of the two matters is more suitable for them in religion: the existence of these meanings or their removal? If they say: Their existence. They have made what is from God Almighty as a punishment for them — sealing of hearts and stamping them and placing a covering over their eyes — more suitable for them in religion than leaving them, and this is great ignorance. And if they say: Their absence. Then they have affirmed that He Almighty does with the tested what is not more suitable for them in religion, and they have demolished all their foundations. Then it is said: And what harm is there for them in sealing and stamping, since they did not suffer pain from them in this world, but rather they took revenge through them, while they were more suitable for them in their religious affair, so that God would punish them by that for their commission of sin and their disbelief in His signs, and there is no harm for them in the Hereafter by this sealing existing in this world, since it became more suitable in religion, and what is more suitable in religion is a cause of benefit in the Hereafter. And they have no answer to it more eloquent than silence, and God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 1023

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a doctrine held by a group (likely the Mu'tazila) regarding divine reward and punishment based on the principle of al-aslah (the most beneficial). The author uses a dialectical method, posing questions to show contradictions in the opponents' view. He first addresses the issue of thawab (reward) for believers: if the act of rewarding provides a 'surplus of assistance' (fadl mu'awana) towards good deeds, then why did God not give it before the believer earned it, since it would be more beneficial? If it does not assist, then it is useless and not a genuine reward. Similarly, for the disbeliever, if the act causing disbelief (like sealing the heart) would lead to faith if absent, then by giving it God prevented faith. Next, he considers the state of disbelievers after God seals their hearts. If they are no longer tested (mumtahinun), then their sins would be excused, which is disbelief. If they are still tested, then the opponents must say whether the sealing is more beneficial for their religion or its absence. If they say the sealing is more beneficial, they absurdly claim that what is clearly a punishment is actually beneficial. If they say its absence is more beneficial, then God does something not most beneficial, contradicting their principle. Finally, he argues that sealing causes no harm in this world or the next because it is a means to punishment in the Hereafter, so it is not harmful. The opponents have no answer but silence.

Key Terms
ثواب
فضل معونة
أصلح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God must always give the most beneficial reward to believers.
Correction: God's reward is a grace, not obligated to be the most beneficial by human standards; the argument shows contradictions if one insists on al-aslah.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what happens if the opponents say the reward provides no surplus assistance?
A) The reward is more beneficial.
B) The reward is useless and not a true reward.
C) The reward should have been given earlier.
D) The reward causes disbelief.

Key Takeaway
God's reward is a gracious act, not a required best outcome; the al-aslah doctrine fails logically.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you sometimes feel that God owes you a reward because of your good deeds? How does this passage challenge that entitlement, and what would it mean for you to accept reward purely as grace?
?
Think of a time you prayed for something you thought was best for you, but it didn't happen. How does Nasafi's argument about God withholding what seems 'most beneficial' reshape your understanding of His wisdom? Are you ready to trust that His withholding might be more beneficial?
?
If you truly believed that God's reward is not obligated to be the best by your standards, how would that change your perception of trials you face or blessings you lack? Would you still obey Him even if you saw no immediate benefit?

Refuting al-Aslah in Punishment and Sealing
Nasafi refutes al-aslah regarding divine punishment through a dilemma on sealing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that God must act most beneficially even in punishment, using the example of sealing the hearts of disbelievers.

Core Idea
Sealing hearts is a divine punishment, not a failure to do what is best.

The second part of the argument addresses the case of disbelievers whose hearts are sealed. Nasafi questions whether they remain tested after being sealed, leading to a dilemma that undermines the al-aslah principle entirely.

Guided Path
1
Consider the state of disbelievers
Read the passage and note the initial question: after sealing, are the disbelievers still tested (mumtahanun)?
2
If not tested
If they are no longer tested, then their sins are excused, which is disbelief and contradicts consensus.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
If tested
Then ask: is the sealing more beneficial for their religion or not? Either answer causes problems for al-aslah.
4
The final twist
Nasafi argues that sealing causes no harm in this world or the Hereafter, so the objection is moot.
The opponents are left silent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المثوبة للمؤمنين وبطريق العقوبة للكافرين فاسد لأنا نقول ما فعل من ذلك بطريق الثواب هل كان به فضل معونة على الخير والطاعة أم لا فإن قالوا نعم قيل ولم لم يعطه ذلك قبل استحقاقه بطريق الثواب وهو أنفع له وأصلح فقد منع الأصلح إذا قبل استجابة ذلك بفعله وإن قالوا ليس يحصل به فضل معونة قيل لا فائدة إذا به ولا منه ولم يكن هو نعمة فلا معنى لجعله ثوابا وكذا يقال هل هذا المعنى بحيث لو فعل الكافر لآمن إن قالوا لا فإذا لا فائدة فيه فلا يصلح ثوابا وإن قالوا نعم قيل فقد منع الكافر ذلك فأما ما فعل بالكافر فنقول أبقى الكفار بعد ما فعل بهم من الختم والطبع وما ذكرنا ممتحنين أم لا فإن قالوا لا فقد جعلوهم فيما يعتقدونه ويفترون به على الله تعالى ويرتكبون من أنواع المعاصي معذورين وجعلوا هذه الأفعال لهم غير جائزة المؤاخذة والقول بذلك كفر وخروج أيضا عن إجماع أهل القبلة وإن قالوا هم بعد ما فعل بهم من الختم والطبع وغير ذلك ممتحنون قلنا فإذا كانوا ممتحنين فأي الأمرين أصلح لهم في الدين وجود هذه المعاني أم ارتفاعها فإن قالوا وجودها جعلوا ما هو من الله تعالى عقوبة لهم من ختم القلوب وطبعها وجعل الغشاوة على أبصارهم أصلح لهم في الدين من تركها وهذا جهل عظيم وإن قالوا عدمها فقد أقروا أنه تعالى يفعل بالممتحنين ما ليس بأصلح لهم في الدين وقد هدموا جميع قواعدهم ثم يقال وأي ضرر عليهم في الختم والطبع ولم يتألموا بهما في الدنيا بل انتقموا بهما حيث كانا أصلح لهم في أمر دينهم حتى ليعاقبهم الله بذلك على ارتكابهم معصية وكفرهم بآياته ولا ضرر عليهم في الآخرة بهذا الختم الموجود في الدنيا إذ صار أصلح في الدين وما هو أصلح في الدين سبب نفع الآخرة ولا جواب لهم عنه بأفصح من السكوت والله الموفق
Reward for believers and by way of punishment for disbelievers is false, for we say: What He did by way of reward, was there in it a surplus of assistance towards good and obedience or not? If they say: Yes. It is said: Then why did He not give it to him before his entitlement by way of reward, while it is more beneficial and more suitable for him? So he prevented the most suitable, since he accepted [the response] to that by his action. And if they say: There does not occur by it a surplus of assistance. It is said: Then there is no benefit in it at all, nor from it, and it is not a blessing, so there is no meaning in making it a reward. And similarly it is said: Is this meaning such that if the disbeliever did it he would believe? If they say: No. Then there is no benefit in it, so it is not suitable as a reward. And if they say: Yes. It is said: Then he prevented the disbeliever from that. As for what He did with the disbeliever, we say: Do the disbelievers remain, after what was done to them of sealing and stamping and what we mentioned, tested or not? If they say: No. Then they have made them, in what they believe and fabricate against God Almighty and commit from types of sins, excused, and they have made these acts for them not subject to accountability, and saying that is disbelief and also departure from the consensus of the people of the qibla. And if they say: They are, after what was done to them of sealing and stamping and other than that, tested. We say: If they are tested, then which of the two matters is more suitable for them in religion: the existence of these meanings or their removal? If they say: Their existence. They have made what is from God Almighty as a punishment for them — sealing of hearts and stamping them and placing a covering over their eyes — more suitable for them in religion than leaving them, and this is great ignorance. And if they say: Their absence. Then they have affirmed that He Almighty does with the tested what is not more suitable for them in religion, and they have demolished all their foundations. Then it is said: And what harm is there for them in sealing and stamping, since they did not suffer pain from them in this world, but rather they took revenge through them, while they were more suitable for them in their religious affair, so that God would punish them by that for their commission of sin and their disbelief in His signs, and there is no harm for them in the Hereafter by this sealing existing in this world, since it became more suitable in religion, and what is more suitable in religion is a cause of benefit in the Hereafter. And they have no answer to it more eloquent than silence, and God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 1023

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a doctrine held by a group (likely the Mu'tazila) regarding divine reward and punishment based on the principle of al-aslah (the most beneficial). The author uses a dialectical method, posing questions to show contradictions in the opponents' view. He first addresses the issue of thawab (reward) for believers: if the act of rewarding provides a 'surplus of assistance' (fadl mu'awana) towards good deeds, then why did God not give it before the believer earned it, since it would be more beneficial? If it does not assist, then it is useless and not a genuine reward. Similarly, for the disbeliever, if the act causing disbelief (like sealing the heart) would lead to faith if absent, then by giving it God prevented faith. Next, he considers the state of disbelievers after God seals their hearts. If they are no longer tested (mumtahinun), then their sins would be excused, which is disbelief. If they are still tested, then the opponents must say whether the sealing is more beneficial for their religion or its absence. If they say the sealing is more beneficial, they absurdly claim that what is clearly a punishment is actually beneficial. If they say its absence is more beneficial, then God does something not most beneficial, contradicting their principle. Finally, he argues that sealing causes no harm in this world or the next because it is a means to punishment in the Hereafter, so it is not harmful. The opponents have no answer but silence.

Key Terms
ختم
طبع
ممتحن
أصلح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's punishment (like sealing hearts) is unjust or not done for the best.
Correction: Sealing is a just punishment that does not harm the disbeliever in this life or the next; it is a means to divine justice.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the opponents say the disbelievers are not tested after sealing?
A) The disbelievers are still accountable.
B) The disbelievers are excused for their sins, which is kufr.
C) The sealing is more beneficial.
D) The disbelievers will be punished anyway.

Key Takeaway
Divine punishment is just and not subject to human standards of optimal benefit; the al-aslah doctrine collapses under the dilemma of sealing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage shows that God’s punishment can be sealing a person’s heart from guidance. Have you ever blamed God for someone’s disbelief, thinking He should have guided them? How does this dilemma force you to reconsider that assumption? Will you now surrender to His justice even when you cannot understand it?
?
The opponents are silenced because their logic leads to absurdity. When you encounter a test of faith (like a trial in your life), do you demand that God explain why it is best for you? Or will you accept that punishment and hardship can be just without being ‘beneficial’ in your eyes? What will you do the next time you face such a trial?
?
The sealing is described as causing no pain in this world but still leading to just punishment in the afterlife. Are there sins in your life that you have become numb to—sins that no longer bother you? Could that numbness itself be a form of sealing? If so, what accountability do you face, and how will you seek to break that seal before it is too late?

Paradise Not Diminished by Merit
Imam Nasafi argues that paradise cannot be diminished by merit via an infinite regress argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why human actions cannot independently earn reward in paradise and why all reward is by divine favor alone.

Core Idea
All human obedience is gratitude for prior blessings; gratitude itself is a gift.

Imam Nasafi presents a powerful argument against the view that human actions merit reward. He shows that every act of worship is actually a response to a prior blessing from Allah. This leads to an infinite regress, demonstrating that any reward in paradise is purely by Allah's grace, not by right. This passage is a classic Maturidi refutation of the Mu'tazilite concept of obligation (wujub 'ala Allah).

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite claim
The Mu'tazilites held that human actions can earn reward from Allah by right. Recognize this as the backdrop of the argument.
This claim is what Imam Nasafi refutes.
2
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Nasafi shows that if reward were based on merit, paradise would be sullied because all good deeds are gratitude for prior blessings.
The term 'sullied' (منغصة) indicates a decrease in perfection.
3
Grasp the infinite regress of gratitude
Every act of gratitude requires tawfiq (divine success) from Allah, and that tawfiq itself is a new blessing requiring further gratitude, ad infinitum.
Thus, no one can fully repay even a single blessing.
4
See the Quranic proof
The passage ends with the verse 'And if you count the blessing of Allah, you cannot enumerate them' (Ibrahim 34), confirming the impossibility of counting blessings.
This supports the argument that reward is by favor, not merit.
5
Conclude: reward is pure grace
Since no one can earn paradise by works, any reward is a gift from Allah's bounty and mercy.
This preserves the perfection of paradise and the sovereignty of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لو كان الأمر على ما زعم لكانت الجنة العليا وما فيها من النعم منغصة على أولياء الله وأهل كرامته، لأن نيلهم ذلك كله كان بفضل من الله ونعمة منه، إذ لا أحد يستوجب بشيء من عباداته وطاعاته على الله تعالى شيئًا وإن زجي عمره في طاعته ولم يعصه طرفة عين، وذلك لأن العبد ما يأتيه من الطاعة يأتيه شكرًا لما أنعم عليه، ومن أدى إلى غيره حقا مستحقاً لا يستوجب بإزاء ما أدى شيئًا من العوض، على أن العبد لا يمكنه الخروج في جميع عمره وإن طال عن شكر نعمة واحدة وإن قلت لما أنه لا يؤدي شكره إلا بتوفيق من ربه وما وصل إليه من أثر التوفيق نعمة مستأنفة يقتضى عليها شكرًا مستأنفا ثم لا يؤدي شكر هذا التوفيق إلا بتوفيق هكذا إلى ما لا يتناهى، وإذا كان لا يمكنه الخروج عن شكر نعمة واحدة فكيف عن شكر ما عليه من النعم الوافية الوافرة والمنن المتوالية المتظاهرة التي لا يمكنه إحصاؤها وعدها ويتعذر عليه حصرها وحدها على ما نطق به الكتاب بقوله تعالى : { وَإِن تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَةَ اللهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا }.
Then if the matter were as they claim, then the highest paradise and whatever blessings it contains would be sullied for the friends of Allah and the people of His generosity, because their attainment of all that was by Allah's bounty and grace from Him, since no one deserves anything from Allah Most High by any of his acts of worship and obedience, even if he spends his life in obedience and does not disobey Him for the blink of an eye. That is because the servant's obedience that he performs he performs as gratitude for what He has bestowed upon him. And one who delivers to another a due right does not deserve in return for what he delivered any compensation. Moreover, the servant cannot in his entire life, however long, escape from gratitude for a single blessing, however small, because he does not perform its gratitude except by success (tawfiq) from his Lord, and what reached him of the effect of success is a new blessing requiring new gratitude, and then he does not perform gratitude for this success except by success, and so on ad infinitum. And if he cannot escape from gratitude for one blessing, then how can he escape from gratitude for the abundant and ample blessings and successive and manifest favors that he cannot enumerate or count, and it is impossible for him to limit and bound them, as the Book has spoken with His saying: "And if you count the blessing of Allah, you cannot enumerate them."
Source pages p. 1029

Commentary
This passage is a reductio ad absurdum against the Mu'tazilite view that human actions earn reward. The author argues that if rewards were based on merit, then paradise would be diminished because all good deeds are actually gratitude for prior blessings. Since gratitude itself requires further divine assistance (tawfiq) which is another blessing, an infinite regress shows that no one can fully repay the first blessing. Thus, any reward is purely by divine favor, not by right. The passage ends with the Quranic verse emphasizing the impossibility of counting Allah's blessings.

Key Terms
الجنة العليا
منغصة
شكر
توفيق
نعمة
عوض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human actions independently merit reward from Allah.
Correction: All actions are performed as gratitude for prior blessings, and gratitude itself requires divine grace, so no action can earn reward by right.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can a servant never fully repay even one of Allah's blessings?
A) Because blessings are infinite.
B) Because gratitude for one blessing requires another tawfiq which is another blessing.
C) Because servants are ungrateful by nature.
D) Because rewards are only for prophets.

Key Takeaway
Paradise is not earned by works; it is a gift of divine grace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you identify even one act of worship in your life that was not preceded by a blessing from Allah? If not, what claim to merit can you possibly have? Let this strip you of all self-righteousness before your next prayer.
?
Think of a single blessing you received today. Now trace the gratitude you offered for it. Did that gratitude come from your own power, or did Allah enable you to say 'Alhamdulillah'? How does this change your view of your own spiritual accomplishments?
?
If every good deed you have ever done is a response to a gift, and the response itself is another gift, then what remains for you to boast about? How should this realization reshape the way you approach your Salah tonight?

Mu'tazilite Proof for Eternal Punishment
Mu'tazilites cite Qur'anic verses to prove grave sinners are eternally punished.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila use Qur'anic verses to argue that grave sinners will be eternally punished, and how they defend their position against objections of false threats or specification.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila ground eternal punishment in the irrevocable threat (waʿīd) of the Qur'an.

The Mu'tazilites were known for their emphasis on divine justice and the reality of threats and promises. In this passage, they marshal several Qur'anic verses to prove that the grave sinner will be eternally punished in Hell. They also address two possible objections: that the threat might be false, or that the general commands might be specified. Understanding their reasoning is key to grasping their theological system.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qur'anic citations
Start by reading the three verses the Mu'tazila cite (Q. 4:93, 4:10, 32:18-20). Notice how each verse threatens eternal punishment or contrasts believers and sinners.
These verses are the foundation of their proof.
2
Analyze the classification
The Mu'tazila note that the verses classify people into believers and sinners (fasiq), implying that the grave sinner is not a believer and thus deserves eternal punishment.
This is a key step in their argument.
3
Understand the objections and responses
The passage then presents two objections: (1) the threat could be false (khalaf al-waʿīd), and (2) the general reports could be specified (takhṣīṣ). The Mu'tazila reject both because they would imply lying (kidhb) or abrogation (naskh), which are impossible for God.
These refutations are central to Mu'tazilite theology.
4
Note the internal disagreement on pardon
Within the Mu'tazila, there is a split: some permit God's pardon in wisdom, but still affirm the threat; others deny even the possibility of pardon, arguing it would contradict wisdom.
This shows internal diversity.
5
Consider the final note on minor sins
The passage ends by noting that minor sins are forgiven when major sins are avoided, citing Q. 4:31. This is consistent with their overall position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حكم الخلود فلقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مؤْمِنًا مُتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَلِدًا فِيهَا ) الآية، وقوله: ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَأْكُلُونَ أمْوَالَ الْيَتَامَى ظُلْمًا ﴾ الآية، وقال تعالى: أَفَمَن كَانَ مُؤْمِنًا كَمَن كَانَ فَاسِقًا فالله تعالى جعل الفسق بمقابلة الإيمان وجعل المؤمن قسمًا والفاسق قسما، دل أن الفاسق غير والمؤمن غير، ثم بين حكم كل واحد منهما فقال : أَمَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّلِحَتِ فَلَهُمْ جَنَّتُ الْمَأْوَى نُزُلاً )) بما كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ وَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ فَسَقُوا فَمَا وَنهُمُ النَّارُ كُلَّمَا أَرَادُوا أَن يَخْرُجُوا مِنْهَا أَعِيدُوا فِيهَا وَقِيلَ لَهُمْ ذُوقُوا عَذَابَ النَّارِ الَّذِي كُنتُم بِهِ، تُكَذِبُونَ فكان في الآية دليل انتفاء اسم الإيمان وثبوت اسم الفسق ودليل حكم التخليد، ثم إنهم يقولون: إن الإخبار بتعذيب القاتل للمؤمن عمدًا وغير ذلك قد ورد، ولا وجه للقول بالخلف الوعيد لما فيه من إثبات الكذب ولا وجه إلى القول بتخصيص عموم الأخبار لوجوب القول بالعموم المتعرى عن دليل الخصوص إذ الصيغة المتعرية عن دليل الخصوص دليل إرادة المتكلم العموم، فصار كأنه ذكر كل فرد من أفراد العموم باسمه الخاص، وما هذا سبيله لا يتصور تخصيصه بل يكون إخراجه على حكم العموم نسخا، ولا وجه إلى القول بنسخ الأخبار لما فيه من إثبات الكذب، وجماعة منهم يجوزون العفو عن صاحب الكبيرة في الحكمة إلا أنهم يقولون: بتحقيق الوعيد للأخبار الواردة في الكتاب بتعذيبه وجماعة منهم يقولون ليس في الحكمة جواز عفوه إذ لو كان يجوز عفوه لما جاز تعذيبه إذ العفو حينئذ يكون كرما، والإعراض عن الكرم غير جائز في الحكمة، وهذا منهم قريب من تعليل إيجاب الصلح بل هو عينه، وأما الصغائر فإنها مغفورة عند اجتناب الكبائر لقوله تعالى: إن تَجتَنِبُوا كَبَابِرَ مَا تُنْهَوْنَ عَنْهُ نُكَفِّرْ عَنكُمْ سَيِّئَاتِكُمْ الآية
As for the ruling of eternity (khulūd), due to His saying - exalted be He: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein forever' (Q. 4:93) and His saying: 'Indeed, those who consume the property of orphans unjustly...' (Q. 4:10). And He said - exalted be He: 'Is one who is a believer like one who is a sinner? They are not equal.' (Q. 32:18). So Allah - exalted be He - made sin (fisq) opposite to faith (īmān) and made the believer a category and the sinner a category, showing that the fasiq is other than the mu'min. Then He explained the ruling of each: 'As for those who believed and did righteous deeds, for them are the Gardens of Refuge, a hospitality for what they used to do. But as for those who sinned, their refuge is the Fire. Every time they wish to emerge from it, they are returned to it, and it is said to them: "Taste the punishment of the Fire which you used to deny."' (Q. 32:19-20). So in the verse there is evidence of the negation of the name īmān and the establishment of the name fisq, and evidence of the ruling of eternity. Then they say: The reports (akhbār) have come regarding the punishment of the intentional killer of a believer and other than that. There is no basis for claiming that the threat (waʿīd) is false (khalaf), because that would involve affirming lying (kidhb). Nor is there basis for specifying the generality of the reports (takhṣīṣ al-ʿumūm), because it is necessary to adhere to the general expression that is free from evidence of specification (qarīna al-khuṣūṣ). Since the general form without evidence of specification indicates the speaker's intent for generality, it becomes as if he mentioned every individual of the general class by its specific name. What is of this nature cannot be specified; rather, removing it from the ruling of generality would be abrogation (naskh). And there is no basis for claiming abrogation of the reports, because that would involve affirming lying. And a group among them permit pardon (ʿafw) for the grave sinner in terms of wisdom (ḥikma), but they say: the threat (al-waʿīd) is realized due to the reports in the Book (Qur'an) that punishes him. And a group among them says: It is not in wisdom to permit His pardon, because if His pardon were permissible, His punishment would not be permissible, since pardon then would be generosity (karam), and turning away from generosity is not permissible in wisdom. This from them is close to justifying the obligation of reconciliation (ṣulḥ), rather it is the same. As for minor sins, they are forgiven when avoiding the major sins, due to His saying - exalted be He: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden, We will remove from you your lesser sins' (Q. 4:31).
Source pages p. 1046

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite proof for the eternal punishment (khulūd) of the grave sinner. They cite three Qur'anic verses: (1) Q. 4:93, which threatens the intentional murderer of a believer with eternal Hell; (2) Q. 4:10, about consuming orphans' property; (3) Q. 32:18-20, which contrasts believers and sinners and assigns each their permanent abode. The Mu'tazila interpret these verses to show that grave sinners are not believers and will be punished eternally. They then argue against two possible objections: (a) that the threat might be false (khalaf al-waʿīd), which they reject because it would imply God lies; (b) that the general reports might be specified (takhṣīṣ), which they reject because the general form without evidence of specification must be taken as universal, and to exclude is abrogation (naskh), which would also imply God lies. Finally, they present two internal Mu'tazilite positions on pardon: one group allows God's pardon in wisdom but insists the threat is real; another denies even the possibility of pardon because it would contradict wisdom. The passage ends with the note that minor sins are forgiven when major sins are avoided, citing Q. 4:31.

Key Terms
الخلود
الوعيد
الكذب
التخصيص
النسخ
العفو
الحكمة
الصغائر
الكبائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Mu'tazila believe God must punish the grave sinner (i.e., they deny divine mercy).
Correction: The Mu'tazila ground the necessity of punishment in God's truthfulness (waʿīd must be fulfilled), not in a lack of mercy. Some even allow for pardon, though they affirm the threat is real.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila in this passage, what is the consequence of claiming that the threat (waʿīd) is false (khalaf)?
A) It is permissible
B) It implies affirming lying about God
C) It is an act of mercy
D) It is abrogation

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila affirm eternal punishment for grave sinners based on the Qur'an's universal threats, rejecting any possibility of falsehood or specification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila insist that God cannot go back on His word: every threat in the Qur'an must be executed without exception. Do you live as though every single forbidden act carries a guaranteed eternal consequence? If not, what does that say about your trust in God's truthfulness?
?
Some Mu'tazila argue that if God forgave a grave sinner after threatening punishment, He would be turning away from generosity (karam). When you sin, do you silently hope God will be 'generous' and ignore His own threats? What would it cost you to fully reckon with His seriousness?
?
This passage shows that even within a school that affirms strict punishment, there is disagreement over whether God could pardon. Are you more comfortable with a God who must punish or a God who might pardon? Which view makes you take your sins more seriously today?
